# 神经多样性

**作者**: Sue Fletcher-Watson

---

Chapter 1 Introducing neurodiversity

Chapter 1 Introducing neurodiversity

第一章 神经多样性导论

A brief history of the movement

运动简史

To understand the neurodiversity movement it will help to begin with its history. For this we need to turn back to the early 1990s, when autistic people first began gaining recognition for their self-advocacy work. At this time autism was generally seen as a terrible individual tragedy, and most researchers hoped to develop a ‘treatment’ or ‘cure’ for autism. Autism itself was mainly defined as a cognitive deficit in social understanding with biological underpinnings. The thought was that new biomedical, psychological, or behavioural intervention might help eliminate this deficit. Most autism advocacy was dominated by the parents of autistic children as well as concerned doctors. They mainly adopted this dominant way of thinking about autism and thus argued for greater funding for medical intervention and support.

要理解神经多样性运动，最好从其历史背景入手。这需要回溯到 20 世纪 90 年代初，当时孤独谱系群体首次因其自我倡导工作而获得认可。在那个时期，孤独谱系普遍被视为一种可怕的个人悲剧，大多数研究者都希望能开发出针对孤独谱系的"疗法"或"治愈方案"。孤独谱系本身主要被定义为一种具有生物学基础的社会理解认知缺陷。当时的观点认为，新的生物医学、心理学或行为干预可能有助于消除这种缺陷。大多数孤独谱系倡导活动由孤独谱系儿童的父母以及相关医生主导，他们主要采纳了这种主流的孤独谱系认知方式，因此主张为医疗干预和支持提供更多资金。

This began to be challenged when autistic people were first able to connect with each other online. This happened as the internet and personal computers became more widely available in the early 1990s. Autism Network International, a pioneering effort run by and for autistic people, was formed in 1992. In turn, some tech-savvy autistics began making email lists and then chat rooms for autistic people to discuss autism. The first was Autism Network International’s list from 1994. As more autistic people gained access to the internet, and more were being diagnosed due to the broadening of the autism concept, many of them realized they found online communication much easier than in-person communication. Many also found that communicating with other autistics came more naturally to them than communicating with non-autistics.

当孤独谱系群体首次能够在网络上相互联系时，这一观念开始受到挑战。这发生在 20 世纪 90 年代初，随着互联网和个人电脑的日益普及。1992 年，一个由孤独谱系人士运营、为其服务的开创性组织——国际孤独谱系网络成立。随后，一些精通技术的孤独谱系人士开始创建电子邮件列表，进而开设聊天室，供孤独谱系群体讨论孤独谱系相关议题。最早的是国际孤独谱系网络于 1994 年建立的邮件列表。随着越来越多的孤独谱系人士能够接触互联网，以及由于孤独谱系概念的拓宽导致更多人被诊断，他们中的许多人意识到，线上交流比面对面交流要容易得多。许多人还发现，与其他孤独谱系人士交流比与非孤独谱系人士交流更为自然。

Based on these experiences, early autistic self-advocates in an autistic-led email list called Independent Living (which was abbreviated to InLv)—a term taken from the earlier disability rights movement, emphasizing the importance of freeing disabled people from institutions—began arguing that many of the problems autistic people face were more about societal expectations and barriers rather than being intrinsic to autism. They also began suggesting that autistic people might have characteristic yet overlooked cognitive strengths, such as logical thinking or attention to detail. This sought to provide a more balanced view of autism that would reduce stigma and increase opportunity for autistic people. In the same years, the term ‘neurotypical’ began to be used—for instance on the satirical website by Laura Tisoncik, The Institute for the Neurologically Typical, which was a spoof of a medical institute that playfully reversed the medical gaze back on to those considered ‘normal’. But the term also had a less humorous role, as online advocates were also talking about ‘neurotypical’ as just one of many equally legitimate ways of being, challenging the widespread assumption that it was the only correct way for a brain to be wired.

基于这些经历，早期孤独谱系自我倡导者在一个名为"独立生活"（缩写为 InLv）的孤独谱系主导的电子邮件列表中——这一术语源自早期的残障权利运动，强调将残障人士从机构中解放出来的重要性——开始主张，孤独谱系群体面临的许多问题更多与社会期望和障碍有关，而非孤独谱系本身固有的缺陷。他们还开始提出，孤独谱系群体可能拥有独特但被忽视的认知优势，例如逻辑思维或对细节的关注。这旨在提供一个更平衡的孤独谱系观，以减少污名化并增加孤独谱系群体的机会。在同一时期，"神经典型"一词开始被使用——例如在劳拉·蒂松西克的讽刺网站"神经典型研究所"上，该网站戏仿了一个医学机构，俏皮地将医学凝视反转回那些被认为是"正常"的人身上。 但这个术语也有不那么幽默的一面，因为网络倡导者们也在谈论"神经典型性"只是众多同样合理的存在方式之一，挑战了那种认为它是大脑唯一正确连接方式的普遍假设。

These new concepts, and the new politics surrounding them, were brought out of these groups by a journalist called Harvey Blume who wrote several articles in the late 1990s, including one in the New York Times, and then an Atlantic article that introduced the term ‘neurodiversity’ to a broader audience. Shortly after this, a then sociology student called Judy Singer used the word neurodiversity in a book chapter. This is the first known use in an academic source, though it is now considered inaccurate to credit any single person with coining the word or birthing the idea. Following these early publications, the movement grew rapidly, and its theories were continually developed by an ever-growing number of neurodivergent people. This was not just autistic people, but also those with a wide range of other diagnoses, or even with no official diagnosis at all. In time, groups such as the Autistic Self-Advocacy Network, driven by advocates such as Ari Ne’eman, began to exert significant political influence in the USA, while the UK Labour Party would eventually develop a ‘neurodiversity manifesto’ led by neurodivergent members, and in Chile a recently proposed new constitution included an explicit commitment to neurodivergent liberation. The book Neurotribes by the late Steve Silberman did a huge amount to bring neurodiversity—and the autistic experience specifically—into the mainstream. At the same time, grassroots and mutual aid organizations such as the Autistic Women and Nonbinary Network and the neurodivergent abolitionist organization Neuromancers have been doing vital community organizing. All this was able to happen because so many neurodivergent people have organized together not just to fight for rights and justice, but also to collectively develop the theories that we seek to explain—and contribute to—in this book.

这些新概念及其相关的新政治理念，由一位名叫哈维·布鲁姆的记者从这些群体中带出。他在 1990 年代末撰写了多篇文章，包括一篇发表在《纽约时报》上，随后又在《大西洋月刊》上发表文章，将"神经多样性"这一术语介绍给了更广泛的受众。此后不久，一位当时的社会学学生朱迪·辛格在一本书的章节中使用了神经多样性这个词。这是已知在学术文献中的首次使用，尽管现在认为将这个词或这个概念的创造归功于任何单一个人都是不准确的。在这些早期出版物之后，这场运动迅速发展，其理论被越来越多的神经殊异者不断完善。这不仅包括孤独谱系群体，还包括许多其他诊断的人群，甚至根本没有正式诊断的人。 随着时间的推移，由阿里·尼曼等倡导者推动的孤独谱系自我倡导网络等团体开始在美国发挥重要的政治影响力，而英国工党最终也由神经殊异成员主导制定了“神经多样性宣言”，智利最近提出的新宪法则明确承诺致力于神经殊异解放。已故的史蒂夫·西尔伯曼所著的《神经部落》一书，为将神经多样性——特别是孤独谱系体验——带入主流视野做出了巨大贡献。与此同时，诸如孤独谱系女性与非二元性别网络等草根组织和互助团体，以及神经殊异废奴主义组织“神经术士”，一直在进行至关重要的社区组织工作。 这一切之所以能够发生，是因为众多神经殊异者团结组织起来，不仅为争取权利与正义而奋斗，同时也旨在共同发展我们在这本书中试图解释并贡献的理论。

Defining neurodiversity

定义神经多样性

In this book we want to emphasize—following the work of a range of neurodiversity activists and scholars—how useful it is to see neurodiversity as bringing the possibility of a new scientific and cultural paradigm. That is, we want to emphasize that it has the potential to bring a mass shift in the fundamental way we think about, study, and respond to people across the whole neurological spectrum of humanity. Part of what we want to establish is that this could help improve our scientific understanding and professional practice alongside understandings of politics and culture. At the same time, we want to show how this has radical potential to be liberating for people with a wide range of disabilities, and ultimately helpful for everyone, including neurotypicals. This is because it will help us change how we carry out research, approach clinical practice, and think about policy and law, among other things.

在这本书中，我们希望沿袭众多神经多样性活动家和学者的研究，强调将神经多样性视为一种能够开启全新科学与文化范式的可能性，这一点具有何等重要的意义。换言之，我们希望强调，神经多样性有潜力从根本上改变我们对人类整个神经谱系中各群体的思考、研究和应对方式，从而引发一场巨大的转变。 我们希望阐明的一点是，这种视角不仅有助于提升我们的科学认知和专业实践，还能深化我们对政治与文化的理解。与此同时，我们希望展示这种视角如何具有彻底解放各类残障人士的潜力，并最终惠及所有人，包括神经典型人群。这是因为它将帮助我们改变研究方法、临床实践方式，以及对政策和法律的思考方式等诸多方面。

In this chapter we will explain this in more detail. Our framing of the neurodiversity paradigm emphasizes two core principles: affirm complexity and politicize neuronormativity. Together these principles capture the applied consequences of neurodiversity. Application of these principles will constitute a paradigm shift. As such, we will begin by saying a bit more about what the words ‘paradigm’ and ‘paradigm shift’ mean and why they are important. We then provide a brief history of the neurodiversity movement and clarify some of the key concepts of its proponents. This will put us in a good place to return to our two key principles and our definition of the neurodiversity paradigm as we understand it.

在本章中，我们将对此进行更详细的阐述。我们对神经多样性范式的阐释强调两个核心原则：肯定复杂性，以及将神经规范性政治化。这两项原则共同体现了神经多样性的实际应用后果。应用这些原则将构成一次范式转变。因此，我们首先将简要说明“范式”和“范式转变”这两个词的含义及其重要性。接着，我们将简述神经多样性运动的历史，并阐明其倡导者提出的一些关键概念。这将为我们回归到两个核心原则以及我们对神经多样性范式的定义奠定良好基础。

What is a scientific paradigm?

什么是科学范式？

A scientific paradigm, at base, is a set of assumptions, principles, practices, and commitments that groups of researchers or practitioners share to get their work done, for a given historical period. Looked at this way, every science has a dominant paradigm at any given time, which can then change as our understanding progresses. For instance, in physics we might talk of Newton’s paradigm and Einstein’s paradigm, since each of these pioneering thinkers in turn established different fundamental theories that the scientists who followed them then relied on to do their own research. Or in biology we might talk of there being different paradigms before and after Darwin’s theory of evolution became widely accepted by other biologists.

从根本上说，科学范式是一套假设、原则、实践和承诺的集合，在特定历史时期内，研究者或实践者群体共享这些内容以完成他们的工作。从这个角度看，每一门科学在特定时期都有一个主导范式，随着我们理解的进步，范式也会发生变化。例如，在物理学中，我们可能会谈论牛顿的范式和爱因斯坦的范式，因为这两位开创性的思想家依次建立了不同的基础理论，后来的科学家们依赖这些理论进行自己的研究。或者在生物学中，我们可能会谈论达尔文的进化论被其他生物学家广泛接受之前和之后存在的不同范式。

A paradigm shift occurs whenever a new theoretical framework comes along that radically changes how research and scholarship in a given field operates. Every now and again, as the dominant paradigm of a given field becomes outdated or struggles to accommodate new data, new approaches with different assumptions and theoretical bases are proposed. Ideally, one of these will become widely adopted to guide scientists working in the respective field—if not, the field might split into factions adopting different paradigms. Paradigm shifts should improve the work of scientists by better explaining recent findings and opening up new lines of enquiry.

当一个新的理论框架出现，彻底改变某一领域的研究和学术运作方式时，就会发生范式转变。随着某一领域的主导范式变得过时或难以容纳新数据，人们会不时提出具有不同假设和理论基础的新方法。理想情况下，其中一种方法会被广泛采纳，以指导该领域的科学家开展工作——否则，该领域可能会分裂成采用不同范式的派系。范式转变应能更好地解释最新发现并开辟新的研究路径，从而改进科学家的工作。

Consider another clear example of such a shift: the Copernican revolution in cosmology. Shifting from viewing the earth at the centre of the solar system to viewing the sun at the centre of the solar system changed some of the most fundamental assumptions that cosmologists were working with, allowing them to develop a vastly improved scientific understanding of the cosmos. More generally, then, when we look at the development of science in this way, we might say that all our mature sciences have paradigms, and that paradigms are temporary (albeit sometimes long-lasting) frameworks shared by the majority of those in the given field. And we can add that, in time, our current paradigms will no doubt be replaced by future ones as our scientific understanding continues to develop.

再考虑一个此类转变的鲜明例证：宇宙学领域的哥白尼革命。从将地球视为太阳系中心转变为将太阳视为太阳系中心，这一转变改变了宇宙学家所依据的一些最基本假设，使他们能够发展出对宇宙更为精深的科学理解。更广泛地说，当我们以这种方式审视科学发展时，或许可以说，我们所有成熟的科学体系都拥有范式，而这些范式是特定领域内大多数研究者所共享的（尽管有时持久存在）临时框架。我们还可以补充说，随着科学认知的持续发展，当前的范式无疑将在未来被新的范式所取代。

Of course, our sciences are not totally separate from each other, and often paradigms overlap or are shared between different fields. When it comes to scientific understandings of neurodiversity, we are concerned with a range of disciplines and fields. Important here are both the ‘psych’ sciences and fields, which includes psychiatry, psychology, psychometrics, as well as the ‘neuro’ sciences, such as neurology or neuro-psychology. In turn, we are also concerned with how these relate to biology and genetics, which are often deployed in efforts to explain variations in cognitive and emotional functioning. We are equally concerned with more applied and social science approaches relating to therapy, education, and so forth. We are concerned with all of these as, together, they are the cluster of sciences that are used to determine policy and practice when it comes to human neurodiversity—both neurotypicals and neurodivergents.

当然，我们的科学并非彼此完全割裂，范式往往在不同领域间重叠或共享。当涉及对神经多样性的科学理解时，我们关注一系列学科和领域。其中重要的既包括"心理"类科学与领域——如精神病学、心理学、心理测量学，也包括"神经"类科学——如神经学或神经心理学。相应地，我们也关注这些学科如何与生物学和遗传学产生关联，后者常被用于解释认知与情感功能的变异。我们同样关注与治疗、教育等相关的更偏应用及社会科学的研究路径。我们关注所有这些领域，因为它们共同构成了用于制定人类神经多样性——无论是神经典型者还是神经差异者——相关政策与实践的科学集群。

What about cultural paradigm shifts?

那么文化范式转变又如何呢？

We can also talk about shifts in cultural paradigms. This would refer to similarly fundamental shifts regarding how we understand aspects of human diversity, arts, cultural practices, and so on. They may also relate to social attitudes, norms, and practices. Consider the shift from seeing homosexuality as a mental illness in the 20th century to seeing being gay, lesbian, or queer as minority sexual orientations related to our own cultural practices and histories, of which we can be proud. We might say that this, alongside feminism, helped propel—although did not complete, since many queer people still face all kinds of stigma and discrimination—a mass cultural paradigm shift relating to sexual and gendered norms. This cultural shift is why, for instance in the UK, like some other countries, gay marriage is now legal, and LGBTQ pride events now happen all over the nation.

我们也可以讨论文化范式的转变。这指的是在理解人类多样性、艺术、文化实践等方面同样根本性的转变。它们也可能与社会态度、规范和实践相关。例如，从 20 世纪将同性恋视为精神疾病，转变为将同性恋、女同性恋或酷儿视为与我们自身文化实践和历史相关的少数性取向，并引以为傲。可以说，这一转变与女权主义一起，推动了——尽管尚未完成，因为许多酷儿群体仍面临各种污名和歧视——一场涉及性与性别规范的大规模文化范式转变。正是这种文化转变，使得例如在英国等一些国家，同性婚姻现已合法，LGBTQ 骄傲活动在全国各地举行。

Importantly, this progress has been made in significant part through the campaigning of a great many LGBTQ activists and organizers, who put in decades of hard work with many risks to push for mass cultural change. This includes artists, writers, and so on who have played important roles in creating the space to celebrate LGBTQ cultures. Similarly to this, along with the attempt to develop a scientific paradigm shift, neurodivergent activists, artists, writers, creators, and organizers have, over recent decades, begun the significant project of starting a paradigm shift in cultural understandings, norms, and practices relating to neurodiversity. Many neurodivergent artists now create explicitly neurodivergent arts, and it is becoming more common for neurodivergent characters to be portrayed in humane and inclusive ways in literature and film. As we will see, the attempt at developing a paradigm shift is also highly relevant for research in the arts and humanities, including disability theory, which is no less important, and perhaps more fundamental, for the neurodiversity movement than the attempt at a paradigm shift in the sciences. Neurodiversity theory can help us rethink our histories, the significance of neurodivergent art, and much else.

重要的是，这一进步在很大程度上得益于众多 LGBTQ 活动家和组织者的不懈倡导，他们冒着巨大风险，经过数十年的艰苦努力，推动了大规模的文化变革。这包括艺术家、作家等，他们在创造庆祝 LGBTQ 文化的空间方面发挥了重要作用。与此类似，伴随着试图发展科学范式的转变，近几十年来，神经殊异的活动家、艺术家、作家、创作者和组织者已经开始了一项重要工程：启动与神经多样性相关的文化理解、规范和实践的范式转变。如今，许多神经殊异艺术家创作出明确体现神经殊异的艺术作品，在文学和电影中以人性化和包容的方式描绘神经殊异角色也变得越来越普遍。正如我们将看到的，发展范式转变的尝试也与艺术和人文学科的研究高度相关，包括残疾理论，这对神经多样性运动而言，其重要性不亚于科学领域的范式转变尝试，甚至可能更为根本。 神经多样性理论可以帮助我们重新思考我们的历史、神经殊异艺术的意义以及其他许多方面。

The normalcy paradigm

常态范式

The term we use for the currently dominant paradigm for studying and responding to neurodiversity is the normalcy paradigm. Nick Walker, a leading thinker and scholar in the neurodiversity movement, called this ‘the pathology paradigm’. While we broadly follow Walker’s analysis, we use the term normalcy paradigm rather than her preferred term pathology paradigm. We call it this because the core issue is not the recognition of mental or neurological pathology as such, but rather the conflation of normalcy and health, and thus atypicality with pathology. Overcoming the normalcy paradigm is not about rejecting the very concept of mental or neurological pathology, variations of which are ancient and can be found across different cultures globally. Rather, it is about overcoming the default pathologization of people or groups who are atypical and thereby at risk of struggling. The neurodiversity paradigm recognizes and empowers all people who fall outside neuronormativity, regardless of health or disability status.

我们用来指代当前研究和应对神经多样性的主导范式的术语是常态范式。神经多样性运动的主要思想家和学者尼克·沃克称之为"病理学范式"。虽然我们大体上遵循沃克的分析，但我们使用"常态范式"这个术语，而非她偏好的"病理学范式"。我们这样称呼它，是因为核心问题并非承认精神或神经病理学本身，而是将常态与健康混为一谈，从而将非典型性与病理学等同起来。克服常态范式并非要完全否定精神或神经病理学的概念——其各种变体古已有之，在全球不同文化中都能找到。相反，它是要克服对非典型性、因而可能面临困境的个人或群体的默认病理化。神经多样性范式承认并赋权于所有偏离神经常态的人，无论其健康或残疾状况如何。

Importantly, neurodiversity proponents take the normalcy paradigm to be dominant both in culture and in scientific understandings, not least since science is, after all, a human cultural practice, aiming at objectivity while intimately intertwined with all sorts of cultural normative assumptions. Indeed, for neurodiversity proponents, it is important to try to shift both cultural and scientific paradigms simultaneously, since the assumptions of each are intertwined with and enforce those of the other.

重要的是，神经多样性的支持者认为正常性范式在文化和科学理解中都占据主导地位，尤其是因为科学毕竟是一种人类文化实践，旨在追求客观性，同时又与各种文化规范假设紧密交织。事实上，对于神经多样性的支持者来说，同时尝试转变文化和科学范式至关重要，因为两者的假设相互交织并强化彼此。

To briefly consider another parallel in historic social justice movements, we can compare what neurodiversity activists are trying to achieve with the past achievements of anti-racist movements. While the work needed to combat both interpersonal and institutional racism is barely started, shifts have been made that shape both cultural and scientific understandings. Importantly, the modern understanding of race as a social construction (which is not diminished in its impact by that understanding) has come from a combination of activism, creative artefacts (e.g. literature, theatre, fine arts), scholarship in the arts and humanities, and scientific discovery.

简要回顾历史上社会正义运动的另一个类似案例，我们可以将神经多样性活动家试图实现的目标与反种族主义运动过去的成就进行比较。尽管对抗人际和制度性种族主义所需的工作才刚刚起步，但已经发生的转变正在塑造文化和科学理解。重要的是，现代将种族视为社会建构的理解（这种理解并未削弱其影响力）源于行动主义、创造性作品（如文学、戏剧、美术）、艺术与人文领域的学术研究以及科学发现的结合。

The dominant paradigm is most centrally defined by assuming a relatively restricted normal range when it comes to mental or neurological functioning. Within this approach, it is further assumed that if someone falls outside this norm and is struggling in any way then there must be something wrong with them. That is, it is thought that some part of their brain or mind is broken and in need of fixing. We see this, for instance, in the use of the psychiatric word ‘disorder’, as in developmental language disorder (DLD) or attention deficit hyperactivity disorder (ADHD). The term indicates a problem stemming from an underlying dysfunction. Similarly, in neuroscientific research on neurodivergent people, differences in brain structure or functioning are routinely interpreted as deficits, when a value-neutral interpretation would be more reasonable, given our still minimal comprehension of how the brain actually works. Indeed, even the distinctive abilities and positive qualities of neurodivergent people can be pathologized, as in a 1991 journal article describing an ‘autism-specific deception impairment’. We also see this restricted normal range in the scientific search to find ‘cures’ or ‘treatments’ for such disabilities, at biological and psychological levels. In therapies, many likewise seek to erase ‘abnormal’ behaviours or thoughts and to promote ‘normal’ ones. What unites each of these is the assumption of a restricted normal range, and the further assumption that it is bad to fall outside the normal range. This why we say these sciences share a general normalcy paradigm.

主流范式的核心在于，它假设心理或神经功能存在一个相对受限的正常范围。在这种范式下，人们进一步认为，如果有人偏离了这个常态并在某些方面遇到困难，那一定是他们自身出了问题。也就是说，人们认为他们大脑或心智的某部分出现了故障，需要修复。例如，我们在使用“障碍”这一精神病学词汇时就能看到这一点，比如发展性语言障碍（DLD）或注意缺陷多动障碍（ADHD）。这个术语表明问题源于潜在的功能失调。同样，在对神经殊异人群的神经科学研究中，大脑结构或功能的差异通常被解释为缺陷，而考虑到我们对大脑实际运作方式的理解仍然非常有限，一种价值中立的解释可能更为合理。事实上，即使是神经殊异人群的独特能力和积极品质也可能被病理化，比如 1991 年一篇期刊文章就曾描述了一种“孤独谱系特有的欺骗能力缺陷”。 在科学领域，无论是从生物学还是心理学层面，为这些障碍寻找"治愈"或"治疗"方法的研究中，我们同样能看到这种受限的正常范围。在治疗过程中，许多方法也试图消除"异常"行为或思维，并促进"正常"行为或思维。这些做法的共同点在于，它们都假设了一个受限的正常范围，并进一步假设偏离这个正常范围是不好的。这就是为什么我们说这些科学领域共享一个普遍的正常性范式。

Relatedly, especially in modern capitalist societies we also see a broader cultural normalcy paradigm, whereby neurodivergence is often automatically seen to be a tragic deviation or something to be ashamed of in society more generally. Following a diagnosis, whether of Down syndrome or dyscalculia (aka developmental coordination disorder, or DCD), parents often feel a sense of grief on finding that their child is not ‘normal’. We also see such assumptions manifesting when children are bullied for being ‘weird’ or adults are feared for being ‘crazy’. These patterns are reinforced by representations on film which frequently use the atypical behaviour of neurodivergent characters to produce dramatic events to drive the plot forward—as in the film Rain Man, when the character of Raymond Babbitt has a meltdown in an airport, forcing his brother to drive him across the USA. Both in our sciences and in our broader culture, then, it is widely assumed that normal is good and abnormal is bad. This is what neurodiversity proponents mean when they say the normalcy paradigm is the dominant paradigm. To say that it is dominant is to say that it underlies and structures the standard ways we think about, study, represent, and respond to variations in cognitive or emotional functioning. Black neurodivergent scholars Chantelle Jessica Lewis and Jason Arday have referred to this cultural dominance as ‘neurotypical hegemony’, indicating how it closes off other ways of understanding and relating to ourselves, each other, and the world around us.

与此相关的是，特别是在现代资本主义社会中，我们还看到一种更广泛的文化常态范式，即神经殊异性往往被自动视为一种悲剧性的偏离，或是在更广泛的社会中令人羞耻的事物。在获得诊断后，无论是唐氏综合征还是计算障碍（又称发育性协调障碍，DCD），父母常常会感到一种悲伤，因为他们发现自己的孩子并不“正常”。我们也能看到这种假设在儿童因“怪异”而受欺凌，或成人因“疯狂”而遭恐惧时显现出来。这些模式在电影表现中得到强化，电影常常利用神经殊异角色的非典型行为来制造戏剧性事件，推动情节发展——就像电影《雨人》中，雷蒙德·巴比特在机场情绪崩溃，迫使他的兄弟开车带他穿越美国。因此，无论是在我们的科学中，还是在更广泛的文化中，人们普遍认为正常是好的，异常是坏的。这就是神经多样性支持者所说的常态范式是主导范式时的含义。 说它占据主导地位，意味着它构成了我们思考、研究、描述和应对认知或情感功能差异的标准方式的基础和结构。黑人神经殊异学者尚特尔·杰西卡·刘易斯和杰森·阿代将这种文化主导称为“神经典型霸权”，指出它如何封闭了其他理解并与我们自己、彼此以及周围世界建立联系的方式。

While much of the way neurodivergent and neurotypical people are understood is often just seen as established fact, it may surprise some readers to be told that the idea of the ‘normal’ person is relatively recent. Prior to the 19th century, health and illness were usually seen as a matter of balance and imbalance rather than being associated with normality and abnormality. To any doctor working in the year 1800, the idea of a ‘normal’ person or of a ‘normal’ heart rate, lung capacity, intelligence, and so forth would not make much sense. In fact, while much more abstract conceptions of the average date back to Pythagoras in ancient Greece, their use for conceptualizing concrete things only began when astronomers first developed concepts of normality to track stars in the early 19th century.

尽管神经殊异者和神经典型者被理解的方式大多被视为既定事实，但若被告知“正常人”这一概念其实相对晚近，可能会让一些读者感到惊讶。在 19 世纪之前，健康与疾病通常被视为平衡与失衡的问题，而非与正常和异常挂钩。对于任何在 1800 年行医的医生来说，“正常人”或“正常心率”、“正常肺活量”、“正常智力”等概念都难以理解。事实上，虽然更抽象的平均概念可追溯至古希腊的毕达哥拉斯，但将其用于具体事物的概念化，直到 19 世纪初天文学家首次发展出正常性概念来追踪星辰时才真正开始。

It was following this, in the 1830s, that the notion of the average began to be applied to people and populations. In 1835 the Belgian social scientist Adolphe Quetelet proposed the notion of the ‘average man’ for the first time, based on comparing measurements of soldiers and then working out their average height, weight, and so forth. This fitted with a modern capitalist and swiftly industrializing society that required humans to adjust to standardized machinery in the workplace, and which valued people in relation to their purported individual productive capacities. It changed how we thought about, studied, and responded to illness and disability in a very significant way. It was in this context that the normalcy paradigm began to be developed. Scientists such as Francis Galton drew on Quetelet to propose that human mental functioning could be ranked in relation to a ‘normal’ range. Importantly, Galton was also a white supremacist who wrote books seeking to rank the races in terms of cognitive ability. While his more overt racism is now widely rejected, his underlying framework nonetheless came to underpin much thinking in the psychological and neuro-sciences since this time, not to mention shifting broader cultural understandings that position people as subnormal (disabled), normal (abled), or supernormal (gifted) in terms of their bodily or mental functioning. From this time on, much of our science has assumed that we can rank all aspects of mental or bodily functioning in relation to a normal range, and moreover that we should try to make people more normal if they fall outside that range.

正是在此之后，19 世纪 30 年代，"平均值"这一概念开始被应用于人类和群体。1835 年，比利时社会科学家阿道夫·凯特莱首次提出"平均人"的概念，其基础是对士兵的测量数据进行比较，然后计算出他们的平均身高、体重等指标。这一概念契合了现代资本主义和快速工业化的社会需求——社会要求人们适应工作场所的标准化机械，并根据个人声称的生产能力来评价人的价值。这一转变极大地改变了我们对疾病和残疾的认知、研究及应对方式。正是在这样的背景下，"常态范式"开始形成。弗朗西斯·高尔顿等科学家借鉴凯特莱的理论，提出人类的心智功能可以参照"正常"范围进行排序。值得注意的是，高尔顿同时是一位白人至上主义者，曾著书试图按认知能力对种族进行分级。 尽管他更为露骨的种族主义如今已广受唾弃，但其根本框架却自此支撑了心理学和神经科学领域的诸多思想，更不用说它改变了更广泛的文化认知，将人们在身体或心智功能上划分为低于正常（残疾）、正常（健全）或超常（天赋）。从那时起，我们的科学在很大程度上假定，我们可以将心智或身体功能的各个方面与一个正常范围进行排序，并且，如果人们偏离了这个范围，我们应当努力使他们变得更正常。

Another scientific tradition which has shaped our concept of ‘normal’ is the history of neuropsychology, grounded in adult case studies. Before brain imaging techniques became widespread, the only insight into the functions of different brain regions came from cases where ‘normal’ brain function had been grossly disrupted, often by injury or stroke. The famous case of Phineas Gage, a railway worker who survived a massive injury to his frontal lobes at work, provided much of the early understanding of that brain region’s role in what we now term ‘executive functions’. This focus on people who had abilities that were lost as a result of injury reinforces the direct correspondence between atypical and unhealthy. More than just this, a simplistic mapping of specific brain regions to cognitive, emotional, or sensorimotor functions generated a modular notion of the brain and shaped a largely fruitless and expensive quest to identify regional anomalies in the brain associated with specific diagnoses.

塑造我们“正常”概念的另一个科学传统是神经心理学史，其基础在于成人案例研究。在脑成像技术普及之前，对大脑不同区域功能的唯一洞见来自于那些“正常”大脑功能因损伤或中风而严重受损的案例。著名的菲尼亚斯·盖奇案例——一位在工作中前额叶遭受重创却幸存的铁路工人——为我们早期理解该大脑区域在如今所称“执行功能”中的作用提供了重要依据。这种对因损伤而丧失能力者的关注，强化了非典型与不健康之间的直接对应关系。不仅如此，将特定大脑区域简单映射到认知、情感或感觉运动功能的做法，催生了一种模块化的大脑观念，并引发了一场代价高昂却大多徒劳的探索，试图找出与特定诊断相关的大脑区域异常。

Sometimes, of course, concepts of ‘normality’ have been very useful. When it comes to relatively simple organs, such as the heart, a sense of the ‘normal’ heart rate has for the most part been useful for understanding when we should be worried about any given person’s health, and what a healthy range might look like. But in other cases, this approach has been far more controversial. Often the norms we construct have a racialized or gendered bias due to studies only focusing on certain parts of the population. This can lead to biased results that impact access to healthcare for marginalized people. Even in the seemingly simple example of a ‘normal’ heart rate, reliance on data drawn from a limited population (in terms of gender or race) produces unhelpfully narrow or skewed expectations. Similarly, our conceptions of ‘normal’ body weight may reinforce harmful and unrealistic pressures that all bodies should be the same specific kind of idealized body type.

当然，有时“正常”这一概念非常有用。对于相对简单的器官，比如心脏，了解“正常”心率在很大程度上有助于判断何时应关注某人的健康状况，以及健康范围大致是怎样的。但在其他情况下，这种方法则引发了更多争议。我们构建的规范往往带有种族或性别偏见，因为研究仅聚焦于特定人群。这可能导致结果偏颇，影响边缘群体获得医疗保健服务。即使在看似简单的“正常”心率例子中，依赖来自有限人群（就性别或种族而言）的数据也会产生过于狭隘或扭曲的期望。同样，我们对“正常”体重的概念可能强化了有害且不切实际的观念，即所有身体都应符合某种特定的理想体型。

Most relevantly for our purposes, the idea of the ‘normal’ brain or mind may contribute to stigma, misunderstanding, and support for harmful practices. In one trial, children with working memory problems were offered targeted training: the intervention improved working memory test scores, but did not generalize to better learning outcomes. In fact, these children ended up doing worse in their school maths tests, because they had missed maths lessons to do the working memory training. Neurodiversity proponents question whether we should retain the idea of an objectively ‘normal’ brain at all, if by ‘normal’ we mean correctly functioning. We now acknowledge that there is no correct sexuality, culture, or ethnicity, so why should we think there is a correct way for brains to develop? Likewise, we recognize that while a marginalized identity, such as being queer, may lead to societal disadvantage, the solution is not to change the person, but to change their circumstances. Neurodiversity proponents, and others, argue for the same approach to understanding and supporting neurodivergent people. When we consider these kinds of problems and questions, we can see that it might be time to develop a new paradigm. This would be one that doesn’t discriminate based on an arbitrary standard of normality, let alone standards determined by the needs of the capitalist economy rather than those of humans.

与我们目的最相关的是，“正常”大脑或心智的概念可能助长了污名化、误解以及对有害做法的支持。在一项试验中，有工作记忆问题的儿童接受了针对性训练：干预提高了工作记忆测试分数，但并未推广至更好的学习成果。事实上，这些儿童最终在学校数学考试中表现更差，因为他们为了进行工作记忆训练而错过了数学课。神经多样性倡导者质疑我们是否应该完全保留客观“正常”大脑的概念，如果“正常”意味着功能正确的话。我们现在承认没有正确的性取向、文化或种族，那么我们为什么认为大脑存在一种正确的发展方式呢？同样，我们认识到，虽然一种边缘化的身份，比如酷儿身份，可能导致社会劣势，但解决方案不是改变这个人，而是改变他们的环境。神经多样性倡导者和其他人主张采用同样的方法来理解和支持神经殊异人群。 当我们思考这类问题和疑问时，或许会发现，是时候建立一个新的范式了。这个范式不应基于武断的"正常"标准进行区分，更不应以资本主义经济需求而非人类需求为准则。

The need for a neurodiversity paradigm

神经多样性范式的必要性

The neurodiversity movement is the movement of people who are advocating for liberation of neurodivergent people. While there are influential neurodiversity activists, the movement has no leader and is made up of loosely connected individuals and groups across the globe. Anyone who advocates for justice for neurodivergent people in the various ways we describe in this book might be said to be part of the movement.

神经多样性运动是一场倡导神经殊异者解放的运动。虽然存在具有影响力的神经多样性活动家，但这场运动没有领导者，由全球范围内松散联系的个体和群体组成。任何以本书所述各种方式为神经殊异者争取正义的人，都可以被视为这场运动的一部分。

This is where the idea of the neurodiversity paradigm comes in. Walker suggests that a key goal of the neurodiversity movement can be understood as a widespread supplanting of the normalcy paradigm with the neurodiversity paradigm. This is her term for the theoretical, scientific, and cultural paradigm Walker sees as being built by neurodiversity proponents. In particular, she associates this emerging paradigm with a rejection of the idea of the ‘normal’ brain or mind being associated with the average range. Instead, it begins with an embrace of neurological diversity as itself ‘normal’ or natural. Here Walker follows earlier advocates, such as those on Independent Living, Harvey Blume, and Judy Singer, who suggest that just in the way it is ‘normal’ for a forest or meadow to have a diverse ecosystem, so too is it ‘normal’ for humanity to have a diversity of kinds of minds.

这正是神经多样性范式理念的切入点。沃克指出，神经多样性运动的一个核心目标可被理解为以神经多样性范式广泛取代常态范式。这是她为沃克眼中由神经多样性倡导者所构建的理论、科学及文化范式所创造的术语。她特别将这一新兴范式与摒弃“正常”大脑或心智等同于平均范围的观点联系起来。相反，它始于对神经多样性本身作为“正常”或自然状态的接纳。在此，沃克追随了早期倡导者如独立生活运动者、哈维·布鲁姆和朱迪·辛格的脚步，他们提出：正如森林或草地拥有多样化的生态系统是“正常”的，人类拥有多样化的心智类型同样也是“正常”的。

In this view, the fact that we discriminate against some minds and not others does not reflect a natural order, but rather current societal value. Consider the case of left-handedness, which was discriminated against historically. There is nothing inherently wrong with being left-handed, despite it being statistically rare, yet in the past left-handed people were forced to learn to use their right hands, rather than to embrace their natural disposition to use their left hands. While left-handedness is thought to be underpinned by neurological differences, and is atypical, we can now clearly see that left-handed people were not disordered and in need of fixing. Rather, they were punished because they were socially marginalized. The attempt to shift from the normalcy paradigm to a still emerging neurodiversity paradigm is partially analogous to this shift in understandings of handedness. After all, scientists still study left-handedness, and it is still acknowledged in educational settings, but without the unduly negative framing that was previously so widespread.

在这种观点看来，我们歧视某些心智类型而非其他，并不反映某种自然秩序，而是反映了当前的社会价值观。以左撇子为例，它在历史上曾遭受歧视。左撇子本身并无任何内在问题，尽管在统计上较为罕见，但在过去，左撇子被迫学习使用右手，而非接纳其天生使用左手的倾向。虽然左撇子被认为有神经学差异作为基础，且属于非典型情况，但我们现在可以清楚地看到，左撇子并非功能失调、需要矫正。相反，他们之所以受到惩罚，是因为在社会中被边缘化。从常态范式转向仍在发展中的神经多样性范式的尝试，在某种程度上类似于这种对手性认知的转变。毕竟，科学家仍在研究左撇子，教育环境中也仍然承认其存在，但不再像过去那样普遍地赋予其不当的负面框架。

As to the political significance of this shift, let us consider a second partial analogy. The attempt to build a neurodiversity paradigm follows a similar pattern of change we have already begun to see when it comes to other kinds of ethnic and cultural diversity. In the 19th century, for instance, many white British people, including leading scientists, thought that there was a natural hierarchy of races, with white people at the top. But now we know that was grounded in a racist worldview, and that no ethnicity is better than any other. Importantly, this shift is not just attitudinal—a progressive reframing in response to social pressure—but genuinely paradigmatic. We now believe the concept of race is socially constructed and has no basis in genetics, nor biology more generally. Moreover, we recognize that 19th-century attempts to rank the races scientifically were infused with white supremacist ideological and cultural baggage. These previous scientists thought that their view was objective, but we have since switched our paradigm. Scientists now study ethnic diversity among humans in a very different way, usually not grounded in a racist worldview to anything like the same extent. We say ‘to the same extent’ because racism does still affect scientific research to some degree, but it seems clear that there has been some progress in both scientific and cultural understandings since the 19th century.

关于这一转变的政治意义，让我们考虑第二个部分类比。构建神经多样性范式的尝试，遵循着我们在其他种族和文化多样性方面已经开始看到的类似变革模式。例如，在 19 世纪，许多英国白人，包括顶尖科学家，认为存在一种自然的种族等级制度，白人处于顶端。但现在我们知道，这种观点根植于种族主义世界观，没有任何一个种族优于其他种族。重要的是，这一转变不仅仅是态度上的——即在社会压力下的一种进步性重构——而是真正意义上的范式转变。我们现在相信种族概念是社会建构的，在遗传学乃至更广泛的生物学中没有基础。此外，我们认识到，19 世纪试图科学地对种族进行排名的做法，充满了白人至上主义的意识形态和文化包袱。那些过去的科学家认为他们的观点是客观的，但我们已经改变了我们的范式。 如今，科学家们以截然不同的方式研究人类的种族多样性，通常不再像过去那样根植于种族主义世界观。我们之所以说“像过去那样”，是因为种族主义在某种程度上仍然影响着科学研究，但自 19 世纪以来，科学和文化理解显然已取得一定进展。

It is important to note here that our current way of ranking brains and minds grew together, historically, with these earlier attempts to rank by race. Often it was the same scientists, such as Francis Galton, developing both sets of ranking. This relates to how racism was built into the origins of both capitalism and modern imperialism, as Black studies scholars such as Cedric Robinson have detailed. As with the study of ethnic diversity, making a shift away from these views when it comes to human neurological variation should similarly lead to a totally different way of conceptualizing, researching, and responding to issues relating to human neurodiversity. Following this partial analogy, we can see that the attempt to build a new paradigm is not just about improving scientific research, but also about cultivating disability justice and neurodivergent liberation. If we can build a better paradigm, the shift may in turn help us see how to build a better world that is more inclusive of neurodivergent people. The potential is not just for an improvement in scientific understanding, but also for moral progress, and to reorganize our society in a way that is liberating for everyone who falls outside the overly restrictive boundaries of the normalcy paradigm. This is an important part of what we want to establish throughout this book.

需要指出的是，我们当前对大脑和心智进行排序的方式，在历史上与早期按种族排序的尝试是一同发展起来的。通常，这是同一批科学家，如弗朗西斯·高尔顿，在同时发展这两套排序体系。这与种族主义如何被嵌入资本主义和现代帝国主义的起源有关，正如塞德里克·罗宾逊等黑人研究学者所详细阐述的那样。与种族多样性的研究类似，当涉及人类神经系统的变异时，摆脱这些观点，同样应该导向一种完全不同的方式来概念化、研究并应对与人类神经多样性相关的问题。沿着这一部分类比，我们可以看到，构建新范式的尝试不仅关乎改进科学研究，也关乎培育残障正义与神经殊异者的解放。如果我们能建立一个更好的范式，这种转变反过来可能帮助我们看清如何建设一个更包容神经殊异者的美好世界。 这种潜力不仅在于增进科学理解，还在于推动道德进步，并以一种解放性的方式重组我们的社会，让所有被过度狭隘的常态范式排除在外的人们获得自由。这正是我们希望通过本书确立的重要理念。

Contested and evolving terminology

充满争议且不断演变的术语体系

Before we clarify how we understand the neurodiversity paradigm, it is important to consider that the neurodiversity paradigm comes with a new set of terms and concepts. Yet we should also caveat that, as with all words and concepts, their meanings change over time, and which are most useful will continue to change. Doubtless readers of the future will reject some of the language we use, as thinking and discourse moves forward. Even at this moment in time, there is no single set of words that are necessarily associated with the neurodiversity paradigm or which all neurodiversity proponents use in the precise same way. And even those that are more often associated with it can be challenged or reinterpreted. Moreover, throughout this book we will draw parallels between the neurodiversity movement and other liberation movements and attempt to explore the intersectionality of those movements. The terminology of those communities is likewise shifting and evolving, and so it is certain that language we use here will be replaced over time.

在阐明我们如何理解神经多样性范式之前，有必要认识到，神经多样性范式带来了一套新的术语和概念。然而，我们也需提醒，如同所有词汇和概念一样，它们的含义会随时间而变化，哪些最为有用也将持续改变。随着思想和话语的进步，未来的读者无疑会摒弃我们使用的某些语言。即便在当下，也没有一套固定的词汇必然与神经多样性范式相关联，或者被所有神经多样性的支持者以完全相同的方式使用。即使是那些更常与之相关的词汇，也可能受到质疑或重新诠释。此外，在本书中，我们将把神经多样性运动与其他解放运动进行类比，并尝试探讨这些运动之间的交叉性。这些社群的术语同样在不断变化和发展，因此可以肯定，我们在此使用的语言也将会随时间被取代。

Still, in recent decades, at least a fairly coherent set of important terms and concepts has emerged, which we will adopt in this book. It will help to give some definitions before we go any further.

尽管如此，近几十年来，至少出现了一套相当连贯的重要术语和概念，我们将在本书中采用这些术语和概念。在进一步探讨之前，先给出一些定义会有所帮助。

By ‘neuro’ we are primarily referring to things to do with the brain or nervous system. This in turn is intimately intertwined with our mental life and our cognitive and emotional functioning. Often, when we say ‘neuro’ we will make the reasonable assumption that there is a link between neurological processes (e.g. synaptic firing, blood-flow in the brain) and mental processes—those relating to cognition or emotion—even if we don’t know exactly how this works yet in any given case. At the same time, though, we also make the equally reasonable and important assumption that mental functioning cannot be reduced to neurology. This is because mental functioning is also determined by all sorts of other things. These include other parts of the body, our social learning and relationships with other people, our current environment, our past experiences, our culture, and much else. Thus, when we say ‘neuro’ we mean it in a purposely broad sense, acknowledging how complex are the interactions between brain, body, and world that together constitute each of our mental lives.

“神经”一词主要指的是与大脑或神经系统相关的事物。这进而与我们的精神生活、认知和情感功能紧密交织。通常，当我们提到“神经”时，我们会做出一个合理的假设：神经过程（如突触放电、大脑中的血流）与心理过程——即与认知或情感相关的那些过程——之间存在联系，即使我们在具体情况下尚不清楚这种联系是如何运作的。然而，与此同时，我们也同样合理且重要地假设，心理功能不能简化为神经学。这是因为心理功能还受到许多其他因素的影响，包括身体的其他部分、我们的社会学习及与他人的关系、当前环境、过往经历、文化等等。因此，当我们说“神经”时，我们有意采用一个宽泛的含义，承认大脑、身体和世界之间复杂的相互作用共同构成了我们每个人的精神生活。

‘Diversity’ indicates that there is variation, and is a trait that only groups can have, not individuals. Combined with ‘neuro’, ‘neurodiversity’ refers to variations in neurological and nervous system functioning that we can say any given group has to a greater or lesser extent. For instance, a group of four people where one is autistic, another dyspraxic, another with ADHD, and another with schizophrenia would be a relatively neurologically diverse group. By contrast, a group of four where everyone has the same diagnosis, or where nobody qualifies for any diagnosis, would likely be relatively neurologically uniform. Importantly, it would not make sense to call an individual ‘neurodiverse’ unless they literally had multiple brains that were different from each other. For the most part, only groups can be neurodiverse, not individuals.

“多样性”意味着存在差异，并且是只有群体才可能具备、而非个体所能拥有的特征。与“神经”一词结合后，“神经多样性”指的是神经与神经系统功能上的差异，我们可以说任何特定群体都在不同程度上具有这种差异。例如，一个由四人组成的群体，其中一人是孤独谱系人士，另一人有发展性协调障碍，另一人患有注意力缺陷多动障碍，还有一人患有精神分裂症，那么这便是一个神经多样性程度相对较高的群体。相比之下，一个四人群体中若所有人都有相同的诊断，或无人符合任何诊断标准，则其神经特征可能相对单一。重要的是，除非一个人真的拥有多个彼此不同的大脑，否则称个体“神经多元”是没有意义的。在绝大多数情况下，只有群体才可能是神经多元的，而非个体。

The next important term is ‘neurotypical’. This is a term developed by neurodiversity proponents to refer to people who are considered to function ‘normally’, and thus who do not qualify for diagnoses of neurological disabilities. A neurotypical person might otherwise be described as ‘typically developed’ or as falling within the ‘normal range’ of cognitive and emotional functioning. It is important to emphasize, however, that in the neurodiversity paradigm this is not taken to refer to a natural grouping of people. Rather, who is considered normal will be determined by social norms of a given society. This in turn will be determined by the economic system, the state of technology, religious and ideological beliefs, and many other factors. Put another way, ‘neurotypicals’ refers to a rough cluster of people who sit in a fairly central place within the neurological power structures of a given society or global system. To recognize them as neurotypicals is to recognize their socially privileged position, rather than suggesting they are normal in a more objective sense, such as having a shared, identifiable essence in their brains.

下一个重要术语是“神经典型者”。这是神经多样性倡导者创造的一个术语，指那些被认为功能“正常”、因此不符合神经发育障碍诊断标准的人。神经典型者也可以被描述为“典型发育者”，或处于认知和情感功能的“正常范围”内。然而，必须强调的是，在神经多样性范式中，这并不被视为指代一个自然的人群分类。相反，谁被视为正常，将由特定社会的社会规范决定。而这又取决于经济体系、技术发展水平、宗教和意识形态信仰以及许多其他因素。换句话说，“神经典型者”指的是在特定社会或全球体系的神经权力结构中处于相当中心位置的一个大致人群集合。将他们识别为神经典型者，是为了认识到他们的社会特权地位，而不是暗示他们在更客观的意义上是正常的，例如他们的大脑中具有某种共同的、可识别的本质。

In contrast to the neurotypical are those who are neurodivergent (coined by Kasianne Asasumasu). Just as neurotypical refers to anyone who falls closer to the normative ideal of the society, those who are neurodivergent fall outside that ideal. There is no strict or clear dividing line since these norms themselves have some level of vagueness and also shift. But neurodivergence is generally associated with people who struggle to function in line with the neurological norms of a society, whose needs are less commonly met within standard systems (e.g. mainstream school classrooms), and who are discriminated against specifically in light of this. Some people might choose to identify as multiply neurodivergent where they have more than one overlapping profile that would on its own be considered neurodivergent—for example, people with a diagnosis of ADHD and autism. However, the term neurodivergent is not meant to be limited to those with one of a specific list of diagnoses, and so identifying as neurodivergent alone can capture any profile outside the current norm. Individuals who are neurodivergent might also use other language to describe themselves, such as neuro-atypical, or a specific diagnostic label, such as dyspraxic. Of course, every individual can and should use terminology they prefer, and in this book we are more concerned with language we can use when talking in general terms about neurodiversity.

与神经典型者形成对比的是神经殊异者（由 Kasianne Asasumasu 创造）。正如神经典型者指那些更接近社会规范理想的人，神经殊异者则落在此理想之外。由于这些规范本身存在一定程度的模糊性且会变化，因此没有严格或清晰的分界线。但神经殊异性通常与那些难以按照社会神经学规范运作的人相关联，他们的需求在标准体系（例如主流学校课堂）中较少得到满足，并因此受到歧视。有些人可能选择认同为多重神经殊异，即他们拥有不止一种重叠的特质，而每种特质本身都可被视为神经殊异——例如，被诊断为 ADHD 和孤独谱系的人。然而，神经殊异一词并非旨在仅限于那些拥有特定诊断列表中的一种的人，因此，仅认同为神经殊异本身就能涵盖当前规范之外的任何特质。 神经殊异个体也可能使用其他术语来描述自己，比如神经非典型，或者具体的诊断标签，如运动障碍。当然，每个人都可以并且应该使用他们偏好的术语，而在本书中，我们更关注的是在一般性地谈论神经多样性时可以使用的语言。

Most neurodivergent people are disabled, although there are also neurodivergent people who are only marginally neurodivergent, not to the point of being disabled. For instance, left-handedness can be seen as a form of marginal neurodivergence. While left-handed people are no longer stigmatized, many things, from scissors to guitars, are still typically built for right-handed people, and this can sometimes be a problem for those who are left-handed. We also include degenerative illnesses such as dementia, mental health conditions such as bipolar disorder or schizophrenia, and some neurologically based physical conditions, such as epilepsy, in neurodivergence. Neurodivergence can be non-medical (as in the case of left-handedness) or medical (as in the case of epilepsy). Thus while ‘neurodivergence’ helps us talk about minds that fall outside the ‘norm’ without pathologizing them, this term alone does not imply any particular health status. This is important to remember because, even though the neurodiversity movement exists partly to move away from default pathologization, people with disorders also face systemic forms of injustice and human rights abuses on account of diverging from neuronormativity, no less than wrongfully pathologized neurodivergent people.

大多数神经殊异人士都是残疾人士，尽管也存在一些仅具有边缘性神经殊异特征、尚未达到残疾程度的人。例如，左撇子可被视为一种边缘性的神经殊异表现。虽然左撇子已不再被污名化，但许多物品——从剪刀到吉他——通常仍是为右撇子设计的，这有时会给左撇子带来不便。我们也将痴呆症等退行性疾病、双相情感障碍或精神分裂症等心理健康状况，以及癫痫等某些神经性躯体疾病纳入神经殊异性的范畴。神经殊异性可以是非医学性的（如左撇子），也可以是医学性的（如癫痫）。因此，尽管“神经殊异性”这一概念有助于我们讨论那些偏离“常态”的心智状态而不将其病理化，但仅凭这个术语本身并不暗示任何特定的健康状况。 这一点很重要，因为尽管神经多样性运动的存在部分是为了摆脱默认的病理化倾向，但患有障碍的人同样会因为偏离神经规范性而面临系统性的不公正和人权侵犯，其程度不亚于被错误病理化的神经殊异者。

A helpful term for groups of neurodivergent people is ‘neurominority’ (coined by Nick Walker). These are minority groups of people with at least vaguely similar traits in their cognitive or emotional functioning. Usually so far, this term has been used to reclaim psychiatric diagnoses such as autism or ADHD, and to reinterpret them in line with the neurodiversity paradigm framing. It is important to emphasize, however, that such classifications could have been different. They are as they are given complex historical circumstances rather than being natural groupings. For instance, ‘autism’ is a concept that has continually shifted since being termed in the early 20th century, as various social, economic, and political factors relating to sensory and emotional processing continue to change. There is also lots of overlap between many neurominorities and variation within any given one. Two autistic people might be very different from each other, while some autistic people are quite similar, cognitively speaking, to some people with ADHD. In this, neurominorities have some level of similarity with other kinds of minorities. Our conceptions of race and ethnicity, for instance, are not natural groupings, but rather reflect complex historical conditions that led to certain naming conventions for groups of people with roughly similar clusters of traits. Similarly, neurominorities are not natural groupings, but rather reflect the power structures of a given age, which lead us to notice some clusters of traits more than others.

一个用于指代神经殊异群体的有用术语是"神经少数群体"（由尼克·沃克创造）。这些少数群体在认知或情感功能上至少具有大致相似的特征。迄今为止，这个术语通常被用来重新定义诸如孤独谱系或 ADHD 等精神医学诊断，并依据神经多样性范式的框架对其进行重新诠释。然而，必须强调的是，这样的分类本可以是不同的。它们之所以是现在的样子，是由于复杂的历史环境，而非天然形成的群体。例如，"孤独谱系"这一概念自 20 世纪初被提出以来就不断演变，因为与感官和情感处理相关的各种社会、经济和政治因素持续变化。许多神经少数群体之间存在大量重叠，且任何特定群体内部也存在差异。两个孤独谱系个体可能彼此非常不同，而有些孤独谱系个体在认知上与有 ADHD 的群体相当相似。在这方面，神经少数群体与其他类型的少数群体具有一定程度的相似性。 例如，我们对种族和民族的概念并非自然形成的分类，而是反映了复杂的历史条件，这些条件导致了对具有大致相似特征群体的一系列命名惯例。同样，神经少数群体也并非自然形成的分类，而是反映了特定时代的权力结构，这些结构使我们更关注某些特征组合而非其他。

Finally, ‘neuronormativity’ refers to societal valuations of different kinds of neurological or cognitive functioning. The term was developed in particular to challenge default assumptions that some kinds of brains or minds are just inherently superior or inferior to others: for instance, that neurotypicality is superior to neurodivergence. Instead of seeing our current societal cognitive hierarchies as timeless and objective, the concept of neuronormativity draws attention to how our neurological norms always reflect not just natural differences in functioning, but also contingent societal and cultural expectations.

最后，"神经规范性"指的是社会对不同类型神经或认知功能的价值评判。这一术语的提出，尤其旨在挑战那种认为某些类型的大脑或心智天生就优于或劣于其他类型的默认假设：例如，认为神经典型性优于神经殊异性。神经规范性的概念并非将当前社会中的认知等级视为永恒且客观的，而是提醒我们注意：我们的神经规范总是不仅反映了功能上的自然差异，也反映了偶然的社会和文化期望。

There is also some language associated with the normalcy paradigm which is worth briefly defining, since neurodiversity is often making efforts to explain, interpret, and sometimes replace these categories. Most forms of neurodivergence, under the normalcy paradigm, would fall into one of five categories. Learning difficulties (also called specific learning difficulties) are those forms of neurodivergence most apparent in education contexts, and often diagnosed within the school system rather than by clinicians. Examples include dyslexia, dyscalculia, and dysgraphia. A learning disability, by contrast, is diagnosed in the presence of an IQ score below 70, representing a relatively comprehensive challenge to learning new information. Many individuals with a learning disability will also have some kind of genetic syndrome, such as Down syndrome, fragile x syndrome, or Williams syndrome, which commonly entails a low IQ test score along with other common features. A neurodevelopmental disorder (or condition) is normally diagnosed by a clinician, often a psychologist, and is a lifelong diagnosis which usually becomes apparent in childhood and shapes developmental pathways. Examples include ADHD, autism, and developmental language disorder. With the exception of stimulants for people with ADHD, it is rare for any of these three categories to be treated with medications—though many may take medicines for co-occurring difficulties like anxiety or poor sleep. A mental disorder or mental illness is usually diagnosed by a psychiatrist and often medications are a primary treatment option. Examples of things widely considered mental disorders include bipolar disorder, schizophrenia, and obsessive-compulsive disorder. Though many may be chronic, they are not necessarily considered lifelong and cures are both pursued and, in some cases, achieved. Finally, there is a range of neurodegenerative disorders including the dementias, Parkinson’s disease, and motor neurone disease. These tend to arise in middle-to-late life and represent a degeneration in cognitive, affective, and sensorimotor abilities. One prominent form of neurodivergence that isn’t neatly represented in these categories is epilepsy (and other seizure disorders). Any person falling into one or more of these groups might consider themselves disabled, depending on their context, experience, and identity. Of note, these definitions adhere to standard UK usage and may vary around the world—for example in the USA the term ‘learning disability’ can be used to refer to what we call ‘learning difficulties’, while Americans would use ‘intellectual disability’ for the UK’s ‘learning disability’. More broadly, outside of the terms developed in Western psychiatry over the last two centuries, there are countless further terms and concepts that name various forms of things we refer to as neurodivergence, relative to each culture and place. We advocate a version of the neurodiversity paradigm that holds space for a range of understandings from around the globe.

与正常性范式相关的一些术语也值得简要定义，因为神经多样性常常致力于解释、诠释，有时甚至替代这些分类。在正常性范式下，大多数神经殊异形式可归入以下五类之一。学习困难（亦称特定学习困难）是那些在教育情境中最为明显的神经殊异形式，通常在学校体系内而非临床医生处诊断。例如阅读障碍、计算障碍和书写障碍。相比之下，学习障碍的诊断则需智商分数低于 70，代表学习新信息面临相对全面的挑战。许多学习障碍者还伴有某种遗传综合征，如唐氏综合征、脆性 X 综合征或威廉姆斯综合征，这些综合征通常导致智商测试分数偏低及其他共同特征。神经发育障碍（或状况）通常由临床医生（常为心理学家）诊断，是一种终身诊断，通常在童年时期显现并影响发展路径。 例如 ADHD、孤独谱系以及发展性语言障碍。除了对有 ADHD 的群体使用兴奋剂外，这三种类别很少通过药物治疗——尽管许多人可能会因伴随的困难如焦虑或睡眠不佳而服药。精神障碍或精神疾病通常由精神科医生诊断，药物治疗往往是主要的治疗选择。被广泛认为是精神障碍的例子包括双相情感障碍、精神分裂症和强迫症。尽管许多可能是慢性的，但它们不一定被视为终身性的，并且人们既在寻求治愈方法，在某些情况下也实现了治愈。最后，还有一系列神经退行性疾病，包括痴呆症、帕金森病和运动神经元病。这些疾病往往在中晚年出现，表现为认知、情感和感觉运动能力的退化。在这些类别中没有得到清晰体现的一种显著神经殊异性形式是癫痫（以及其他发作性疾病）。 任何属于一个或多个这些类别的人，根据其背景、经历和身份认同，可能会认为自己有残疾。值得注意的是，这些定义遵循英国的标准用法，在世界各地可能有所不同——例如，在美国，"learning disability" 一词可能用来指我们所说的 "learning difficulties"，而美国人会用 "intellectual disability" 来指代英国的 "learning disability"。更广泛地说，在过去两个世纪西方精神病学发展出的术语之外，还有无数其他的术语和概念，用于命名我们称之为神经殊异性的各种形式的事物，这些术语和概念因文化和地域而异。我们倡导一种神经多样性范式的版本，该版本为来自全球的各种理解留出空间。

How we understand the neurodiversity paradigm

我们如何理解神经多样性范式

Now we have covered some—although by no means all—basic concepts and history, we are in a position to return to the understanding of the neurodiversity paradigm we adopt for this book. Before we get to this, it is important to emphasize that while there are more or less helpful ways to understand the neurodiversity paradigm, there is no single or correct way to conceptualize it. Especially since it is something that is still emerging and continually changing, any attempt to summarize it will remain incomplete.

在介绍了部分（尽管远非全部）基本概念和历史之后，我们现在可以回到本书所采用的神经多样性范式的理解上。在此之前需要强调的是，虽然理解神经多样性范式的方式存在优劣之分，但并没有唯一或正确的概念化路径。尤其鉴于这一范式仍在形成中且持续演变，任何概括性尝试都难免存在局限。

Still, for the purposes of this book, one way of thinking about it is to break it down into core principles, which together fit well with the kinds of efforts we associate with the neurodiversity movement. While there are various valid ways to do this, for this book we suggest that in its simplest form, we can associate the neurodiversity paradigm with two core principles: affirm complexity and politicize neuronormativity. We will now explain these in turn, and how they differ from the normalcy paradigm, before going on to apply them throughout this book.

不过就本书而言，一种思考方式是将该范式分解为核心原则，这些原则共同契合神经多样性运动所倡导的实践方向。虽然存在多种有效的分解方式，但本书认为其最简形式可归纳为两大核心原则：肯定复杂性，以及政治化神经规范性。接下来我们将依次阐释这两项原则及其与常态范式的差异，并在此后的章节中持续运用这些原则。

Affirm complexity

肯定复杂性

To explain what we mean by affirm complexity, it is first worth noting that all science is value-laden to at least some extent. This is because science is a human activity and everything humans do is driven by what our values are. We study chemistry, for instance, because we value understanding and manipulating the natural world, while we study medicine because we value health. That science is a value-laden activity is simply part of what science is, and thus is not, in itself, a bad thing. However, sometimes science and practice can at least implicitly be driven by ideological values that may end up being oppressive or harmful. This is part of the issue we identify in the normalcy paradigm and hope to correct with the alternative principles of the neurodiversity paradigm.

要解释我们所说的“肯定复杂性”意味着什么，首先值得指出的是，所有科学在某种程度上都带有价值取向。这是因为科学是一种人类活动，而人类所做的一切都受到我们价值观的驱动。例如，我们研究化学是因为我们重视理解和操控自然世界，而我们研究医学则是因为我们重视健康。科学是一种带有价值取向的活动，这本身就是科学的一部分，因此，就其本身而言，这并非坏事。然而，有时科学和实践可能至少隐性地受到意识形态价值观的驱动，这些价值观最终可能具有压迫性或有害性。这正是我们在常态范式中识别出的问题之一，并希望通过神经多样性范式的替代原则来加以纠正。

In our view, the normalcy paradigm is, in significant part, driven by the aim of controlling neurological complexity across the human population. Sometimes controlling biological heterogeneity is good. For instance, it is good for scientists to try to control cancer, diabetes, or dementia. But the normalcy paradigm takes the need to control heterogeneity too far. This paradigm is both based on, and reinforces, an overvaluation of cognitive and emotional uniformity and order in the human population. We can see this when we consider that much of our medical and psychological research and practice assumes that neurological heterogeneity is always a bad thing, and that neurological divergence is something we should always try to correct. The issue is that this seeks to control our species-level neurological heterogeneity in line with how we seek to control things like cancer or diabetes. This can be detrimental for people who are atypical but who do not want to be controlled, and indeed who find pressures to conform harmful.

在我们看来，常态范式在很大程度上是由控制人类群体中神经复杂性的目标所驱动的。有时控制生物异质性是件好事。例如，科学家努力控制癌症、糖尿病或痴呆症是值得肯定的。但常态范式将控制异质性的需求推向了极端。这一范式既基于对人类认知和情感统一性与秩序性的过度重视，又进一步强化了这种观念。当我们考虑到，我们的许多医学和心理学研究与实践都假定神经异质性总是不好的，神经差异总是我们应该努力纠正的问题时，就能看到这一点。问题在于，这种做法试图按照我们控制癌症或糖尿病的方式来控制我们物种层面的神经异质性。这对于那些非典型但不想被控制，甚至认为顺应压力是有害的人来说，可能是有害的。

We also see this overvaluation of uniformity manifesting in how diagnoses are conceived of. Consider the example of autism. As with many other diagnoses, much research on autism has been geared to finding an autistic ‘essence’ in the genes, brain, or cognition of autistic people. The implicit point of this is to be able to control autism, for instance by developing a prenatal test for terminating autistic foetuses or finding a neurological marker that could be used to identify autistic infants and shape their environment to ‘prevent’ them from ‘becoming’ autistic. So far, we have not found underlying biomarkers for autism, and within the normalcy paradigm this is seen as a failure. Indeed, in response to this perceived failure, some researchers suggest that the classification of autism lacks utility or should be abandoned in favour of more specific classifications that would map onto clear biomarkers. While individual researchers on this quest may not be seeking to control individual autistic people, the general endeavour serves to control in terms of being able to predict who is autistic and shape them into a more ‘normal’ ideal. Notably too, these kinds of efforts and discourses are not limited to autism, but are also something we see in many other similar diagnoses, from dyslexia to ADHD. As with autism, most learning difficulties and mental disorders have no known single biomarker, and often this leads to calls to abandon or refine such classifications. This looks more like people being adapted to serve science, rather than the opposite way around.

我们也看到这种对一致性的过度重视体现在诊断概念的构建方式上。以孤独谱系为例。与许多其他诊断一样，大量关于孤独谱系的研究旨在从孤独谱系群体的基因、大脑或认知中找到一种孤独谱系的“本质”。这背后的隐含目的是为了能够控制孤独谱系，例如通过开发产前检测来终止孤独谱系胎儿的妊娠，或寻找可用于识别孤独谱系婴儿的神经标记，并塑造他们的环境以“防止”他们“变成”孤独谱系。迄今为止，我们尚未找到孤独谱系的潜在生物标志物，而在常态范式中，这被视为一种失败。事实上，针对这种被感知的失败，一些研究人员提出，孤独谱系的分类缺乏实用性，应被放弃，转而采用更具体的分类，这些分类将对应明确的生物标志物。尽管从事这项研究的个别研究人员可能并非旨在控制具体的孤独谱系个体，但这一总体努力在能够预测谁是孤独谱系并塑造他们以符合更“正常”的理想方面，确实起到了控制作用。 值得注意的是，这些努力和讨论并不仅限于孤独谱系，我们在许多其他类似的诊断中也能看到，从阅读障碍到注意力缺陷多动障碍（ADHD）都是如此。与孤独谱系一样，大多数学习困难和心理障碍都没有已知的单一生物标志物，这常常导致人们呼吁放弃或改进这类分类。这看起来更像是人们在适应科学，而不是相反。

While normalcy paradigm science is surely genuine science—rather than pseudoscience—it is guided by implicit values for uniformity that undermine our ability to recognize, support, and value a wider range of human neurodiversity. By contrast, we suggest, the neurodiversity paradigm does not see uniformity (or even more precise classification) as the goal. For instance, when it comes to the autism classification, neurodiversity proponents tend to embrace the heterogeneity within the autistic population. They more often see this heterogeneity as part of what constitutes autistic community and culture. From the neurodiversity paradigm perspective, then, it is not necessarily a failure of our disability classifications that they contain diversity. Rather, it is a source of the richness of the communities that form around them. After all, a community or culture where everyone was identical would most likely lack the kind of richness that comes with including more diversity. Hence the neurodiversity perspective more often embraces heterogeneity at the level of the classification.

虽然常态范式科学无疑是真正的科学——而非伪科学——但它受到追求统一性的隐性价值观引导，这种价值观削弱了我们识别、支持和珍视更广泛人类神经多样性的能力。相比之下，我们认为，神经多样性范式并不将统一性（甚至更精确的分类）视为目标。例如，在孤独谱系分类方面，神经多样性的支持者倾向于接纳孤独谱系群体内部的异质性。他们更多地将这种异质性视为构成孤独谱系社群与文化的一部分。因此，从神经多样性范式的视角来看，残疾分类中包含多样性并不必然意味着分类的失败。相反，这恰恰是围绕这些分类形成的社群丰富性的源泉。毕竟，一个每个人都完全相同的社群或文化，很可能缺乏因包容更多样性而带来的那种丰富性。因此，神经多样性的视角更常在分类层面接纳异质性。

More broadly, from a neurodiversity approach, we should also affirm complexity at the species level. Rather than automatically seeing divergence from the norm as something to be feared or controlled, we should precisely expect divergence at the population level and should base our research, practice, and policy on this expectation. After all, it is not just that many of us are born diverging from the statistically normal neurological functioning. It is also that all of us, including neurotypicals, become neurodivergent if we live long enough. This can be through accidents that impact cognitive functioning, acquired impairments such as those associated with long Covid, or, ultimately, cognitive decline and degenerative diseases such as Alzheimer’s in later life. Affirming complexity requires recognizing that there are a diverse range of support needs across the human spectrum, and that all should be accommodated regardless of how far from the norm they fall. It also requires having medical care in place for those conditions where this is relevant, such as epilepsy or dementia.

更广泛地说，从神经多样性的视角出发，我们也应在物种层面肯定复杂性。我们不应自动将偏离常态视为需要恐惧或控制的事物，而恰恰应预期在群体层面存在差异，并基于这一预期来构建我们的研究、实践与政策。毕竟，不仅我们许多人天生就偏离了统计意义上的正常神经功能，而且包括神经典型者在内的所有人，只要活得足够久，都会变得神经殊异。这可能源于影响认知功能的事故、后天获得的损伤（如与长期新冠相关的症状），或者最终在晚年出现的认知衰退和退行性疾病（如阿尔茨海默病）。肯定复杂性要求我们认识到，人类谱系中存在多样化的支持需求，无论这些需求偏离常态多远，都应得到满足。同时，这也要求为那些相关的病症（如癫痫或痴呆）提供相应的医疗照护。

A related requirement of the demand to affirm complexity is to recognize the strength and opportunity that arises from our naturally occurring diversity. This is an important way to embed the call for recognition of the many and varied ways that individuals bring value to our society. The radical potential of the idea rests on recognition that heterogeneity in the human race—or in any subgroup of that whole—is in itself a source of strength and creativity.

与肯定复杂性要求相关的是，要认识到我们自然存在的多样性所带来的力量与机遇。这是将呼吁认可个体以多种多样方式为社会创造价值的重要途径。这一理念的激进潜力在于认识到，人类整体或其中任何子群体的异质性本身就是力量与创造力的源泉。

On a practical level, for instance, diversity between people means we bring different experiences and views to the table and propose varied solutions to the challenges in our lives and society. This may have concrete benefits: diversity drives creativity and innovation as we spark ideas from each other and work collectively to tackle the many and varied barriers we each encounter in our lives. One study, for instance, found that adding one person with ADHD to a group of ‘normal’ controls made that group significantly better at creative problem solving, despite ADHD being associated with disability at the individual level. But more than this, a benefit of collective variety is the requirement to empathize—a society where everyone is the same is a society where we no longer need to imagine someone else’s perspective or experience, nor work to escape our own narrow view.

从实践层面来看，人与人之间的多样性意味着我们能为讨论带来不同的经验和观点，并为生活和社会中的挑战提出多样化的解决方案。这可能会带来具体的好处：多样性推动创造力和创新，因为我们相互激发想法，并共同努力应对生活中各自遇到的各种障碍。例如，一项研究发现，在一个由“正常”对照组组成的团队中加入一名患有注意力缺陷多动障碍（ADHD）的成员，能显著提升该团队的创造性问题解决能力，尽管 ADHD 在个体层面常被视为一种障碍。但更重要的是，集体多样性的益处在于它要求我们具备同理心——在一个所有人都相同的社会里，我们不再需要想象他人的视角或经历，也无需努力摆脱自身狭隘的视野。

To be clear, affirming complexity does not mean overlooking difficulties or never trying to control neurodivergent traits. For instance, we think it is vital to develop treatments to target diseases such as Alzheimer’s, alongside socially supporting those with this condition. However, even in this relatively clear-cut example, an over-focus on the former and under-investment in the latter is a cause for concern. Our sole approach to neurodivergence—even in its most negative form—cannot be prevention and elimination. We must also incorporate support and understanding. Affirming complexity is about acknowledging that neurological diversity is inevitable and often forms part of the richness of human cultures as much as it is associated with illness or disability. Neurodiversity must shape our research, practice, and policy to accommodate that, so that neurodivergent people can thrive across the spectrum of humanity, regardless of whether we are healthy, disabled, or ill.

需要澄清的是，肯定复杂性并不意味着忽视困难或从不尝试控制神经殊异特质。例如，我们认为针对阿尔茨海默病等疾病开发治疗方法，同时为患者提供社会支持至关重要。然而，即便在这个相对清晰的案例中，过度关注前者而忽视后者投入也令人担忧。我们对神经殊异性——即使其以最负面的形式呈现——的唯一方法不能仅仅是预防和消除。我们还必须融入支持与理解。肯定复杂性就是要承认神经多样性是不可避免的，它常常构成人类文化丰富性的一部分，正如它与疾病或残疾相关联那样。神经多样性必须塑造我们的研究、实践和政策以适应这一点，从而使神经殊异者能够在人类全谱系中茁壮成长，无论我们是健康、残疾还是患病。

Politicize neuronormativity

将神经规范性政治化

The second principle is politicize neuronormativity. Neuronormativity regards how we evaluate which forms of neurological functioning are desirable or undesirable, and how this relates to what we consider normal or not. Often, the way we rank different kinds of minds is simply seen as natural. For instance, it is often assumed that having higher intelligence is simply naturally and objectively better than having lower intelligence. It is also often assumed that being ‘normal’ is simply inherently better than being disabled, and so on.

第二个原则是政治化神经规范性。神经规范性涉及我们如何评估哪些形式的神经功能是可取的或不可取的，以及这如何与我们视为正常或不正常的标准相关联。通常，我们对不同思维方式的排序被简单地视为自然现象。例如，人们常常认为拥有较高的智力自然且客观地优于较低的智力。同样，人们也常常认为"正常"本质上就优于残疾状态，等等。

Politicizing neuronormativity challenges this through several interrelated commitments. Broadly, these question the way neurological or cognitive ability has often been constructed as an individual or natural matter. This is important, for us, as part of the power of the normalcy paradigm has precisely been to make things like autism or dyslexia seem like natural and individual dysfunctions rather than relationally constituted disabilities. Politicizing neuronormativity resists this naturalization, and helps us better understand the nature and working of neuronormativity.

政治化神经规范性通过几个相互关联的承诺来挑战这种观念。广义而言，这些承诺质疑神经或认知能力常被构建为个人或自然问题的传统方式。这对我们至关重要，因为正常性范式的部分力量恰恰在于使孤独谱系或阅读障碍等现象看起来像是自然且个人的功能障碍，而非关系性构成的残疾。政治化神经规范性抵制这种自然化倾向，并帮助我们更好地理解神经规范性的本质及其运作方式。

The first way the paradigm commits to this is to always view what counts as ‘normal’ or ‘healthy’ neurological, cognitive, or behavioural functioning as itself something that occurs in a specific social and historical context. This is not to reject that the use of population averages can have scientific utility—as in the case of using a normal distribution of blood pressure to identify individuals whose blood pressure is worryingly low or high. Neither is it to deny that some conception of mental or neurological health or pathology is vital for medical science and healthcare as we know it. Rather, it is to acknowledge that while these often can have utility from a scientific and humanitarian perspective, they are nonetheless always mediated by cultural and economic norms. For instance, dyslexia only came to be seen as a pathology in literate societies that functioned through standardized schooling. In preliterate societies people we would now call dyslexic would have existed, but they would not have been disabled. Moreover, concepts of pathology always arise within and often reproduce unjust power relations of a given time and place. For example, women who resist patriarchal oppression have been pathologized as ‘hysterical’, when in fact they were responding to their oppression in a reasonable way. Similarly, Black civil rights activists in the USA in the 1960s were pathologized as having a ‘protest psychosis’. Being aware of the political nature of neuronormativity, and how it relates not just to disability but also other intersections, is thus vital.

该范式实现这一点的首要方式，是始终将所谓“正常”或“健康”的神经、认知或行为功能本身，视为在特定社会历史背景下的产物。这并非否定使用人口平均值可能具有科学价值——例如利用血压的正态分布来识别血压过低或过高的人群。也并非否认某种关于精神或神经健康与病理的概念对医学科学和医疗保健至关重要。相反，这是要承认，尽管从科学和人道主义的角度来看，这些概念往往具有实用价值，但它们始终受到文化和经济规范的调节。例如，阅读障碍只有在依赖标准化教育的识字社会中才被视为一种病理现象。在文字出现前的社会里，那些我们今天称为阅读障碍者的人虽然存在，却并不会被视为残障。此外，病理概念总是在特定时空背景下产生，并常常复制当时当地不公正的权力关系。 例如，反抗父权压迫的女性曾被病理化为"歇斯底里"，而实际上她们只是以合理的方式回应压迫。同样，20 世纪 60 年代美国黑人民权活动家也曾被病理化为患有"抗议性精神病"。 认识到神经规范性的政治本质，及其不仅与残障相关、更与其他交叉性议题的关联，因此至关重要。

The second key way neuronormativity is politicized is in terms of how we understand ability and disability. In the normalcy paradigm, these have tended to be understood as individual attributes, which could either be stronger or weaker when compared to comparable attributes in other people. But the neurodiversity perspective, while acknowledging that individual biology is part of what grounds abilities, always sees them as socially, relationally, and collectively produced. That is, whether any given neurological or cognitive trait turns out to be useful or not will depend on a range of contextual factors. This includes what the task is, what technology or resources the individual has access to, the immediate environment they are in and how it was constructed, who they are working with, their motivation, and so forth.

神经规范被政治化的第二个关键方式，在于我们如何理解能力与残疾。在常态范式中，这些往往被理解为个体属性，当与其他人的类似属性相比较时，可能更强或更弱。但神经多样性的视角，虽然承认个体生物学是能力基础的一部分，却始终将它们视为在社会、关系和集体中产生的。也就是说，任何特定的神经或认知特质是否有用，将取决于一系列情境因素。这包括任务是什么、个体能获得的技术或资源、他们所处的直接环境及其构建方式、他们与谁合作、他们的动机等等。

Relatedly, it is also important to consider that whether people tend to count as ‘strong’ or ‘weak’ is also culturally produced. For example, whether we see a disposition to be highly emotional and cry in response to personal tragedy as strong or weak will depend on cultural norms, not to mention expectation relating to age, gender, race, and so forth. For instance, there is often more pressure on Black women to seem strong and to not cry, while white women may find they experience comparatively more support when they cry. This is important to note because, often, and at any given time, people will assume that their cultural norms relating to emotional and cognitive dispositions are objective, correct, or universal. But in fact they are contingent, and since cultural norms can be oppressive for those who fall outside them, finding ways to position our understandings of ability and disability in these ways is also a vital part of the neurodiversity paradigm lens.

与此相关，同样重要的是要认识到，人们通常被视为“坚强”还是“软弱”也是文化塑造的结果。例如，我们是将面对个人悲剧时情绪激动、容易哭泣的倾向视为坚强还是软弱，这取决于文化规范，更不用说与年龄、性别、种族等相关的期望了。举例来说，黑人女性往往面临更大的压力，需要表现得坚强、不轻易流泪，而白人女性在哭泣时可能会感受到相对更多的支持。这一点值得注意，因为人们常常会认为，自己在情感和认知倾向方面的文化规范是客观、正确或普世的。但事实上，这些规范是偶然的，并且由于文化规范可能对那些不符合规范的人造成压迫，因此，以这种方式来定位我们对能力和残疾的理解，也是神经多样性范式视角的重要组成部分。

Overall, acknowledging all of this and making all efforts to be vigilant of the potential ways neuronormativity can reproduce oppressive power dynamics is a vital part of politicizing neuronormativity. To work within a neurodiversity paradigm approach, then, this understanding and awareness must be built into everything from study design in scientific research to policies regarding the ways schools and workplaces are organized. As we will further clarify throughout this book, this is necessary for improving our theory, research, and practice in ways that are neurodivergence-inclusive.

总的来说，承认这一切并竭尽全力警惕神经规范性可能再现压迫性权力动态的各种方式，是神经规范性政治化的关键部分。因此，要在神经多样性范式框架内开展工作，就必须将这种理解和意识融入从科学研究的设计到学校和工作场所组织方式的相关政策等方方面面。正如我们将在本书中进一步阐明的那样，这对于以包容神经殊异性的方式改进我们的理论、研究和实践是必要的。

Taking the two core principles of affirming complexity and politicizing neuronormativity helps us remain aware of how different forms of oppression often intersect. The neurodiversity paradigm will fail if it aims at neurodivergent liberation only, rather than collective liberation more generally. This means that to make the neurodiversity paradigm effective, its proponents also need to commit to other liberatory struggles.

秉持肯定复杂性和政治化神经规范性这两项核心原则，有助于我们认识到不同形式的压迫往往是如何相互交织的。如果神经多样性范式仅仅旨在实现神经殊异者的解放，而非更广泛的集体解放，那么它终将失败。这意味着，要使神经多样性范式行之有效，其倡导者也需要投身于其他解放斗争。



---

Chapter 2 Neurodiversity as democratic theory and research

Chapter 2 Neurodiversity as democratic theory and research

第二章  作为民主理论与研究的神经多样性

In the previous chapter we began to introduce what we might call ‘neurodiversity theory’. This refers to the body of theory associated with the neurodiversity movement. In this chapter we will cover core components of the theory in more detail, with a particular focus on models of disability, the very idea of the ‘normal’ mind or brain, and the nature of neurominorities and controversies around diagnosis. This by no means covers all of neurodiversity, but these are core themes that are helpful for beginning with.

在上一章中，我们开始介绍可称为“神经多样性理论”的内容。这指的是与神经多样性运动相关的理论体系。本章我们将更详细地探讨该理论的核心组成部分，特别聚焦于残障模型、“正常”心智或大脑这一概念本身，以及神经少数群体的本质与围绕诊断的争议。这绝非涵盖神经多样性的全部内容，但这些核心主题有助于我们入门。

While we cover several different themes, something we want to emphasize throughout is that in the neurodiversity movement we see a shift towards a democratic approach to theory and research. By this we mean a shift away from viewing knowledge, and the practices we base on this, being constructed by a relatively small number of (usually neurotypical) experts, and towards a broader understanding of expertise as dispersed across our neurologically diverse populations. We take this shift towards greater democracy as following from the core neurodiversity paradigm principles of affirming complexity and politicizing neuronormativity, since democracy is always an attempt to navigate the complexities of political issues. It is notable here that a slogan of the Disability Rights movement, as well as of struggles for Black liberation, has long been ‘nothing about us without us’. With this in mind, the notion of neurodiversity theory as a shift towards a more democratic approach, which emphasizes the need to centre neurodivergent voices, is a thread that we will use throughout this chapter to help clarify how the various themes we cover interrelate. Towards the end of the chapter, we will shift from theory to research, to show how a more democratic approach might help change empirical knowledge production in line with the principles of the neurodiversity paradigm.

尽管我们涉及多个不同的主题，但贯穿始终我们想强调的是，在神经多样性运动中，我们看到理论和研究正朝着民主化的方向转变。这意味着，我们正从将知识及其相关实践视为由少数（通常是神经典型）专家构建的观点，转向更广泛地理解专业知识如何分散在我们神经多样化的群体中。我们认为这种向更民主化方向的转变，源于神经多样性范式的核心原则——肯定复杂性和政治化神经规范性，因为民主始终是应对政治问题复杂性的尝试。值得注意的是，残疾权利运动以及黑人解放斗争长期以来一直有一个口号：“没有我们的参与，就不要为我们做决定”。考虑到这一点，神经多样性理论作为一种向更民主化方法的转变，强调需要以神经殊异者的声音为中心，这一主线将贯穿本章，帮助我们阐明所涉及的各种主题如何相互关联。 在本章末尾，我们将从理论转向实证研究，以展示更具民主性的研究方法如何能帮助改变经验知识的生产方式，使其符合神经多样性范式的基本原则。

Models of disability

残障模型

Disability is the general term used for whenever someone has a body or mind that is considered impaired, and which is associated with struggling to fulfil the usual expectations of society. This includes expectations in school, the workplace, in day-to-day activities, and so on. Disabilities may in some cases also be associated with disease or illness, while in other cases someone can be disabled but healthy. They can also be permanent, temporary, or sporadic states. Legal definitions also differ in different contexts, and what is officially recognized as a disability thus slightly changes in different times and places.

残障是一个通用术语，指当一个人的身体或心智被认为存在缺陷，并且因此难以满足社会的常规期望时的情况。这包括在学校、工作场所、日常活动等方面的期望。在某些情况下，残障可能与疾病或病症相关，而在其他情况下，一个人可能身有残障但身体健康。残障状态也可能是永久性的、暂时性的或偶发性的。法律定义在不同情境下也有所不同，因此官方认定的残障范围在不同时间和地点会略有变化。

Beyond definitions, our understandings of and responses to disability can change dramatically depending on which model of disability we adopt. Disability models are a bit like different lenses that we can use to understand disability, each of which comes with different assumptions and commitments. This is relevant for neurodiversity theory since the neurodiversity paradigm challenges the dominant way of viewing neurological disabilities and suggests different ways of viewing them. Historically, moral or religious models of disability have often dominated. These saw disability as caused by supernatural forces: a disability might be viewed as a punishment from a god, or an opportunity for moral growth. But in the modern era we have shifted towards a more medical and scientific approach. This rejects the idea of disability as a moral issue and instead views it naturalistically, as a problem of the body or mind to be prevented or corrected through scientifically based medical intervention. We will explain this before going on to alternative models that we associate more with the neurodiversity movement.

除了定义之外，我们对残疾的理解和应对方式，会因所采用的残疾模型而发生巨大变化。残疾模型有点像我们理解残疾时可以使用的不同透镜，每一种都带有不同的假设和承诺。这与神经多样性理论相关，因为神经多样性范式挑战了看待神经残疾的主流方式，并提出了不同的视角。历史上，道德或宗教的残疾模型常常占据主导地位。这些模型将残疾归因于超自然力量：残疾可能被视为来自神灵的惩罚，或是道德成长的机会。但在现代，我们已转向更为医学和科学的方法。这种方法拒绝将残疾视为道德问题，而是以自然主义视角看待它，将其视为身体或心灵的问题，需要通过基于科学的医疗干预来预防或纠正。在继续讨论我们更多与神经多样性运动相关的替代模型之前，我们将先对此进行解释。

The basic idea of the medical model is that bodily or mental impairment or dysfunction is what causes illness or disability—you may recognize this as this model goes hand-in-hand with the normalcy paradigm we have already described, but has more direct implications for practice. Namely, that to respond to disability or illness appropriately means trying to prevent, treat, or cure underlying impairments or dysfunctions. Since the early 19th century at least, medical science and practice have been geared towards this, primarily through the use of genetic, physiological, or psychological intervention. As a result, autism or ADHD, bipolar disorder or schizophrenia have traditionally been seen as individual medical problems to be corrected by therapy or biomedical intervention.

医学模式的基本理念是，身体或精神上的损伤或功能障碍是导致疾病或残疾的原因——你可能已经意识到，这种模式与我们之前描述的常态范式紧密相连，但对实践有更直接的影响。也就是说，要恰当地应对残疾或疾病，就意味着要努力预防、治疗或治愈潜在的损伤或功能障碍。至少从 19 世纪初开始，医学科学与实践就一直致力于此，主要通过遗传、生理或心理干预来实现。因此，孤独谱系或注意力缺陷多动障碍、双相情感障碍或精神分裂症，传统上被视为需要通过治疗或生物医学干预来纠正的个人医学问题。

The medical model has been a significant improvement on the moral model in a range of ways. First, it avoids the stigma of viewing disability or illness as moral failure, and it also avoids pressuring disabled people (or their carers) to see their disability or illness as a chance for moral growth—a chance to be virtuous or inspirational while bearing great suffering. More importantly still, the medical model has often been hugely successful at preventing, treating, or curing a variety of illnesses or disabilities. Vaccines, antibiotics, and surgery, not to mention public health, sanitation, and so on, have radically reduced human suffering and increased the average lifespan considerably. All of this is in part the product of adopting and developing a medical model approach over the previous few centuries.

医学模式在一系列方面相较于道德模式有了显著进步。首先，它避免了将残疾或疾病视为道德缺陷的污名化，也避免了迫使残疾人（或其照顾者）将自己的残疾或疾病视为道德成长的机会——即在承受巨大痛苦的同时变得高尚或鼓舞人心的机会。更重要的是，医学模式在预防、治疗或治愈各种疾病或残疾方面往往取得了巨大成功。疫苗、抗生素和手术，更不用说公共卫生、环境卫生等，极大地减少了人类的痛苦，并显著提高了平均寿命。所有这一切，部分都是过去几个世纪采纳和发展医学模式方法的成果。

Despite the many benefits the medical model is associated with, it also has significant limitations and has brought its own harms. One issue is that the medical model tends to frame disability as an inherent tragedy, especially in cases where there is no effective treatment or cure. This can bring a kind of stigma of its own, leading disabled people to be viewed as inferior or as objects of pity. As a part of this, disabled people who achieve impressive things—including a degree of what is considered ‘normal’, such as having a job—are viewed as inspirational, something which disability advocates routinely reject. Relatedly, only focusing on deficits can also often lead to overlooking positives associated with many forms of neurodivergence. In the worst-case scenario, which is rather common, any difference between a neurodivergent and neurotypical person is immediately classified as a neurodivergent deficit. Finally, disabled people have argued that many of their key problems do not stem primarily from their impairments, but rather from societal exclusion, discrimination, and barriers. From their perspective, the medical model overlooks this, and thereby contributes to depoliticizing disablement.
