尽管医学模式带来了诸多益处，但它也存在显著局限并造成了自身的伤害。其中一个问题是，医学模式倾向于将残疾视为固有的悲剧，尤其是在没有有效治疗或治愈手段的情况下。这本身就会带来一种污名，导致残疾人被视为低人一等或怜悯的对象。作为这种观念的一部分，那些取得令人瞩目成就的残疾人——包括达到某种“正常”程度，比如拥有一份工作——会被视为励志榜样，而残疾倡导者通常对此持反对态度。与此相关的是，仅仅关注缺陷也常常导致忽视许多神经殊异形式所伴随的积极面。在最坏的情况下——这种情况相当普遍——神经殊异者与神经典型者之间的任何差异都会立即被归类为神经殊异者的缺陷。最后，残疾人指出，他们面临的许多核心问题主要并非源于自身的损伤，而是源于社会排斥、歧视和障碍。 从他们的视角来看，医疗模式忽视了这一点，从而助长了对残障问题的去政治化。

Because of the failures of the medical model, in the 1970s radical disability activists proposed what came to be called the social model of disability. This model is only about disability rather than illness, and it distinguishes between impairment (of the body or mind) and disablement. Based on this, instead of assuming that disability always stems directly from an impairment, it suggests a different story, whereby disablement is caused primarily by societal barriers. For instance, a wheelchair user with mobility impairments will be excluded from participation in society when access is via steps but not ramps, when dropped pavements are blocked by inconsiderate parking, when public toilets are not built to accommodate them, or when airlines lose or damage their wheelchair. This shifts the emphasis away from viewing disablement simply as an apolitical, individual problem to be fixed by medical intervention. Instead, disabled people are recast as an oppressed group, in need of rights, justice, and liberation no less than some are in need of access to medical treatment.

由于医疗模式的不足，20 世纪 70 年代，激进的残障活动家提出了后来被称为"残障社会模式"的理论。这一模式仅针对残障而非疾病，并区分了损伤（身体或精神上的）与残障。基于此，它不再假设残障总是直接源于损伤，而是提出了另一种解释：残障主要由社会障碍造成。例如，一位行动不便的轮椅使用者会在以下情境中被排斥在社会参与之外：当通道只有台阶而无坡道时，当无障碍人行道被随意停放的车辆堵塞时，当公共厕所未按无障碍标准建造时，或是当航空公司丢失或损坏其轮椅时。这将关注重点从将残障简单地视为一个非政治性的、需要通过医疗干预解决的个体问题转移开来。相反，残障人士被重新定义为受压迫的群体，他们需要权利、正义和解放，其迫切程度不亚于某些人需要获得医疗救治。

The understanding that disabled people are both oppressed and marginalized has permitted attention to be paid to the role of minority stress in the lives of disabled—and more specifically, neurodivergent—people. Minority stress describes the forms of stress particularly experienced as a result of being part of a minority group, in a given society. Minority stress arises in part from phenomena like discrimination and prejudice-driven aggression, but is also present in the absence of these, as a direct result of being ‘other than’ the majority. Recognizing the experience and effects of minority stress is a crucial part of working towards neurodivergent liberation and directly flows from the social model of disability which recasts disabled people as a societal minority.

认识到残疾人既受压迫又被边缘化，使得人们开始关注少数群体压力在残疾人——更具体地说，是神经殊异者——生活中的作用。少数群体压力描述的是在一个特定社会中，作为少数群体成员所特别经历的压力形式。这种压力部分源于歧视和偏见驱动的攻击等现象，但即便没有这些现象，仅仅因为“不同于”多数群体，压力也会存在。承认少数群体压力的经历和影响，是推动神经殊异者解放的关键部分，这直接源于将残疾人重新定义为社会少数群体的社会模式残疾观。

The original social model of disability (and its variants, since many theorists have since suggested various tweaks or additions to this basic conceptualization) has been a powerful tool for disabled people to fight for rights and justice in recent decades. This was also one of the key theoretical tools that neurodiversity proponents adopted from the 1990s onward. For instance, this allowed autistic people to begin seeing their sensory processing problems as stemming in large part from the neurotypical-biased design of schools, workplaces, and so on. Similarly, it allowed the insight that dyslexic people’s struggles in the classroom could be viewed as stemming in significant part from the neuronormative focus on writing and texts rather than speech and audio, or problems in timing on exams, and so on. Based on this, neurodiversity proponents have been able to successfully challenge the neuronormative ways much of the world is structured.

最初的残障社会模式（及其变体，因为许多理论家后来对这一基本概念提出了各种调整或补充）近几十年来一直是残障人士争取权利和正义的有力工具。这也是神经多样性倡导者自 20 世纪 90 年代以来采用的关键理论工具之一。例如，这使得孤独谱系群体开始认识到他们的感官处理问题在很大程度上源于学校和职场等环境中偏向神经典型性的设计。同样，它也带来了这样的洞见：阅读障碍者在课堂上的挣扎，可以很大程度上归因于神经规范性对书写和文本而非口语和音频的侧重，或是考试时间安排等问题。基于此，神经多样性倡导者得以成功挑战世界上许多领域构建的神经规范性方式。

The social model has also allowed a shift away from viewing disability as an individual tragedy. Some disabled people have even cultivated conceptions of disability pride, analogous to gay pride. Most relevantly, when it comes to neurodiversity, this includes notions of Autistic pride, Mad pride, and Weird pride. These indicate celebrations of Mad and Autistic culture, community, and solidarity. This has been extremely empowering for many neurodivergent people and has helped challenge overly negative perceptions of neurodivergence left over from the medical model.

社会模式也促成了从将残疾视为个人悲剧的视角转变。一些残障人士甚至培育了类似于同性恋骄傲的残疾骄傲概念。最相关的是，在神经多样性领域，这包括了孤独谱系骄傲、疯狂骄傲和怪异骄傲等概念。这些概念体现了对疯狂文化和孤独谱系文化、社群以及团结的庆祝。这对许多神经殊异者来说极具赋权意义，并有助于挑战医学模式遗留下来的对神经殊异性的过度负面看法。

It should be noted here that not all disabled people fully embrace the social model. Some suggest that it leads to overlooking the harmful effects of impairments, and some feel the medical model better fits with aspects of their experience. Because of this, some disability theorists have proposed relational models (or interactional models) that seek to provide a middle ground. Instead of committing to the idea that disability stems either from the impairment (within the person) or from society (outside the person), relational models view it as stemming from a complex interaction between individual bodyminds and the world. Moreover, the extent to which any given individual’s disability stems from one or the other will be different in different cases. These models thus seek to provide more space for a wider range of disabilities, drawing on the most beneficial aspects of both medicalized and social approaches. Other theorists have simply supplemented the social model with the concept of ‘impairment effects’, which can be acknowledged even while viewing disability as a more general political problem.

需要指出的是，并非所有残障人士都完全认同社会模式。有人认为这种模式会导致忽视损伤本身的有害影响，也有人认为医疗模式更符合他们的部分经历。正因如此，一些残障理论家提出了关系模型（或称互动模型），试图提供一种折中方案。关系模型不将残障归因于个体内在的损伤或外在的社会环境，而是将其视为个体身心与世界复杂互动的产物。此外，不同案例中个体残障的成因权重也各不相同。这些模型试图融合医疗化与社会化路径中最有益的部分，为更广泛的残障类型提供解释空间。另一些理论家则选择用"损伤效应"概念来补充社会模型——即使将残障视为更广泛的政治问题，仍可承认损伤效应的客观存在。

The neurodiversity movement has been influenced by both social and relational models, and either is compatible with the neurodiversity approach. While they do not deny the utility of a medical approach in many instances, by shifting the focus onto how society excludes and disables neurodivergent people, they have combated overly negative and pathologizing approaches to neurodivergent disablement and distress. Adopting and updating the insights of social and relational models of disability is thus a key part of neurodiversity theory.

神经多样性运动受到社会模式和关系模式的影响，两者都与神经多样性方法兼容。虽然它们并不否认医学方法在许多情况下的实用性，但通过将焦点转移到社会如何排斥和致残神经殊异人士，它们对抗了针对神经殊异障碍和痛苦的过度负面和病理化方法。因此，采纳并更新残疾的社会和关系模式的见解是神经多样性理论的关键部分。

Standpoint epistemology

立场认识论

A related shift that is at least implicit in much neurodiversity advocacy is a shift in epistemology. Epistemology refers to theories of knowledge, which are particularly relevant when it comes to understanding what might constitute expertise about neurodivergence. The medical model draws on a theory of knowledge that positions medical researchers, clinicians, and physicians as the experts. Their specialist training and access to scientific knowledge is considered to give them unique capacity when it comes not just to understanding disability, but also how to respond to it. These assumptions are reinforced by anxieties in biomedical sciences about ‘bias’ as a consequence of subjectivity. Much of biomedical research methodology is designed to recognize and eliminate sources of bias, most notably in systematic reviews and clinical trials. A number of international registration and reporting systems are now in place to enforce these anti-bias measures. In this context, the idea that an individual, or a group of people with some degree of shared lived experience, might have not just privileged insight but valuable expertise is hard for some to recognize.

神经多样性倡导中至少隐含着一个相关的转变，即认识论的转变。认识论指的是知识理论，这在理解什么可能构成关于神经殊异性的专业知识时尤为重要。医学模式基于一种知识理论，将医学研究者、临床医生和医师定位为专家。他们的专业训练和获取科学知识的途径被认为赋予了他们独特的能力，不仅在于理解残疾，还在于如何应对残疾。这些假设因生物医学科学中对“偏见”作为主观性后果的担忧而得到强化。生物医学研究方法论的大部分内容旨在识别和消除偏见来源，最显著的是在系统综述和临床试验中。目前已有许多国际注册和报告系统来执行这些反偏见措施。在这种背景下，个人或一群具有某种程度共同生活经验的人可能不仅拥有独特的洞察力，还拥有宝贵的专业知识，这一观点对一些人来说难以认同。

This is challenged, although not wholly rejected, by neurodiversity proponents. As we have just discussed, by shifting to a social model of disability, neurodiversity proponents also make the shift to viewing disabled people as forming an oppressed class, with more specific disabilities forming more specific classes. Looked at this way, it becomes possible to emphasize how disabled people may have special insight into their own positioning, and how this impacts their lives, that outsiders do not have. Thus, a doctor may have specific knowledge about, say, the scientific literature on a given disability, but a disabled person will have their own life experiences, and often also community knowledge, making them an expert too. This community knowledge becomes both more scientifically valuable and politically influential when it forms a collective cultural understanding. Sharing and combining experiences to extrapolate cultural norms for neurodivergent people, or for a specific group within that, helps to generate authoritative statements about ‘the ADHD experience’ that can shape practice while being resilient to the effects of individual agendas or bias.

神经多样性倡导者对此提出了挑战，尽管并未完全否定。正如我们刚刚讨论的，通过转向残疾的社会模式，神经多样性倡导者也将视角转向将残障人士视为一个受压迫的阶层，而更具体的残障则构成更具体的阶层。从这个角度看，我们可以强调残障人士如何可能对自己的处境及其对生活的影响拥有局外人所不具备的特殊洞察力。因此，医生可能拥有关于特定残障的科学文献的具体知识，但残障人士拥有自己的生活经历，通常还有社群知识，这也使他们成为专家。当这种社群知识形成一种集体文化理解时，它在科学上更具价值，在政治上更具影响力。分享和结合经验，为神经殊异人群或其中的特定群体推断文化规范，有助于形成关于“ADHD 体验”的权威论述，这些论述能够塑造实践，同时抵御个人议程或偏见的影响。

When we relate this back to affirming complexity and politicizing neuronormativity, this helps us see why we say that neurodiversity proponents can be seen as pushing for a more democratic approach. The shift to what some social theorists refer to as standpoint epistemology emphasizes that all knowledge comes from one specific standpoint or another, and moreover that members of oppressed classes often have insights into their oppression that will be missed from outside. As applied to neurodivergence, this does not deny that non-disabled doctors and researchers can contribute relevant expert knowledge, but it also emphasizes that in other ways they will often be ignorant. By the same token, disabled people also have their own expertise, but may be ignorant about various other things, such as the potential side effects of a given medication. Even for this superficially clear example, though, the doctor’s authority is not absolute. We know that medications can work differently for some neurodivergent people, and this might not be apparent from clinical trial data where neurodivergence is not taken into account. Thus, neurodivergent people may have situated knowledge from their community that doctors might lack. This will be different in every case, not least because disabled people and doctors are not mutually exclusive categories. Moreover, many disabled people may also be multiply marginalized, and will thus have access to experiences and knowledge that may be missed by disabled people who are not multiply marginalized. Given all of this, the neurodiversity paradigm shifts to a more democratic approach to knowledge production. That is, it emphasizes that our understandings must be developed collectively, and this goes for anything from theory to empirical research.

将这一点与肯定复杂性和政治化神经常态性联系起来，有助于我们理解为何可以说神经多样性的倡导者是在推动一种更为民主的路径。转向某些社会理论家所称的立场认识论，强调所有知识都源于特定的立场，而且受压迫阶层的成员往往对其所受压迫具有外部视角难以企及的洞见。应用于神经殊异性时，这并不否认非残障医生和研究人员能够贡献相关的专业知识，但也强调他们在其他方面往往存在认知盲区。同理，残障人士亦拥有自身的专长，但可能对其他诸多事物（如特定药物的潜在副作用）缺乏了解。然而，即便在这个表面清晰的例证中，医生的权威也非绝对。我们知道某些药物对部分神经殊异者可能产生不同反应，而这在未考虑神经殊异性的临床试验数据中或许并不明显。 因此，神经殊异者可能拥有其社群中医生所缺乏的情境性知识。这在每个案例中都会有所不同，尤其因为残疾人与医生并非互斥的类别。此外，许多残疾人可能还面临多重边缘化，因此他们能接触到那些未经历多重边缘化的残疾人所可能错过的经验和知识。考虑到所有这些因素，神经多样性范式转向了一种更为民主的知识生产方式。也就是说，它强调我们的理解必须通过集体协作来发展，这适用于从理论到实证研究的各个方面。

The concept of health and the normal mind

健康与正常心智的概念

An important issue raised by the neurodiversity movement and its challenge to the normalcy paradigm regards how we understand what it means to be healthy or ill. It should be emphasized that the concept of health, as well as related concepts such as disease, illness, pathology, and so on, are continually and constantly contested. There has never been a single, universally accepted definition of any of these, and understandings change in different cultures, times, and places. Still, it is notable that all cultures globally have at least some conception of mental and physical health. Ancient medical texts from Egypt, India, Greece, and China, for instance, all document conceptions of health that are applied to both body and mind.

神经多样性运动及其对常态范式的挑战，提出了一个重要问题，即我们如何理解健康与疾病的意义。必须强调的是，健康的概念，以及疾病、病症、病理学等相关概念，始终处于不断争议之中。这些概念从未有过单一、普遍接受的定义，其理解在不同文化、时代和地点中不断变化。然而，值得注意的是，全球所有文化都至少拥有某种关于心理和身体健康的概念。例如，来自埃及、印度、希腊和中国的古代医学文献，都记载了适用于身体和心灵的健康观念。

While concepts of health have changed over time, what is most important for neurodiversity theory is that health became more associated with normality in the 19th century in Europe. This was partly following the industrial revolution, which required bodies and minds to be standardized in relation to machines and products. It was also partly because modern statistical analysis was being developed, which allowed this standardization to be formalized through the use of data collection and analysis of mathematical averages and normal distributions.

尽管健康的概念随时间不断演变，但对神经多样性理论至关重要的是，19 世纪欧洲的健康观念日益与“正常性”挂钩。这一方面是工业革命的影响，它要求人的身体和心智能像机器和产品那样实现标准化；另一方面则源于现代统计分析方法的兴起，通过数据收集以及对数学平均值和正态分布的分析，这种标准化得以被正式确立。

While this has been helpful for the development of medical science in a number of ways, it has also arguably become harmful. The key issue with associating health with normality is that anyone who is atypical and struggling in any way is also seen as being disordered or having a pathology to be treated or cured. Sometimes this is helpful. In the case of epilepsy, for instance, most people with the condition want to be treated, and many would like to be cured if that ever becomes possible. But in other cases, it is harmful. Until the 1980s it was wrongly thought that homosexuality was a mental disorder. Because lots of queer people struggle with mental health problems and since queerness is atypical, psychiatrists came to believe that queerness itself was a disorder that should be treated medically. But this only harmed queer people, and now we recognize that high levels of mental health problems in queer populations are related to the stigma and discrimination queer people face.

尽管这在多方面促进了医学的发展，但可以说它也带来了危害。将健康与常态挂钩的关键问题在于，任何在某种程度上表现异常或面临困境的人，也会被视为患有需要治疗或治愈的疾病或病理状态。有时这确实有益。例如，对于癫痫患者，大多数患者希望得到治疗，如果可能的话，许多人甚至渴望被治愈。但在其他情况下，这种做法却是有害的。直到 20 世纪 80 年代，人们还错误地认为同性恋是一种精神障碍。由于许多性少数群体面临心理健康问题，且性少数身份本身被视为异常，精神病学家便认为性少数本身是一种需要医学治疗的障碍。但这只会伤害性少数群体，如今我们认识到，性少数群体中高发的心理健康问题与他们所面临的污名化和歧视有关。

This means that a big part of combating the normalcy paradigm regards the need to cleave the conceptual link between health and normality. At the moment, it is not totally clear what, if any, single conception of health the neurodiversity paradigm is committed to. After all, neurodiversity proponents do tend to retain some conception of mental or neurological illness (e.g. for epilepsy or dementia), even while contesting others. Reconceptualizing what it means to be healthy is a key task for neurodiversity theory, and more work will need to be done on this over the coming decades. At the same time, it should be noted that since nobody has proposed a perfect definition of health, the fact that neurodiversity proponents don’t have one is not a reason to dismiss the neurodiversity paradigm. It only means that neurodiversity proponents need to grapple with a problem that is equally a problem for everyone else.

这意味着，对抗正常性范式的一个重要方面在于切断健康与正常性之间的概念联系。目前尚不完全清楚神经多样性范式所秉持的（如果存在的话）单一健康概念究竟是什么。毕竟，神经多样性的支持者确实倾向于保留某些关于精神或神经系统疾病的概念（例如癫痫或痴呆），尽管同时也在质疑其他概念。重新构想健康的意义是神经多样性理论的一项关键任务，未来几十年需要在这方面进行更多工作。同时，应当指出，既然没有人提出过一个完美的健康定义，神经多样性支持者没有提出这样的定义，也不应成为否定神经多样性范式的理由。这只是意味着神经多样性支持者需要应对一个对所有人来说同样存在的问题。

For now, one way of thinking about the neurodiversity paradigm approach to theorizing health—and the boundaries between health and pathology—again might consist in democratizing how we approach this. At the moment, for instance, a great many autistic people contest that autism is non-pathological. By contrast, there is nothing like this collective position (yet) in relation to obsessive-compulsive disorder, indicating that most people with OCD see it as a pathological condition. In the neurodiversity movement the emphasis has most often been on allowing atypical people and groups to decide for themselves whether they consider their divergences pathological or not. This can be seen as the beginning of a more democratic approach to determining which forms of divergence are healthy or pathological, rather than our standards being enforced through an equivalence between health and normal functioning.

目前，思考神经多样性范式对健康理论化——以及健康与病理之间界限——的一种方式，或许在于将我们处理这一问题的方式民主化。例如，当下许多孤独谱系群体认为孤独谱系并非病理性状态。相比之下，对于强迫症则尚未形成类似的集体立场，这表明大多数强迫症患者视其为一种病理状态。在神经多样性运动中，重点通常在于允许非典型个体和群体自行决定他们是否认为自己的差异属于病理范畴。这可以视为一种更民主方法的开端，用于确定哪些形式的差异是健康的或病理性的，而不是通过将健康等同于正常功能来强制执行我们的标准。

Neurodiversity and diagnostic categories

神经多样性与诊断类别

Since the standard way to recognize disability is currently clinical diagnosis, it is vital to consider diagnosis in more detail. Moreover, understanding how the neurodiversity paradigm relates to diagnostic systems of classification is essential to the goals both of affirming complexity and politicizing neuronormativity. Our overarching position is that neurodiversity is fully aligned with a process of identification of disability, or divergence, but that this process should be maximally democratized and should serve the needs of the people who attract diagnosis, not just those who assess them. In the longer term, we suggest, a neurodiversity paradigm approach should work towards building a world where independent, formal clinical diagnosis is not always necessary for recognition of disability.

由于当前识别障碍的标准方式是临床诊断，因此有必要更详细地审视诊断过程。此外，理解神经多样性范式如何与诊断分类体系相关联，对于实现确认复杂性和政治化神经规范性的目标至关重要。我们的核心立场是，神经多样性完全符合识别障碍或差异的过程，但这一过程应最大限度地民主化，并服务于被诊断者的需求，而不仅仅是评估者的需求。长远来看，我们认为神经多样性范式方法应致力于构建一个无需依赖独立、正式的临床诊断即可识别障碍的世界。

The first thing to establish is that psychiatric diagnostic classification systems, namely the Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders (currently DSM-5) and the International Classification of Diseases (currently ICD-11), are created by humans to serve human purposes. The explicit rationale for psychiatric diagnoses is that this is necessary for people to access appropriate support or treatment, not to mention for other things such as health insurance and employment rights. They often do function in this way, for instance, accessing ADHD medications or psychotherapy. For many, diagnoses are also helpful for self-understanding and are preferable to more stigmatizing labels they might otherwise receive (‘lazy’, ‘naughty’, etc.). Many also find diagnoses useful for finding communities of other neurodivergent people who share their experiences.

首先需要明确的是，精神科诊断分类系统——即《精神障碍诊断与统计手册》（现行版本为 DSM-5）和《国际疾病分类》（现行版本为 ICD-11）——皆由人类为达成特定目的而创设。精神科诊断的显在理据在于，这是人们获取适当支持或治疗的必要途径，更遑论涉及医疗保险与就业权益等事项。这类系统确实常能发挥此类功能，例如帮助患者获得注意力缺陷多动障碍（ADHD）药物或心理治疗。对许多人而言，诊断亦有助于自我认知，且相较于可能被贴上的其他污名化标签（如“懒惰”“顽劣”等），诊断标签更具接纳性。许多人还发现，诊断有助于寻找拥有相似经历的神经殊异者社群。

At the same time, however, such classifications can also serve purposes of social control. As we have already highlighted, being gay or lesbian used to be pathologized as a mental disorder (and in some countries still is); women resisting patriarchy have been labelled as hysterical or as having disordered personalities; Black civil rights protesters were pathologized as having a ‘protest psychosis’. Still today, diagnosis can be used to deny support as much as to provide it, and moreover some diagnoses increase stigma. In such cases, the label is not serving the needs of the patient. As across all medicine, then, diagnosis can range from being life-saving to lethal depending on how it is used, and which societal functions it serves.

然而，与此同时，这类分类也可能服务于社会控制的目的。正如我们已经强调过的，同性恋者曾被视为精神障碍（在一些国家至今仍是如此）；反抗父权制的女性被贴上歇斯底里或人格障碍的标签；黑人公民权利抗议者被病理化为患有“抗议性精神病”。即使在今天，诊断既可以用于提供支持，也可以用于拒绝支持，而且某些诊断还会加剧污名化。在这些情况下，标签并未服务于患者的需求。因此，正如整个医学领域一样，诊断的作用范围可以从拯救生命到致命，这取决于其使用方式及其所服务的社会功能。

A deeper issue regards the relationship between the map and the territory, and to what extent diagnoses reflect discoveries or inventions. Many clinicians and researchers would like to believe that the diagnostic categories we have derived from observing human behaviour possess a degree of natural authority, or ground truth: that we are not inventing, but instead discovering classifications which are pre-existing. In some cases of neurodivergence, there seems a stronger case for this. The classification of Down syndrome, for instance, based on a single and specific genetic feature, seems closer to a discovery than other, much vaguer classifications with more shifting boundaries.

一个更深层次的问题涉及地图与领土之间的关系，以及诊断在多大程度上反映的是发现还是发明。许多临床医生和研究人员倾向于相信，我们从观察人类行为中得出的诊断类别具有某种程度的自然权威性或基本事实：我们不是在发明，而是在发现预先存在的分类。在某些神经殊异性的案例中，这种观点似乎更有说服力。例如，基于单一且特定遗传特征的唐氏综合征分类，相较于那些边界更为模糊、变动不定的其他分类，似乎更接近于一种发现。

However, viewing diagnoses as fixed or static—and using overly simple binaries between discovery and invention—goes against the neurodiversity paradigm commitments to affirming complexity and politicizing neuronormativity. For the most part, while the human race may be infinitely diverse, often this diversity does not fall into substantively different classes with clear space in between. Increasingly, transdiagnostic research is providing robust scientific support for this position. For example, in one analysis, authors identified 628 symptoms that make up all adult psychopathology described in the DSM-5. Of these, over one-third of the listed symptoms appear in more than one diagnostic classification. The most common number of repeats is for a symptom to appear in three separate diagnoses, but the range spans from 2 to 22 repeat appearances. In other words, in psychiatry, overlap is the norm rather than the exception when it comes to diagnostic classification. Similarly, in research examining neurodevelopmental diversity in children, a number of studies have found it is possible to cluster children, by shared genetics, shared neurological features, shared cognitive profiles, or shared diagnoses. But importantly none of these clustering systems maps across levels—children with the same diagnosis do not consistently share a cognitive, neurological, or genetic signature. Indeed, even Down syndrome has broad variation in terms of the community’s cognitive profiles, and how it is framed and represented is often a social as much as a natural matter.

然而，将诊断视为固定或静态——并在发现与发明之间使用过于简单的二分法——违背了神经多样性范式对确认复杂性和政治化神经元常性的承诺。很大程度上，尽管人类可能无限多样，但这种多样性往往并不会形成具有明确界限的实质性不同类别。越来越多的跨诊断研究为这一立场提供了有力的科学支持。例如，在一项分析中，作者们确定了构成 DSM-5 中描述的所有成人精神病理学的 628 种症状。在这些症状中，超过三分之一出现在不止一个诊断分类中。最常见的情况是同一症状出现在三种不同的诊断中，但重复出现的范围从 2 次到 22 次不等。换句话说，在精神病学中，诊断分类的重叠是常态而非例外。 同样，在考察儿童神经发育多样性的研究中，多项研究发现可以根据共享的遗传特征、共同的神经学特征、共同的认知特征或共同的诊断结果对儿童进行分组。但重要的是，这些分组系统之间并不存在一一对应的关系——具有相同诊断的儿童并不总具有一致的认知、神经或遗传特征。事实上，即使是唐氏综合症，在群体的认知特征方面也存在广泛差异，而如何界定和呈现这些差异，往往既是自然问题，也是社会问题。

If diagnoses often do not represent the formalized endpoint of a process of discovery of underlying truths, then what do they represent? One possibility is that, even when we put aside misuse of diagnoses to enforce patriarchal, heteronormative, or white supremacist ends, diagnostic classifications themselves often serve the purpose of enforcing neuronormativity and carve the world up into groups in order to control us. They may do this both by separating people into categories and by attempting to impose a degree of uniformity (or presumed uniformity) within a category. In this sense, current diagnosis systems, at least insofar as they present their classifications as representing discrete, natural dysfunctions, seem out of step with the neurodiversity paradigm.

如果诊断往往不代表对潜在真相的发现过程的正式终点，那么它们代表什么呢？一种可能性是，即使我们抛开滥用诊断来推行父权制、异性恋正统或白人至上主义目的的情况，诊断分类本身往往也服务于强化神经规范性的目的，并将世界划分为不同群体以便控制我们。它们可能通过将人们分门别类，并试图在类别内强加一定程度的统一性（或假定的统一性）来实现这一点。从这个意义上说，当前的诊断系统，至少在其将分类呈现为代表着离散的、自然的机能障碍的程度上，似乎与神经多样性范式格格不入。

As well as this fundamental mismatch, there are also practical ways in which the current diagnostic hegemony stands in the way of the long-term goals of the neurodiversity movement. In research, diagnostic classifications dominate when it comes to participant recruitment and to measurement of relevant characteristics or phenomena. Case-control methods in which highly selective criteria are applied, and measures chosen based on pre-existing understandings of what is interesting about a given population (in ADHD, executive functions; in autism, social cognition; in dyslexia, verbal IQ), can limit our capacity to capture rich insights into neurodivergent experiences and outcomes. These problems are exacerbated by the desire to find significant differences between groups, which are more achievable when those groups are narrowly defined—for example by excluding people who are multiply neurodivergent. These approaches create artificial clear space between diagnoses, exaggerating differences and obscuring shared features.

除了这种根本性的不匹配，当前诊断霸权还在实践层面阻碍着神经多样性运动的长期目标。在研究中，诊断分类主导着参与者招募及相关特征或现象的测量。采用高度选择性标准的病例对照方法，以及基于对特定群体（如 ADHD 的执行功能、孤独谱系的社交认知、阅读障碍的言语智商）既有认知选择测量指标的做法，可能会限制我们深入理解神经殊异体验与结果的能力。这些问题因追求发现组间显著差异而加剧——当群体被狭隘定义时（例如排除多重神经殊异者），这种差异更容易实现。这些方法在诊断间制造了人为的清晰界限，夸大了差异并掩盖了共同特征。

Another issue worth noting is that, in education and services, the absolute authority of clinical diagnosis frequently acts as a gatekeeper to support—as when children require a diagnosis before support in the classroom or during assessments will be considered. This has practical detriment, as people wait to be seen by clinical services before action is taken to alleviate difficulties. The problems can become severe when diagnostic services are overwhelmed, as at the time of writing in the UK, in the wake of the Covid-19 pandemic. Diagnostic gatekeeping drives inequality as well, in the light of known differentials in access to diagnosis based on social class, ethnicity, and gender.

另一个值得注意的问题是，在教育和服务领域，临床诊断的绝对权威常常成为获取支持的“守门人”——例如儿童在课堂或评估中需要获得诊断才能被考虑提供支持。这种做法具有实际危害，因为人们必须等待临床服务介入才能采取行动缓解困境。当诊断服务不堪重负时，问题会变得尤为严重，正如撰写本文时英国在新冠疫情后所面临的状况。诊断守门机制还会加剧不平等，因为众所周知，不同社会阶层、种族和性别群体在获得诊断的机会上存在显著差异。

This problem is not just practical, but also existential, as waiting for clinical diagnosis can limit people’s potential for self-actualization, via recognition of this element of their identity. By endorsing a diagnostic system governed by clinical professionals and their manuals, we devalue the knowledge of the person who perceives their own neurodivergence, instead focusing on external validation. What does it mean that neurodivergent people do not necessarily feel able to self-identify, that their insight into their own experience of the world is secondary to the judgement of an outsider? The reification of the authority of clinicians is so influential that even within neurodivergent communities the concept of self-identification (as autistic, dyspraxic, having ADHD) is frequently challenged, with people refusing to accept an individual into a community setting unless they have the authority of a clinical diagnosis.

这一问题不仅是实践性的，更是存在性的，因为等待临床诊断可能会限制人们通过认同自身这一身份要素来实现自我潜能的可能。通过支持由临床专业人员及其手册主导的诊断体系，我们贬低了那些感知到自身神经殊异性者的认知，转而强调外部验证。神经殊异者未必感到有能力自我认同，他们对自身世界体验的洞察竟次于外界的评判，这究竟意味着什么？临床医生权威的具体化影响如此深远，以至于即使在神经殊异社群内部，自我认同（如认同为孤独谱系、动作协调障碍者或 ADHD 患者）的概念也常遭质疑——人们往往拒绝接纳未经临床诊断权威背书的个体进入社群环境。

A final problem with our diagnosis system is the way that the concept of diagnosis is colloquially understood. Diagnosis happens most commonly in relation to disease and is normally followed by an effort at a cure. While many patients will seek a diagnosis in the presence of symptoms—meaning the condition was pre-existing—nonetheless the point of diagnosis often marks a transition from being understood as healthy to unhealthy, and the beginning of a process to return to the former state. Of course, seeking to treat a neurodivergent medical condition is sometimes helpful, as in the case of motor neurone disease. But in other cases, identifying neurodivergent disability should really be an experience of uncovering a lifelong way of being, rather than being viewed as a matter of detecting a pathology to be treated.

诊断体系的最后一个问题，在于"诊断"这个概念在通俗理解中的定位。诊断最常与疾病相关，通常随后伴随着治愈的努力。虽然许多患者在有症状时会寻求诊断——这意味着病症早已存在——但诊断的时刻往往标志着从被视为健康到不健康的转变，以及一个旨在恢复原状的过程的开始。当然，在某些情况下，如运动神经元疾病，寻求治疗神经殊异的医学状况是有益的。但在其他情况下，识别神经殊异的残疾实际上应是一种揭示终身存在方式的过程，而不应被视为发现需要治疗的病理问题。

Given all of this, do we call for the wholesale rejection of diagnosis as a system? We remain more ambivalent to diagnosis. One thing that neurodiversity proponents have done highly successfully is reclaim diagnoses, challenging how they are represented, understood, and studied. Many neurodivergent people identify as such, or simply as Mad, regardless of whether this has been certified by a doctor. Some neurodivergent people such as Merri Lisa Johnson have reclaimed diagnoses such as borderline personality. The reasoning here partly relies on the shift to standpoint epistemology and recognition of disabled people as forming marginalized groups in an oppressed class, as we have reviewed previously. Neurodivergent activists have also made their own classifications, such as ‘AuDHD’, which indicates an intersection between autism and ADHD. In line with politicizing neuronormativity, such classifications are then used as a basis for community, culture, and campaigning towards liberatory struggles. Thus while the neurodiversity paradigm seems at odds with much diagnostic practice in its current form, and certainly has room for alternatives to diagnosis, it is not clear that it requires abolition of diagnosis as such. Rather, it requires the abolition of diagnostic categories used in the service of domination and oppression.

考虑到这一切，我们是否呼吁全盘否定诊断体系？我们对诊断的态度更为矛盾。神经多样性倡导者取得的一项重大成功，是重新夺回了诊断的定义权，挑战了其表征方式、理解方式与研究方式。许多神经殊异者自我认同为神经殊异，或简单地自称为“疯人”，无论这是否得到医生的认证。一些神经殊异者，如梅里·丽莎·约翰逊，已重新认领了诸如边缘型人格障碍等诊断标签。这背后的逻辑部分依赖于我们之前讨论过的认识论转向——即转向立场认识论，并承认残疾人士构成了受压迫阶级中的边缘化群体。神经殊异活动家们也创建了自己的分类，例如“AuDHD”，用以表示孤独谱系与注意力缺陷多动障碍之间的交叉。与对神经规范性的政治化相一致，此类分类随后被用作建立社群、形成文化以及开展解放斗争运动的基础。 因此，虽然神经多样性范式似乎与当前许多诊断实践形式相悖，并且当然有替代诊断的空间，但尚不清楚它是否要求完全废除诊断本身。 相反，它要求废除那些服务于支配与压迫的诊断类别。

With all this in mind, the overarching move we suggest, which comes with a neurodiversity approach, follows the more general theme of democratizing theory and research. In clinical diagnostic services, this transition requires recognition of standpoint epistemology: that all knowledge production is constrained by the standpoint of the individual. This epistemological shift should require a clinically trained practitioner to recognize the biases and limitations of their perspective and respectfully integrate them with the perspective of the person seeking a diagnosis. More generally, a shift to democratization of diagnosis should reject the hierarchy of doctor/patient and start to facilitate accurate and helpful self-identification.

考虑到所有这些，我们建议的总体转变——遵循神经多样性方法——遵循了民主化理论和研究的更普遍主题。在临床诊断服务中，这种转变需要承认立场认识论：即所有知识生产都受到个体立场的制约。这种认识论转变应要求临床训练有素的从业者认识到自身视角的偏见和局限，并尊重地将其与寻求诊断者的视角相融合。更广泛地说，向诊断民主化的转变应摒弃医生/患者的等级制度，并开始促进准确且有益于个体的自我认同。

Crucially, this democratization should extend to the classification system itself. Currently, the way medical diagnostic categories are made is through consensus conferences and voting among taskforces primarily made up of psychiatrists and other doctors. This means that there is some level of democracy, but if so, it is a very partial democracy, analogous to early Greek conceptions of democracy whereby only property-owning males of noble birth were able to vote. By contrast, a neurodiversity paradigm approach indicates the need to radically democratize classificatory processes, placing the perspectives of disabled people more centrally than those of clinicians or researchers. This would allow categories and labels that form the diagnostic structures to serve the needs of neurodivergent people, rather than the needs of the medical industrial complex.

关键在于，这种民主化应当延伸至分类系统本身。目前，医学诊断类别的确立方式主要是通过由精神科医生和其他医生组成的专家小组召开共识会议并进行投票。这意味着存在一定程度的民主，但即便如此，这也是一种非常片面的民主，类似于早期希腊的民主观念——只有拥有财产的贵族男性才有投票权。相比之下，神经多样性范式方法指出，需要从根本上民主化分类过程，将残疾人的观点置于临床医生或研究人员之上。这将使构成诊断结构的类别和标签能够服务于神经殊异者的需求，而非医疗工业复合体的利益。

At first glance, this might seem unachievable, but there are many examples of shifts already taking place which are moving towards a more democratized diagnostic framework. One partial shift occurred when the major diagnostic manuals removed the restriction that ADHD could not be diagnosed in the presence of an existing autism diagnosis. This had meant it was literally impossible for a clinician to diagnose ADHD and autism in the same person, meaning that diagnoses served the system’s desire for clean categorical boundaries far more than the patient’s need to be understood and to understand themselves. Another shift took place in the diagnostic criteria for autism, when the requirement for symptoms to be present in early development was softened to include recognition that they ‘may not become fully manifest until social demands exceed limited capacities, or may be masked by learned strategies in later life’ in DSM-5. Notably, this change was driven by the Autistic Self-Advocacy Network, who lobbied the American Psychiatric Association while they were updating diagnostic categories, forcing the classification to reflect the needs of autistic communities rather than centring clinician standpoints. This change in the language of diagnostic manuals is now being extended even further in diagnostic practice, as individual clinicians shift their understanding of their role away from identifying clinical ‘impairment’ and towards identifying characteristic patterns of behaviour and experience—thus expanding access to diagnosis and uplifting the authority of the patient. Finally, there is the mass shift towards self-identification already noted. While clinical diagnosis is often vital, for instance for accessing prescriptions or ruling out underlying neurological problems, the general shift towards self-identification is indicative of the beginnings of a mass democratizing process in how our classifications are made and used.

乍看之下，这似乎难以实现，但已有许多转变正在发生，它们正朝着更民主化的诊断框架迈进。其中一个局部转变发生在主要诊断手册取消了"若已有孤独谱系诊断则不能诊断 ADHD"的限制。这意味着临床医生实际上不可能对同一个人同时诊断 ADHD 和孤独谱系，表明诊断更多地服务于系统对清晰分类界限的需求，而非患者被理解与理解自我的需要。另一个转变体现在孤独谱系的诊断标准中：DSM-5 将"症状必须在发育早期出现"的要求放宽为承认"症状可能直到社交需求超过有限能力时才完全显现，或在后续生活中被习得的策略所掩盖"。 值得注意的是，这一变革是由孤独谱系自我倡导网络推动的。该组织在美国精神病学协会更新诊断分类时积极游说，迫使诊断体系从以临床医生立场为中心，转向反映孤独谱系群体的实际需求。诊断手册语言的这种转变，如今正进一步延伸到诊断实践中——临床医生逐渐将自身角色从识别临床"缺陷"转向识别行为与体验的特征模式，从而拓宽了诊断的可及性，并提升了患者的主体性。最后，前文已提及的大规模自我认同转向同样至关重要。虽然临床诊断（例如获取处方或排除潜在神经系统问题时）往往不可或缺，但整体向自我认同的转向，标志着我们的分类体系在构建与运用层面，正开启一场大规模民主化进程的序幕。

Applications in scientific research

科学研究中的应用

Academic research provides the foundations for policy and practice within nations and globally, by generating conceptual models of understanding and providing a direct evidence base. Therefore, the goals of the neurodiversity movement—or the application of the neurodiversity paradigm—require a neurodiversity-affirmative research culture as well.

学术研究通过构建理解的概念模型并提供直接的证据基础，为国家乃至全球的政策与实践奠定基石。因此，神经多样性运动的目标——或者说神经多样性范式的应用——同样需要一种肯定神经多样性的研究文化。

As it stands, research across disciplines is rife with examples of academic enquiry that directly contravene the neurodiversity paradigm, and instead serve to promote ableism and stigma and entrench or pursue neuronormativity. The long association of autism with a lack of empathy (now refuted) has been used in arguments about the extent to which empathy is a requirement of being human, implicitly and sometimes explicitly calling into question the humanity of autistic people. In psychological sciences, when we look across studies comparing neurodivergent with neurotypical participants we see that opposing group differences (e.g. in one study neurotypical brains have fewer connections, in another the connections are more dense) are routinely interpreted as indicating a deficit in the neurodivergent group. In biomedical sciences, vast quantities of research funding and researcher time are invested in a quest for biomarkers that will reify diagnostic categories and could potentially be used as part of a prenatal screening programme—something which is already widespread for Down syndrome.

目前，跨学科研究中充斥着大量直接违背神经多样性范式的学术探究案例，这些研究反而助长了能力歧视和污名化，并巩固或追求神经规范性。长期以来，孤独谱系被与缺乏共情能力（现已被驳斥）联系在一起，这种观点被用于讨论共情作为人类属性的必要程度，有时甚至隐晦或明确地质疑孤独谱系群体的人性。在心理科学领域，当我们审视那些比较神经殊异与神经典型参与者的研究时，会发现相互矛盾的群体差异（例如，一项研究中神经典型大脑的连接较少，另一项研究中连接更密集）通常被解释为神经殊异群体存在缺陷。在生物医学领域，大量研究资金和研究人员时间被投入到寻找生物标志物的探索中，这些标志物将使诊断类别具体化，并可能被用于产前筛查项目——这在唐氏综合征的筛查中已经非常普遍。

How instead might we deliver a research programme, across disciplines, that could be considered neurodiversity affirmative? The first and primary component of such research is the involvement of neurodivergent people in leadership and decision-making roles. This remains vanishingly rare—even those fields where participatory methods are most established mostly deliver consultations, where neurodivergent input is constrained and channelled. A key way to improve this situation is to cultivate greater neurodivergent representation in academia, so that neurodivergent people are seeking funding, delivering projects, publishing papers, and shaping impact themselves.

那么，我们该如何开展一项跨学科的研究计划，使其能够被视作神经多样性肯定型研究呢？此类研究的首要且核心要素，是让神经殊异人士参与到领导与决策角色中。目前这种情况依然极为罕见——即便是在那些参与式方法最为成熟的领域，大多也只是进行咨询，神经殊异人士的贡献在其中受到限制和引导。改善这一状况的一个关键途径，是在学术界培养更多神经殊异人士的代表性，让神经殊异人士自己去争取资金、执行项目、发表论文并自行塑造影响力。

Even if we achieve greater inclusion for neurodivergent people in academia, this does not negate the need for participatory methods—such as co-production, citizen science, and community partnership—in research. Neurodivergent people who become academics will always represent a subset of this complex and heterogeneous community. Indeed, the process of becoming an academic, studying for a PhD, and pursuing a career in the higher education sector will shape neurodivergent academics in such a way that they will inevitably be set apart from a range of key neurodivergent experiences. Thus, neurodivergent academics are not exempt from the requirement to engage with the community and find ways to democratize their research process.

即便我们在学术界实现了对神经殊异人群更广泛的包容，这也不能否定研究中采用参与式方法——如共同生产、公民科学和社区合作——的必要性。成为学者的神经殊异人士，始终只是这个复杂且异质群体中的一个子集。事实上，成为学者、攻读博士学位、在高等教育领域追求职业发展的过程，会以某种方式塑造神经殊异学者，使他们不可避免地与一系列关键的神经殊异体验产生距离。因此，神经殊异学者同样不能免除与社群互动、并寻求方法使其研究过程民主化的要求。

One example of a neurodiversity affirmative research programme, manifest across multiple disciplines and research teams around the globe, is research into the double empathy problem. First described by Damian Milton, the double empathy problem provides a neat encapsulation of the experience of communication breakdown that can occur between two people of different neurological persuasions. The idea was developed particularly to describe the social experiences of autistic people, and to challenge the interpretation that any communication or interactive challenges experienced between autistic and non-autistic people should be attributed to an impairment within the autistic person. Instead, the double empathy problem highlights that responsibility for the success of an interaction sits with both people involved, and that two interacting people may both need to make an effort to overcome a mismatch in communication style.

全球多个学科和研究团队共同参与的神经多样性认可研究项目中，有一个典型案例是有关双向同理心问题的研究。这一概念由达米安·米尔顿首次提出，巧妙概括了两种不同神经特质的人在交流中可能出现的沟通障碍。该理念特别用于描述孤独谱系群体的社会体验，并挑战了一种固有观念——即孤独谱系与非孤独谱系人群之间的任何沟通或互动障碍都应归咎于孤独谱系个体的缺陷。相反，双向同理心问题强调：互动成功的责任应由双方共同承担，且两位互动者都可能需要付出努力来克服沟通方式的差异。

The double empathy problem has now given rise to a wealth of academic research, examining it from a theoretical, social science, experimental, and experiential perspective. Examples of this include seminal work demonstrating that non-autistic people make negative snap-judgements about autistic people, based on minimal information. Others have shown that the long-established difficulty that autistic people have (on average) judging the emotional facial expressions of others goes in both directions. Non-autistic people also struggle accurately to judge the emotional reactions of autistic people. Catherine Crompton captured the social experiences of autistic people in autistic and non-autistic company through interviews, systematically showing what many autistic people have long noted—that the company of other autistic people is comfortable and rewarding. In later experimental work she built on these findings, directly assessing how information was transferred between autistic, non-autistic, or mixed pairs of people. Her examinations of these interactions revealed that information transfer was more effective, and rapport was higher for matched pairs—both when rated by the participants themselves and by external observers.

双向同理心问题现已催生了大量学术研究，从理论、社会科学、实验和体验等角度对其进行探讨。例如，一些开创性研究表明，非孤独谱系群体在信息有限的情况下会对孤独谱系群体做出负面的仓促判断。其他研究则表明，孤独谱系群体（平均而言）在判断他人面部情绪表达方面长期存在的困难是双向的——非孤独谱系群体同样难以准确判断孤独谱系群体的情绪反应。凯瑟琳·克朗普顿通过访谈记录了孤独谱系群体在孤独谱系与非孤独谱系同伴中的社交体验，系统性地揭示了众多孤独谱系者长期以来的切身感受：与同类相处时更为舒适且收获良多。在后续的实验中，她基于这些发现进一步探索，直接评估了信息在孤独谱系、非孤独谱系或混合配对人群间的传递方式。 她对这类互动的分析显示，无论是参与者自我评价还是外部观察者评估，信息匹配的配对在信息传递效率上更高，且双方关系更为融洽。

Another example of research that affirms complexity, in a very literal sense, is the rise of transdiagnostic studies of development. This is a major departure from a long history of studies in which children are recruited to fit a set of narrow inclusion criteria. Not only selected for their diagnostic status—having ADHD, Tourette’s syndrome, or dyslexia—but also required not to have any secondary diagnoses, intellectual disability, physical disabilities, and so on. By including a carefully filtered selection of children, in pursuit of the maximum possible difference between included groups, these studies can only serve to showcase homogeneity within a group and clear space between groups, thereby reinforcing neuronormativity. In contrast, studies like the CALM cohort in Cambridge, UK, and the POND database in Montreal, Canada, are open to a diverse range of children and teenagers. They are producing insights about how children develop, learn, and thrive which have the potential to showcase and gain insights into neurodiversity—though such work is not automatically or fully neurodiversity affirmative.

另一个从字面意义上肯定复杂性的研究例子是发展性跨诊断研究的兴起。这标志着对长期以来研究范式的重大背离——过去的研究往往招募符合一系列狭窄纳入标准的儿童。这些儿童不仅根据其诊断状态（如患有 ADHD、图雷特综合征或阅读障碍）被筛选，还被要求不能有任何次要诊断、智力障碍、身体残疾等。通过纳入经过严格筛选的儿童样本，并追求组间差异最大化，这类研究只能展示组内同质性和组间清晰界限，从而强化了神经规范性。相比之下，像英国剑桥的 CALM 队列研究和加拿大蒙特利尔的 POND 数据库这类研究，则对多样化的儿童和青少年群体开放。它们正在产生关于儿童如何发展、学习和茁壮成长的见解，这些见解有潜力展示并深入理解神经多样性——尽管这类工作并非自动或完全属于神经多样性肯定性研究。

Applications in the arts and humanities

艺术与人文领域的应用

The influence of neurodiversity in academia is by no means limited to the sciences. A significant part of neurodiversity theory can be seen as part of the discipline of philosophy, and thus we might speak of there being a sub-field of philosophy of neurodiversity. This also has a lot of overlap with the component of disability studies often called disability theory. Much of what we have already covered regarding the basics of neurodiversity theory could be described as part of disability theory or philosophy of disability. This includes, most notably, analysis of the fundamental concepts and theoretical positions associated with the movement, which are more primarily conceptual than scientific matters.

神经多样性在学术界的影响绝非仅限于科学领域。神经多样性理论的很大一部分可被视为哲学学科的一部分，因此我们可以说存在一个神经多样性哲学的子领域。这与残障研究中常被称为残障理论的组成部分也有大量重叠。我们之前讨论的关于神经多样性理论基础的许多内容，都可以被描述为残障理论或残障哲学的一部分。这尤其包括对与该运动相关的基本概念和理论立场的分析，这些分析更主要是概念性的，而非科学性的问题。

But neurodiversity theory equally relates to a range of other disciplines in the arts and humanities. For a start, we could speak of critical neurodiversity theory, which is less about the metaphysical basis of the paradigm and is more about understanding neurodiversity in relation to society as a whole. The point of this is to theorize neurodivergent oppression in relation to broader systems of oppression and historical conditions, in order to think more clearly about what neurodivergent liberation might require.

但神经多样性理论同样关联到艺术与人文领域的一系列其他学科。首先，我们可以探讨批判性神经多样性理论，它较少关注该范式的形而上学基础，而更多关注于理解神经多样性在整体社会中的关联。其目的在于将神经殊异压迫置于更广泛的压迫体系与历史条件中进行理论化，从而更清晰地思考神经殊异解放可能需要什么。

Neurodiversity theory also has important implications for a range of other disciplines in the arts and humanities. Consider history. Most of our current historical work on things like Tourette’s syndrome or ADHD has been developed through a normalcy paradigm lens. Beginning with the assumptions of the normalcy paradigm will inevitably lead to certain interpretations of history which may be different from those developed through a neurodiversity paradigm lens. This may include anything from interpretations of Shakespeare to the history of capitalism. As such it is important to retell our histories through the neurodiversity paradigm, emphasizing how neuronormativity and the scientific research and clinical practice relating to this has always been political.

神经多样性理论对艺术和人文领域的其他学科也具有重要意义。以历史学为例。目前关于图雷特综合征或注意力缺陷多动障碍的大部分历史研究，都是通过正常性范式的视角展开的。从正常性范式的基本假设出发，必然会导致对历史的某些特定解读，而这些解读可能不同于从神经多样性范式视角得出的结论。这可能涵盖从对莎士比亚作品的诠释到资本主义历史的方方面面。因此，通过神经多样性范式重新叙述我们的历史至关重要，强调神经规范性以及与之相关的科学研究和临床实践如何始终具有政治性。

Similarly, neurodiversity theory may also inform disciplines that are engaged in cultural critique, such as literary studies, art history, theatre studies, and film and television studies. Until recently, engagement with neurodiversity in these fields tended to focus on questions of authenticity and the politics of representation: how do we decide what ‘good’ depictions of neurodivergence look like? Who gets to make this judgement? Should neurotypical persons be able to portray neurodivergent characters in film/theatre/television? Can neurotypical authors depict neurodivergence in literature in a non-pathologizing way? It is important that we ask these questions of contemporary media if we are to enact the tenets of the neurodiversity paradigm and its emphasis on self-definition and creating equitable relationships and understandings across neurotypes.

同样，神经多样性理论也可能为从事文化批判的学科提供启示，例如文学研究、艺术史、戏剧研究以及电影与电视研究。直到最近，这些领域对神经多样性的探讨往往聚焦于真实性与表征政治的问题：我们如何判断何为对神经殊异性的“良好”描绘？谁有权做出这一判断？神经典型人士是否可以在电影/戏剧/电视中扮演神经殊异角色？神经典型作家能否以非病理化的方式在文学中描绘神经殊异性？如果我们想要践行神经多样性范式的原则，强调自我定义以及在不同神经类型之间建立公平的关系与理解，那么对当代媒体提出这些问题至关重要。

However, when working with texts or other cultural products that were produced prior to our current understandings of neurodiversity (or of specific diagnoses), scholars caution against the tempting practice of fictional and/or historical diagnosis. The reason for this is that, even when the intention might be to find kinship with fictional characters, the practice of identifying certain characters as autistic, for example, replicates the practices of a culture that seeks to pathologize difference. Relatedly, when we are dealing with fictional constructs, we cannot assume that the established neurological normative of a given text reflects the understanding of its publication contexts. There must always be space to reflect upon the use of neurodivergence as a metaphorical device or as a carrier of cultural critique, rather than a straightforward representation of lived experience. Louise Creechan observes that ‘neurodivergence’ is an implicitly relational term that responds to the normative standard as established within a text which may or may not align with ‘real-world’ categorizations. By this schema, a neurodiversity framework might be applied to texts from any historical period or to the speculative or imaginative worlds of science fiction or fantasy. This form of analysis focuses, not on accuracy, but on the dynamics and tensions created by neurological variation within literary texts. Scholars working at the intersection of critical autism studies and literature have considered the interpretive potential of autistic readership and autistic poetics in literary texts, but these analyses have maintained the pathologizing parameters of autism diagnosis.

然而，在处理那些产生于我们当前对神经多样性（或特定诊断）理解之前的文本或其他文化产品时，学者们警告要避免那种诱人的做法——即对虚构和/或历史人物进行诊断。原因在于，即使意图可能是为了与虚构人物建立共鸣，例如将某些角色识别为孤独谱系的做法，实际上复制了一种试图将差异病理化的文化实践。与此相关的是，当我们处理虚构建构时，我们不能假定特定文本中确立的神经学规范反映了其出版背景下的理解。必须始终留有空间，来反思将神经殊异性用作隐喻手段或文化批判载体，而非对生活经验的直接再现。路易丝·克里尚指出，“神经殊异性”是一个隐含关系性的术语，它回应的是文本内部确立的规范标准，而这些标准可能与“现实世界”的分类一致，也可能不一致。 根据这一框架，神经多样性理论可应用于任何历史时期的文本，也可应用于科幻或奇幻文学中那些虚构或想象的世界。这种分析形式关注的不是准确性，而是文学文本中神经多样性所产生的动态关系与张力。 在批判性自闭症研究与文学交叉领域工作的学者们，虽然探讨了自闭症读者视角及自闭症诗学在文学文本中的诠释潜力，但这些分析仍延续了自闭症诊断中的病理化框架。

As the neurodiversity paradigm advocates for valuing and engaging with the natural diversity of minds, it is perhaps unsurprising that neurodiversity scholarship in the arts and humanities is often deeply invested in questions of form. Neurodivergent artists and activists have sought to redefine the traditions of live performance to accommodate variations in bodyminds, as explored by the contributors to Awkwoods and in Jess Thom’s (aka Touretteshero) tourettic, relaxed performances of Samuel Beckett’s Not I. Similarly, neurodivergent scholars and artists have advocated for forms of scholarship that capitalize upon the inclusive potentialities of mixed media, such as zines and collage. Through embracing and valuing a variety of mediums, atypical bodyminds can forge their access to scholarship in their own terms.

神经多样性范式倡导珍视并参与心智的天然多样性，因此，艺术与人文领域的神经多样性研究常常深度关注形式问题，这或许并不令人意外。神经殊异的艺术家和活动家们试图重新定义现场表演的传统，以适应身心状态的多样性，正如《Awkwoods》的撰稿人所探讨的，以及杰斯·汤姆（又名 Touretteshero）对塞缪尔·贝克特《不是我》的图雷特式、宽松式表演所展现的那样。同样，神经殊异的学者和艺术家们也倡导利用混合媒体（如独立杂志和拼贴艺术）包容性潜力的学术形式。通过拥抱并珍视多样的媒介，非典型身心可以以自己的方式开辟通往学术的道路。

Neurodiversity theory thus has great relevance for a range of humanities fields, and an important part of the paradigm shift will require developing new knowledges within these fields to help reposition neurodivergent people in the past and today. This also relates to the wider attempt at a cultural paradigm, which relates to but goes far beyond academic research, and can be seen in myriad forms of neurodivergent art and literature that are being produced by neurodivergent artists.

因此，神经多样性理论与一系列人文学科领域高度相关，而范式转变的一个重要部分将需要在这些领域内发展新的知识，以帮助重新定位过去和当今神经殊异人群的地位。这也与更广泛的文化范式尝试相关，这种尝试虽与学术研究有关，但远超出学术研究的范畴，并体现在神经殊异艺术家创作出的无数形式的神经殊异艺术和文学作品中。

A general orientation of this effort, and a key way to live up to the principles of affirming complexity and politicizing neuronormativity, is a mass push towards democratizing research, all the way from how we construct our categories to the way we design studies, the questions we ask, and so forth. By democratizing we mean moving away from primarily centring the efforts of a few experts, and instead developing knowledge through and with neurodiverse populations in ways that situate the needs of neurodivergent people over the needs of research. The ultimate point of this is to redirect our theory and research towards changing the world in ways that will be good for neurodivergent people everywhere.

这一努力的一个总体方向，以及践行肯定复杂性原则和政治化神经规范性的关键途径，是大力推动研究民主化——从我们如何构建分类，到我们设计研究的方式、提出的问题等等。所谓民主化，我们指的是不再主要围绕少数专家的努力，而是通过与神经多元人群合作并以其为主导的方式发展知识，将神经殊异人群的需求置于研究需求之上。这样做的最终目的是将我们的理论和研究导向改变世界，使其有益于世界各地的神经殊异人群。



---

Chapter 3 Applications of the neurodiversity paradigm

Chapter 3 Applications of the neurodiversity paradigm

第三章 神经多样性范式的应用

In this chapter we will move on from theory to practice, discussing applications of the neurodiversity approach in education, the workplace, the criminal justice system, and health and social care. To be clear, this is by no means meant to be exhaustive, but these are some of the key areas where developing a neurodiversity paradigm approach has the most potential for impact. These themes also allow us to take a lifespan approach, since our lives typically begin by entering the education system, we then typically move on to or are shut out of the workplace—and, in some cases, may encounter the criminal justice system—and finally, we all need health and social care, and many of us end up in nursing homes. As such, though there is no standard trajectory for any single life, these themes allow us to uncover some issues that neurodivergent people might directly or indirectly encounter.

在本章中，我们将从理论转向实践，探讨神经多样性方法在教育、职场、刑事司法体系以及健康与社会照护领域的应用。需要明确的是，这绝非一份详尽的清单，但这些领域确实是发展神经多样性范式方法最具影响力的关键领域。这些主题也让我们能够采取生命历程的视角——人生通常始于进入教育体系，继而步入或被迫远离职场（在某些情况下还可能遭遇刑事司法体系），最终我们都需要健康与社会照护，许多人会在养老院度过晚年。因此，尽管每个人的生命轨迹并无标准模式，但这些主题能帮助我们揭示神经殊异人群可能直接或间接面临的若干问题。

Before beginning this section, it is important to recognize that the systems and tools used to build current practices, evaluate them, and improve them are themselves potentially neuronormative. As we have mentioned, academic research which supports national and local policy change and also shapes the decisions of individuals (e.g. a headteacher deciding how to spend their pupil support budget in a given year; a clinical service lead making induction materials for new staff) is not an accessible space for many neurodivergent people. Growing numbers of neurodivergent academics describe the challenges and costs of their chosen career, while others only survive by keeping their neurodivergence carefully hidden. At a deeper level, the very tools with which knowledge is constructed are grounded in neuronormative expectations about the nature of evidence and indicators of rigour—as in the title of Audre Lorde’s seminal work The Master’s Tools Will Never Dismantle the Master’s House. In that context, we call for a degree of epistemic disobedience—willingness to challenge the orthodoxy at all levels—when it comes to developing new understandings to support radical shifts in practice across society.

在开始本节之前，必须认识到，用于建立、评估和改进当前实践的那些体系和工具本身，很可能就是神经常态化的。正如我们已提及的，学术研究——它支撑着国家和地方政策的变革，也影响着个人的决策（例如，一位校长决定在特定年份如何分配学生支持预算；一位临床服务负责人为新员工制作入职材料）——对许多神经殊异者而言，并非一个可及的空间。越来越多的神经殊异学者描述了他们所选职业的挑战与代价，而另一些人则只能通过小心翼翼地隐藏自己的神经殊异性来生存。在更深层次上，构建知识所用的工具本身就根植于关于证据本质和严谨性指标的神经常态化期望——正如奥德丽·洛德在其开创性著作《主人的工具永远不会拆毁主人的房子》的标题中所揭示的那样。 在此背景下，我们呼吁在形成新认知以推动全社会实践的根本性转变时，需要一定程度的认知不服从——即愿意在各个层面挑战正统观念。

Being neurodivergent in school

校园中的神经殊异者

The modern, inclusive school system, of the kind laid down in UNESCO and UNICEF guidelines, is where many neurodivergent people first encounter regular discrimination and exclusion. This means that we must change education if we want to shift to a broader neurodiversity paradigm. In this section we will cover the basics of the current system to show some more general issues as well as what it might mean to shift to a neurodiversity-affirmative approach.

依照联合国教科文组织和联合国儿童基金会指导方针建立的现代融合教育体系，往往是许多神经殊异者首次遭遇系统性歧视与排斥的场所。这意味着，若想转向更广泛的神经多样性范式，我们必须变革教育体系。本节将剖析现行体系的基本架构，既揭示其普遍性问题，也探讨转向神经多样性肯定式教育可能带来的深刻意义。

An inclusive education system means that efforts are made to provide a single school setting which caters to a diverse range of young people. However, inclusion is rarely complete. First, those pupils with the most significant learning disabilities, making traditional learning methods and targets inappropriate for them, are usually educated separately in ‘special schools’—though the terminology varies. Second, many mainstream schools which accommodate neurotypical and neurodivergent children will also have an attached ‘learning support base’ or similar. This is intended to give neurodivergent young people the chance to move flexibly between mainstream classrooms and a more tailored learning environment, catering to so-called ‘spikey profiles’ of ability and variations in capacity depending on other factors. Such bases may also be used by children with English as an additional language, or those who have experienced significant trauma. Third, exclusion of neurodivergent pupils from mainstream school is common. Young people may be formally excluded, but even more common are hidden exclusions, which we will describe in more detail below. Finally, anxiety-related school non-attendance and home-schooling is prevalent in families of a neurodivergent child, meaning many have opted out of the state school system, finding it unfit for their needs.

一个包容性的教育体系意味着努力提供一种单一的学校环境，以满足各种年轻人的需求。然而，包容性很少是全面的。首先，那些学习障碍最为严重、传统学习方法与目标不适用于他们的学生，通常会在“特殊学校”中接受单独教育——尽管术语有所不同。其次，许多接纳神经典型和神经殊异儿童的主流学校也会附设“学习支持基地”或类似机构。这旨在让神经殊异的年轻人有机会灵活地在主流教室和更量身定制的学习环境之间切换，以适应所谓的能力“尖峰分布”以及因其他因素导致的能力变化。这些基地也可能被英语作为附加语言的孩子或经历过重大创伤的孩子使用。第三，将神经殊异学生排除在主流学校之外的情况很常见。年轻人可能会被正式排除，但更常见的是隐性排除，我们将在下文中更详细地描述。 最后，与焦虑相关的逃学和家庭教育在神经殊异儿童家庭中十分普遍，这意味着许多人已选择退出公立学校体系，认为其无法满足他们的需求。

Debates about the application of the neurodiversity paradigm in schools must first recognize two things. First, that the goal of inclusive education—well established as a principle worldwide—is inclusion. Specifically, by this we mean that the success of an inclusive education system rests on how well it has managed to include diverse learners. This is distinct from attainment goals, which are often the focus in the classroom, against which some learners will always fail. Attainment goals matter for capitalist societies, where a key purpose of education is preparing young people to enter the job market. Modern education systems typically include mandatory schooling up to a certain point and then optional further education beyond that. Since the 19th century, much learning and assessment in modern school systems has become increasingly standardized. This is supposed to be fair, allowing everyone to be trained and tested in the same way as everyone else. This is why we tend to have standard tests, a standardized curriculum, and so on, used across nations of many millions of people. However, these rigid systems serve a set of capitalist workforce demands (at least for the subset of pupils who meet expectations), but not the goal of inclusion.

关于神经多样性范式在学校应用的讨论，首先必须认识到两点。其一，融合教育的目标——作为一项全球公认的原则——在于实现融合。具体而言，这意味着融合教育体系的成功与否，取决于其能否有效接纳多元化的学习者。这与以学业成就为目标的教育取向截然不同，后者常成为课堂关注的焦点，却注定会让部分学习者受挫。学业成就目标在资本主义社会至关重要，因为教育的一个关键目的是为年轻人进入就业市场做准备。现代教育体系通常包含一定年限的义务教育，之后则是可选择的继续教育。自 19 世纪以来，现代学校体系中的大部分教学与评估已日益标准化。这被认为体现了公平性，让每个人都能以相同的方式接受培训和测试。正因如此，我们倾向于采用标准化考试、统一课程等模式，并将其应用于数千万人口的国家教育体系之中。 然而，这些僵化的体系服务于一套资本主义劳动力需求（至少对于符合期望的那部分学生而言），却与包容性目标背道而驰。

The second acknowledgement is that traditionally a key purpose of a country’s education system is to socialize children to the norms and expectations of their cultural context and especially of the workplace. Children learn about rules, hierarchy, and peer relationships as much as they learn spelling, fractions, and history. This is important because it reminds us that an inclusive education system does not just consider access to formal learning, but also access and affirmation in a system of socialization.

第二个需要承认的是，传统上国家教育体系的一个关键目的是将儿童社会化，使其适应文化背景尤其是职场环境的规范与期望。儿童在学习拼写、分数和历史的同时，也在学习规则、等级制度和同伴关系。这一点很重要，因为它提醒我们：包容性教育体系不仅要考虑正式学习机会的获取，还要关注社会化体系中的参与度与身份认同。

Schools currently fail neurodivergent children across the board. A key issue is that standardized schooling excludes the ways many people function or process information. This means people with statistically rare skills or talents go unrecognized or may fail on tests designed for an imaginary typical student. This is often particularly hard for multiply marginalized neurodivergent people. For instance, a migrant student learning in a second language may diverge both neurologically and culturally from the imagined typical student, making it harder for them to gain access to both education and socialization processes throughout school. Another key issue is that learning and socialization may be especially hard given that schools are often chaotic, loud, and busy places. While this is challenging for nearly everyone, it can be highly detrimental to the processing styles of many neurodivergent people. Finally, schools may also often have rules and norms that are particularly harmful for neurodivergent people. For instance, having to sit still for long periods may be detrimental to the learning of students who fit with the ADHD diagnosis, or expectations in physical education classes may exclude some students with impaired bodily coordination, as is associated with a dyspraxia (or developmental coordination disorder) diagnosis.

当前学校在各个方面都未能满足神经殊异儿童的需求。一个关键问题在于，标准化教育排除了许多人运作或处理信息的方式。这意味着，那些在统计上罕见的技能或天赋往往得不到认可，或者可能在为想象中的典型学生设计的测试中失败。对于多重边缘化的神经殊异者来说，这一点往往尤其困难。例如，一名以第二语言学习的移民学生，可能在神经和文化上都与想象中的典型学生存在差异，这使得他们在整个学校教育过程中更难获得教育和社会化机会。另一个关键问题是，鉴于学校通常是混乱、嘈杂和繁忙的场所，学习和社交可能变得特别困难。虽然这对几乎所有人来说都是一种挑战，但它可能对许多神经殊异者的信息处理方式极为不利。最后，学校通常还可能存在一些对神经殊异者特别有害的规则和规范。 例如，要求长时间静坐可能不利于符合多动症诊断标准学生的学习，体育课上的要求也可能排除一些身体协调能力受损的学生，这与运动障碍（或发展性协调障碍）的诊断相关。

All this means school is often a deeply traumatizing place for many neurodivergent people, especially those who are from working-class and minority ethnic backgrounds. Currently, neurodivergent children and young people are more likely to be excluded from school and have higher rates of non-attendance. They are also subject to unknown rates of ‘hidden exclusions’, such as parents being asked to collect their child before the end of the school day, pupils being excluded on external inspection dates, and pupils spending much of the day in isolation. When they do attend, they have lower participation in class and are more likely to be bullied and victimized. Some families may resort to seeking a placement for their child in a special school. For some neurodivergent people, where the mainstream learning environment is entirely inaccessible, special school placements are helpful and appropriate, but for many it is inadequate. Disabled learners should not have to seek out a placement which presumes less ability, simply in order to be accepted socially and accommodated behaviourally. In practice, desperate families seeking special education placements results in a form of segregation, where people with the same learning potential are divided up into a two-tier education system that perpetuates oppression more than reducing it.

这意味着学校对许多神经殊异者来说，往往是一个造成深刻创伤的地方，尤其是那些来自工人阶级和少数族裔背景的人。目前，神经殊异的儿童和青少年更有可能被学校排斥，并且有更高的缺勤率。他们还面临着未知比例的“隐性排斥”，例如家长被要求在放学前提早接走孩子、学生在外部检查日期被排除在外，以及学生大部分时间被隔离。即使他们到校，课堂参与度也较低，并且更有可能遭受欺凌和伤害。一些家庭可能会尝试为孩子寻求特殊学校的安置。对于一些神经殊异者来说，当主流学习环境完全无法适应时，特殊学校的安置是有帮助且合适的，但对许多人而言，这并不足够。残疾学习者不应仅仅为了获得社会接纳和行为上的便利，而被迫寻求一个预设其能力较低的安置方式。 在实践中，急于寻求特殊教育安置的家庭往往导致某种形式的隔离，将具有相同学习潜力的人群分割为两级教育体系，这种体系非但未能缓解压迫，反而使其长期存在。

These educational inequalities ripple out, contributing to poorer reported quality of life for neurodivergent youth and their families and driving high rates of teacher burnout and dropout from the profession. The effects are long term as well, with many neurodivergent young people following the school-to-prison pipeline and struggling to access higher or further education and employment. As so often in this text, comprehensive figures are just not known, with evidence coming from a patchwork of studies normally limited to examining one diagnostic group or another.

这些教育不平等现象产生连锁反应，导致神经殊异青少年及其家庭报告的生活质量下降，并造成教师职业倦怠和离职率居高不下。其影响同样具有长期性，许多神经殊异年轻人沿着"校园到监狱"的轨迹发展，难以获得高等教育或继续教育机会，就业也面临重重阻碍。正如本书中反复出现的情况，我们缺乏全面数据，现有证据仅来自零散的研究，且通常局限于考察某一特定诊断群体。

Neurodiversity-affirmative education

神经多样性肯定式教育

A different approach to education emphasizes inclusion. This indicates a commitment to changing how classrooms and education more broadly are organized so that they work for everyone, not just those who sit closer to the imagined standard student. Beyond being inclusive, education can also be emancipatory. In his influential book Pedagogy of the Oppressed, the Brazilian educator Paulo Freire emphasized that while socialization is often helpful, preparing students to conform to an unjust society just reproduces injustice. Instead, Freire suggested what he called a ‘dialogical’ approach where students and teachers generate shared understandings and knowledge together. This could include knowledge about how students themselves have been oppressed. This kind of education would not just prepare students to adjust to society as it is, but also to actively participate in challenging the more oppressive tendencies around them.

另一种教育方法强调包容性。这意味着致力于改变课堂乃至整个教育体系的组织方式，使其适用于所有人，而非仅仅迎合想象中的标准学生。除了包容性之外，教育还应具有解放性。巴西教育家保罗·弗莱雷在其影响深远的著作《被压迫者教育学》中强调，虽然社会化通常有益，但让学生适应不公正的社会只会延续不公。相反，弗莱雷提出了一种他称之为“对话式”的方法，即学生和教师共同构建共享的理解和知识。这可能包括关于学生自身如何被压迫的知识。这种教育不仅让学生适应现有社会，还鼓励他们积极参与挑战周围的压迫性倾向。

Neurodiversity-affirmative education systems should be a way to correct these distressing patterns by instead turning to inclusive and emancipatory approaches. Importantly, neurodiversity-affirmative education would help to realize the goals of inclusion by making adjustments not only to formal learning and attainment aspects of education, but also to the socialization agenda in schools. Neurodiversity-informed education should affirm complexity, by expecting and catering to heterogeneity in the student body (and staff) as a matter of course. A shift to talking of needs that are met or unmet could be a useful signal here—moving away from the concept that neurodivergent pupils’ needs are ‘special’ or ‘additional’. Goals should be set based on individual flourishing rather than being centred on normative behaviour. Schools should also politicize neuronormativity, by recognizing the social forces that dictate neurodivergent experiences, including stereotypes, stigma, discrimination, and prejudice, and work to actively fight these. In doing so, they can draw on the strength that comes from diversity by involving diverse teams in developing and delivering policy and practice.

倡导神经多样性的教育体系应当通过采用包容性和解放性的方法，来纠正这些令人不安的模式。重要的是，倡导神经多样性的教育不仅会对教育的正式学习与成绩方面进行调整，还会对学校的社会化议程进行调整，从而有助于实现包容的目标。 基于神经多样性的教育应当肯定复杂性，理所当然地预期并满足学生群体（及教职员工）的异质性。在此背景下，将讨论重点转向“需求是否得到满足”，而非“需求是否特殊”，可能是一个有用的信号——这有助于摆脱“神经多样性学生的需求是‘特殊’或‘额外’的”这一观念。 目标设定应以个体发展为导向，而非以规范行为为中心。学校还应将“神经规范性”纳入政治议程，即认清那些左右神经多样性群体经历的社会力量——包括刻板印象、污名、歧视和偏见——并积极予以对抗。在此过程中，学校可通过让多元化的团队参与政策与实践的制定与实施，从而汲取多样性带来的力量。

Full realization of these principles could drive a pivot towards education as a mechanism of liberation, by educating marginalized people to develop the potential to change society themselves. This is deep inclusion, centring the needs of the excluded and prioritizing the battle against inequality. It requires fundamental and radical change. However, sticking within existing curriculum frameworks, we can still implement neurodiversity-affirmative practices.

充分实现这些原则，可以推动教育转向成为解放的机制，通过教育边缘化人群，培养他们自己改变社会的潜力。这是深层次的包容，以被排斥者的需求为中心，并将对抗不平等置于优先地位。这需要根本性和彻底的变革。然而，在现有的课程框架内，我们仍然可以实施肯定神经多样性的实践。

Implementation of these principles might include a programme of actively teaching children the insight and self-advocacy skills needed to judge their own behavioural and learning needs and request support as needed. Resources such as a classroom visual timetable, or the option to wear noise-cancelling headphones, should be available to all and not doled out selectively to those with a doctor-provided permission slip (in the form of a diagnosis). Relaxing rules is also vital. For instance, students should not be forced to sit still for long periods and should be able to freely use toilet facilities whenever they need to. Teachers should seize every opportunity to celebrate diversity: for example, noting and cherishing the range of approaches taken to writing and illustrating a poem about autumn, rather than selecting the ‘best’ poems. Applying the principles of the neurodiversity paradigm in our schools (and lifelong learning institutions) should help us realize the goals of inclusion by making neurodivergent learners feel accepted and welcome in class. This goal is a prerequisite for both well-being and educational attainment to follow.

实施这些原则可能包括开展一项计划，积极教导儿童掌握洞察力和自我倡导技能，以判断自身的行为和学习需求，并在必要时寻求支持。诸如教室视觉时间表或佩戴降噪耳机的选项等资源，应向所有人开放，而非仅选择性提供给那些持有医生开具的许可单（以诊断形式）的学生。放宽规则同样至关重要。例如，不应强迫学生长时间静坐，而应允许他们在需要时自由使用洗手间设施。教师应抓住每一个机会来颂扬多样性：例如，关注并珍视创作一首关于秋天的诗歌时所采用的各种不同方法，而不是挑选出“最佳”诗作。在我们的学校（以及终身教育机构）中应用神经多样性范式的原则，应有助于通过让神经殊异的学习者在课堂上感到被接纳和受欢迎，从而实现包容性目标。这一目标是后续福祉和教育成就的先决条件。

Finally, helping all students build a general awareness of neuronormative oppression is also vital for emancipatory education. As we have indicated, all too often, key problems neurodivergent people face throughout their lives begin in education before being transported to the workplace and other aspects of adult life. This means that education is also a key place where neurotypical people begin to learn to see themselves as superior to neurodivergent people, and neurodivergent children begin to internalize feelings of inferiority. Collectively building an awareness and understanding of such issues in the classroom, through a dialogical approach building knowledge between teacher and students, is most likely a vital step towards overcoming this. After all, the world of tomorrow will be made by the students of today, and this includes both neurotypical and neurodivergent students.

最后，帮助所有学生建立对神经规范压迫的普遍认识，对于解放性教育也至关重要。正如我们指出的那样，神经殊异者一生中面临的关键问题，往往始于教育阶段，然后被带入职场和成人生活的其他方面。这意味着，教育也是神经典型者开始学会将自己视为优于神经殊异者，以及神经殊异儿童开始内化自卑感的关键场所。通过师生之间以对话方式构建知识的教学法，在课堂上共同建立对此类问题的认识和理解，很可能是克服这一问题的关键一步。毕竟，明天的世界将由今天的学生创造，这既包括神经典型学生，也包括神经殊异学生。

Applications in the workplace

在工作场所的应用

It is always challenging to estimate what proportion of the world is neurodivergent, but we can be clear that for any given neurodivergent group, unemployment rates are higher than in the general population. Sample statistics include full- or part-time employment rates of just 34 per cent for adults with ADHD and 15 per cent for people with a learning disability. Meanwhile, reporting on the National Longitudinal Transition Study 2 in the USA, autistic employment is described as follows: ‘While the rate increased steadily for individuals on the spectrum from 15 to 63%, it was always lower than the average rate for all disability groups, which increased from 54 to 91%.’

要估算全球神经殊异人群的比例总是充满挑战，但我们可以明确的是，对于任何特定的神经殊异群体，其失业率都高于普通人群。样本统计数据显示，患有注意力缺陷多动障碍的成年人全职或兼职就业率仅为 34%，而有学习障碍的人群就业率仅为 15%。与此同时，根据美国国家纵向过渡研究 2 的报告，孤独谱系人群的就业情况描述如下：“虽然谱系个体的就业率从 15%稳步上升至 63%，但始终低于所有残疾群体的平均就业率，后者的就业率从 54%上升至 91%。”

Most of us leave full-time education at some point in our youth, and the general expectation is that decades of paid employment will follow. While, as we describe below, the assumption that paid employment is the only or best way to spend your adult life needs to be challenged, neurodivergent people should certainly have the same right and opportunity to succeed in work as anyone else. Paid employment brings a number of benefits—social connection, daily routine, a chance to use your skills and be rewarded for that. Some would argue, following Marx, that fulfilling one’s creative potential is part of what it means, fundamentally, to be human—just as a beaver builds dams, we work to create new things, use them, and share them. More practically, perhaps the biggest reason to ensure equal access to work is that being paid wages is a huge part of having self-determination and autonomy.

我们大多数人都在青年时期的某个阶段结束全日制教育，随之而来的普遍期望是数十年的有偿就业。尽管正如下文将要阐述的，那种认为有偿就业是度过成年生活的唯一或最佳方式的假设需要受到质疑，但神经殊异人群无疑应当拥有与其他人同等的权利和机会在工作中取得成功。有偿就业带来诸多益处——社会联系、日常规律、运用技能并因此获得回报的机会。一些人会追随马克思的观点认为，实现个人创造潜能是人之为人的根本意义所在——正如河狸筑坝，我们通过工作创造新事物、使用并分享它们。更实际地说，确保工作机会平等或许最重要的原因在于，获得工资报酬是实现自我决定和自主权的核心组成部分。

However, modern workplaces rarely acknowledge, let alone accommodate, neurodivergence—resulting in the low rates of employment already mentioned. Recruitment processes often exclude neurodivergent people in all kinds of ways; for example, some personality tests used in recruitment are remarkably similar to those used for diagnoses such as bipolar disorder, and while it would be illegal to directly discriminate on these grounds, the tests used in recruitment can act as a proxy for discriminating against people with various diagnoses. For those neurodivergent people who do find work, a large majority of workplaces have become enforcers of neuronormativity, by the scientific management of workers and their efficiency. In factories, call centres, and offices, in Starbucks, McDonald’s, and Aldi, workers must do more with less. Even in the UK’s largest employer, the National Health Service, many elements of patient care are allotted by time quota rather than being permitted whatever resource is needed for a careful clinical decision. Productivity is key, and this is anathema to a neurodivergence-informed system that allows for cognitive diversity. It is no wonder then that anyone for whom reading takes a little more time, or whose working memory relies on a chance to recheck instructions, will find modern workplaces inhospitable at best.

然而，现代职场很少承认神经殊异性，更不用说为其提供便利了——这导致了前文提到的低就业率。招聘流程往往以各种方式将神经殊异人群排除在外；例如，招聘中使用的某些性格测试与用于诊断双相情感障碍等疾病的测试惊人地相似，虽然基于这些理由直接歧视是违法的，但招聘中使用的测试可以充当歧视各种诊断人群的代理工具。对于那些确实找到工作的神经殊异者来说，绝大多数职场通过科学管理员工及其效率，已成为神经规范性的强制执行者。在工厂、呼叫中心和办公室，在星巴克、麦当劳和阿尔迪，员工必须用更少的资源做更多的事。即使在英国最大的雇主——国家医疗服务体系中，患者护理的许多环节也是按时间配额分配的，而不是允许为仔细的临床决策提供所需的任何资源。生产力是关键，而这与一个允许认知多样性的、了解神经殊异性的体系是格格不入的。 那么，对于任何需要更多时间阅读、或工作记忆依赖于重新核对指令机会的人来说，现代职场环境充其量也只能说是令人不适的。

There are ways to apply the principles of the neurodiversity paradigm in the workplace, however. The concept of reasonable adjustments goes a long way towards affirming complexity, by placing a legal responsibility on employers to provide for the unique needs of their individual employees. If correctly implemented, this system should allow an employee to ask for support or resources to enable them to do their job. For someone with chronic back pain, this could be a specialized chair or standing desk, and for a neurodivergent person it might be speech-to-text software or a solo office.

然而，仍有方法可以在职场中应用神经多样性范式的原则。合理调整的概念通过将满足员工独特需求的法律责任赋予雇主，极大地肯定了复杂性。如果正确实施，这一制度应允许员工请求支持或资源，以便他们能够完成工作。对于患有慢性背痛的人，这可能是一把专用椅子或站立式办公桌；对于神经殊异者，则可能是语音转文字软件或独立办公室。

Unfortunately, in reality, there is a wealth of reporting from neurodivergent and otherwise disabled people that the reasonable adjustments system is rarely applied as intended in law—or rather, fails to achieve the desired goal of inclusion. One factor that might particularly apply to neurodivergent people is a lack of clarity on what adjustments might be available and helpful for them. This is something that is frequently reported anecdotally and is not surprising given the relative invisibility of neurodivergent people in workplaces until very recently. Many neurodivergent people are not ‘out’ at work—and those who are often report experiencing a negative shift in how they are treated by colleagues when they first reveal their diagnosis.

遗憾的是，现实中存在大量来自神经殊异及其他残障人士的报道，表明合理调整系统很少能如法律所设想的那样得到应用——或者说，未能实现包容的预期目标。一个可能尤其适用于神经殊异人士的因素是，对于哪些调整措施对他们来说是可获得且有益的，缺乏清晰的认识。这在轶事报告中经常被提及，考虑到直到最近神经殊异人士在工作场所的相对隐形性，这并不令人意外。许多神经殊异人士在工作中并未“出柜”——而那些选择公开的人士常常报告说，当他们首次透露自己的诊断时，同事对待他们的方式会发生负面的转变。

Even when the concept of reasonable adjustments is well applied, it is limited in its capacity to conform to the neurodiversity paradigm. One issue is regarding what counts as ‘reasonable’—often this judgement is made by a neurotypical person or, at the very least, is set against neurotypical norms. Universal design offers an alternative route to politicize neuronormativity at work, by rejecting the concept of adjustment—additional or different provision, against an implicit norm—and replacing it with the idea of a profoundly inclusive workplace. Universal design is not easy, and starts with fundamentals like city planning and architecture, but workplaces can make immediate steps towards it by implementing any given adjustment in as widespread a manner as possible, such as changing workplace dress codes to emphasize comfort over externally applied expectations of what is ‘professional’. This is a good example of where intersectional disadvantage is also apparent—it is well known to be easier for someone who is part of a class with social power (e.g. a cisgender white man) to dress down while still being considered professional and authoritative, while someone else (e.g. a Black woman who uses a wheelchair) may be judged more harshly if she doesn’t dress ‘smartly’. As such, some neurodivergent people more than others will be under greater pressure to conform to narrow workplace expectations in terms of dress, hairstyle, social niceties, and so on. A universal adjustment at the national policy level which is gaining attention at the time of writing is Universal Basic Income—perhaps the single most democratizing step that a country could take towards inclusion.

即使合理调整的概念得到良好应用，其在适应神经多样性范式方面的能力仍然有限。一个关键问题在于如何界定“合理”——这一判断往往由神经典型人士做出，或至少以神经典型规范为基准。通用设计提供了一条替代路径，通过摒弃“调整”概念——即针对隐性规范进行额外或不同的安排——并以构建深度包容的工作场所理念取而代之，从而将工作中的神经规范性政治化。通用设计并非易事，它始于城市规划与建筑等基础层面，但工作场所可以通过尽可能广泛地实施任何既定调整来立即迈出步伐，例如改变着装规范，强调舒适性而非外部强加的“专业”期待。 这是一个体现交叉性劣势的绝佳例子——众所周知，属于拥有社会权力的阶层（例如顺性别白人男性）的人，即使穿着随意，也更容易被视为专业且权威；而其他人（例如使用轮椅的黑人女性）如果穿着不够“得体”，则可能受到更严厉的评判。因此，一些神经殊异者会比其他人承受更大的压力，需要在着装、发型、社交礼节等方面迎合狭隘的职场期望。在国家政策层面，一项获得广泛关注的普遍性调整是全民基本收入——这或许是一个国家在迈向包容之路上所能采取的最具民主化意义的举措。

Affirming complexity when it comes to employment and adult life has consequences both within a given workplace and more broadly. Another aspect of working life that serves to exclude or disadvantage neurodivergent people is the social expectations that accompany many jobs. These range from the emotional labour required of those working in the service industry to expectations around things like small talk in break spaces, after-work drinks, and colleagues’ birthdays. These not only serve to exclude many neurodivergent people, but also have negative consequences for cultural diversity at work. A more specific instance of this is found in evidence that autistic people may be particularly likely to be whistle-blowers at work, detecting and reporting deviations from policy and procedure, including corruption. While this is objectively a positive contribution to the employer and industry, whistle-blowing may not be received well by colleagues and can result in autistic people being ostracized.

在就业和成人生活方面承认复杂性，不仅对特定工作场所产生影响，其影响范围更为广泛。工作生活中另一个导致神经殊异群体被排斥或处于不利地位的因素，是伴随许多职位而来的社会期望。这些期望涵盖从服务业从业者所需的情感劳动，到休息区闲聊、下班后饮酒聚会以及同事生日庆祝等场合的行为规范。这些不仅排斥了许多神经殊异者，也对职场文化多样性产生了负面影响。一个更具体的例证是：有证据表明，孤独谱系群体在工作中尤其可能成为举报者，他们善于发现并报告偏离政策程序的行为，包括腐败现象。虽然这对雇主和行业客观上具有积极贡献，但举报行为可能不被同事接纳，并导致孤独谱系群体遭受排挤。

More broadly for society, affirming complexity involves recognizing how narrow our view of ‘employment’ often is—another factor which makes it hard to reliably estimate underemployment among neurodivergent people. Routinely we focus on full-time paid salaried work, and many surveys of employment fail to capture the other ways in which people may be employed in a more general sense. These include unpaid caring roles and work in the home, freelance work and self-employment, ‘underground’ employment such as sex work, supported employment and social enterprise, income generation through things like renting a spare room, and other kinds of gig economy working across multiple part-time jobs. Neurodivergent people may be especially drawn to these forms of employment for their increased flexibility and room for self-determination—or they may find themselves working this way due to circumstance. For example, neurodivergent adults are more likely to have neurodivergent children, some of whom may need care beyond their early years. We should resist neuronormative expectations about what constitutes a good employment outcome and work to capture all these pathways in our efforts to democratize access to fulfilling employment for neurodivergent people. A key way of organizing this will be through neurodivergent people making explicit efforts to unionize as neurodivergents, to make demands from that specific positionality.
