从更广泛的社会层面来看，肯定复杂性意味着要认识到我们对“就业”的看法往往多么狭隘——这也是导致难以可靠估计神经殊异人群就业不足的另一个因素。我们通常只关注全职带薪工作，许多就业调查未能涵盖人们在更广泛意义上可能从事的其他工作形式。这些包括无薪照护角色和家务劳动、自由职业和自雇工作、“地下”就业（如性工作）、支持性就业和社会企业、通过出租闲置房间等方式创收，以及跨多个兼职工作的零工经济形式。神经殊异人群可能特别被这些就业形式所吸引，因为它们提供了更大的灵活性和自主空间——或者他们可能因环境所迫而选择这种方式工作。例如，神经殊异的成年人更有可能养育神经殊异的孩子，其中一些孩子可能在幼儿期之后仍需要照护。 我们应当抵制关于何为良好就业结果的神经典型性期望，并努力在我们的工作中囊括所有这些途径，以实现神经殊异人群获得充实就业机会的民主化。组织这一工作的关键方式，将是神经殊异人群明确努力组建神经殊异者工会，从这一特定立场出发提出诉求。

Neurodiversity in the criminal justice system

刑事司法系统中的神经多样性

As we noted earlier, among neurodivergent populations we often see a school-to-prison pipeline. This is similar to the levels seen among working-class Black populations, who are incarcerated in much greater numbers than those who are white and middle class. On the normalcy paradigm, the implicit assumption is that people with certain conditions or disabilities are inherently more likely to commit crime. For instance, if people with any given diagnosis are seen as deficient in empathy, or disposed to being highly impulsive, they will also be considered naturally disposed towards acting in ways that are harmful to others, more so than those who are more neurotypical. This gives the impression that there is something natural about more neurodivergent people being in prison.

正如我们之前提到的，在神经殊异人群中，我们常常观察到从学校到监狱的输送管道。这与工人阶级黑人群体中的情况类似，他们被监禁的比例远高于白人和中产阶级群体。在常态范式下，隐含的假设是，患有某些疾病或残障的人天生就更有可能犯罪。例如，如果被诊断为某种疾病的人被视为缺乏同理心，或倾向于高度冲动，那么与神经典型性更强的人相比，他们也会被认为天生更容易做出伤害他人的行为。这给人一种印象，即更多神经殊异者入狱是自然而然的事情。

Understanding the relationship between neurodivergence and the criminal justice system from a neurodiversity paradigm approach requires challenging all of this. Politicizing neuronormativity raises questions about what should count as crime in the first place. Affirming complexity requires asking whether having prisons and police are good ways to control our neurologically diverse populations.

从神经多样性范式的角度理解神经殊异性与刑事司法系统的关系，需要挑战所有这些观念。将神经规范性政治化，首先就提出了什么应被视为犯罪的问题。肯定复杂性则需要追问，设立监狱和警察是否是控制我们神经多样性群体的有效方式。

Considering first the rates of neurodivergent people incarcerated: one study looking at a prison in Chelmsford found that over half the inmates had either dyslexia or a related learning difficulty, with similar levels found in a Texan prison. This is striking given that only around 10 per cent of the general population is dyslexic. Similarly, around one in four prisoners are reported to have ADHD, despite prevalence at only around 5 per cent of the population. High numbers are also associated with other forms of neurodivergence, from autism to schizophrenia. Thus, this seems to be a systemic issue that cuts across neurodivergent populations.

首先考虑神经殊异人群的监禁率：一项针对切姆斯福德监狱的研究发现，超过半数的囚犯患有阅读障碍或相关学习障碍，德克萨斯州监狱的数据也与此相近。这一数据令人震惊，因为普通人群中阅读障碍者的比例仅约 10%。同样，据报道约四分之一的囚犯患有注意力缺陷多动障碍，而该障碍在总人口中的患病率仅约 5%。从孤独谱系到精神分裂症等其他形式的神经殊异性也呈现高关联性。由此可见，这似乎是横跨神经殊异人群的系统性问题。

As we just noted, it has often been assumed that neurodivergent people are simply more disposed to commit crime. The neurodiversity paradigm perspective rejects this. When we say ‘school-to-prison pipeline’, we are already emphasizing how neurodivergent people ending up in prison stems less from individual cognitive traits and more from systemic problems that begin in school. As we have seen, neurodivergent people are routinely excluded from receiving adequate education right from their earliest years. This impacts their life chances in endless ways, including prospects for paid employment. In turn, even for those neurodivergent people who do end up in employment, as we have seen, they also face further forms of discrimination and exclusion there. All this pushes at least some neurodivergent people towards criminalized professions, such as drug dealing, sex work, and so forth.

正如我们刚刚指出的，人们常常认为神经殊异者只是更容易犯罪。神经多样性范式视角否定了这一点。当我们谈论"从学校到监狱的管道"时，我们强调的是神经殊异者最终入狱的原因，与其说是个人认知特质所致，不如说是始于学校的系统性问题的结果。正如我们所看到的，神经殊异者从幼年起就常常被排除在获得充分教育之外。这以无数种方式影响了他们的生活机会，包括获得有偿就业的前景。反过来，即使对于那些最终得以就业的神经殊异者，正如我们所见，他们在工作中也面临着进一步的歧视和排斥。所有这些都将至少一部分神经殊异者推向了犯罪化的职业，例如贩毒、性工作等等。

Sometimes the way neurodivergent people comport themselves or act is seen as suspicious by members of the public and police alike. Autistic people often avoid eye contact due to sensory processing issues, but this may wrongly be viewed as a sign of dishonesty. People who hear voices and talk to themselves may be unfairly targeted due to stigmatizing representations of voice hearers and associations of ‘madness’ with violence. Such factors mean that in neuronormative societies, neurodivergent people are more prone to attracting police attention, despite the fact that neurodivergent people are more likely to be victims rather than perpetrators of violence. Neurodivergents are also more likely to be mistreated by the police than neurotypical people. A recent UK report found that three-quarters of those who completed suicide following police contact were neurodivergent, for instance with diagnoses of bipolar disorder or borderline personality disorder. A 2016 report from the USA indicated that the levels of mental disability among those killed by the police are up to 50 per cent. It further found that their having a mental disability was sometimes used to blame victims for being killed.

有时，神经殊异者的行为举止会被公众和警方视为可疑。孤独谱系群体常因感觉处理问题而避免眼神接触，但这可能被错误地视为不诚实的表现。那些听到声音并自言自语的人，可能因为对幻听者的污名化描绘以及将"疯狂"与暴力相关联，而受到不公正的针对。这些因素意味着，在神经常态社会中，神经殊异者更容易引起警方注意，尽管事实上神经殊异者更可能是暴力的受害者而非施暴者。与神经典型人群相比，神经殊异者也更可能受到警方的不当对待。英国近期一份报告发现，在与警方接触后自杀的人中，有四分之三是神经殊异者，例如被诊断为双相情感障碍或边缘型人格障碍。美国 2016 年的一份报告指出，被警察杀害者中，精神残疾的比例高达 50%。 该报告进一步发现，他们的精神残疾有时被用来指责受害者，认为其被杀是咎由自取。

The policing and incarceration of neurodivergent people is particularly intense for those who are Black, Asian, working class, female, or nonbinary—or many of those identities. People who sit at any of these intersections are often at much greater risk. For instance, a Black autistic person experiencing sensory overload in a public space may wrongly be seen as being a threat, by both members of the public and police. Female, trans, and nonbinary neurodivergent people working in criminalized professions such as sex work (and we have already seen how this employment pathway may be more common for neurodivergent people) may also be doubly at risk of police violence, including sexual violence.

对于黑人、亚裔、工人阶级、女性或非二元性别——或兼具多重此类身份的神经殊异者而言，警务执法与监禁的强度尤为严酷。身处这些交叉身份中的个体往往面临更大的风险。例如，一位在公共场合经历感官过载的黑人孤独谱系人士，可能被公众和警察错误地视为威胁。从事性工作等被刑事化的职业的女性、跨性别及非二元性别神经殊异者（我们已经看到这一就业途径在神经殊异群体中可能更为普遍），也可能面临包括性暴力在内的警察暴力的双重风险。

Finally, what even counts as a crime in the first place is a social rather than natural issue. Sometimes immoral things are legal while things that are not inherently problematic are criminalized. Slavery used to be legal, but clearly it should not have been. At the same time, it is far from clear that sex work should be criminalized, as this not only turns sex workers into criminals, but also makes it harder for them to access workers’ rights. Once again, it is notable here that a great many neurodivergent people are either pushed towards or choose to go into sex work, and are thus at greater risk of criminalization than many neurotypicals.

首先，究竟什么才算是犯罪，这本身就是一个社会问题而非自然问题。有时不道德的行为是合法的，而本质上并无问题的事情却被定为犯罪。奴隶制曾经是合法的，但显然它本不该如此。与此同时，性工作是否应该被定为犯罪远非明确，因为这不仅将性工作者变成了罪犯，还使他们更难获得工人权利。值得注意的是，许多神经殊异者要么被迫从事性工作，要么选择进入这一行业，因此他们比许多神经典型者面临更大的被定罪风险。

Politicizing neuronormativity and affirming complexity requires recognizing that our criminal justice systems often function, in significant part, to control and incarcerate neurodivergent people who have been failed by other systems: notably employment and education. This is especially true for those who are multiply marginalized. To be clear, this is not a statement about the intentions of individual police officers, but rather about the facts of the criminal justice system as a whole. Recognizing this requires asking hard questions about whether our policing and prison systems are capable of reform or should be abolished. It may be that there are alternative ways of organizing our justice systems that would be better not just for neurodivergent people, but for everyone. Going forward, efforts should be made to centre neurodivergent perspectives in attempts to conceptualize or build these alternatives.

将神经元规范性政治化并肯定其复杂性，需要认识到我们的刑事司法体系在很大程度上往往是为了控制和监禁那些被其他体系——尤其是就业和教育体系——所辜负的神经殊异者。对于那些遭受多重边缘化的人来说，情况尤其如此。需要明确的是，这并不是针对个别警察的意图，而是关于整个刑事司法体系的事实。认识到这一点，就需要提出一些棘手的问题：我们的警务和监狱体系是否能够改革，还是应该被废除。或许存在组织我们司法体系的其他方式，这些方式不仅对神经殊异者更好，而且对所有人都有益。展望未来，在尝试构思或建立这些替代方案时，应努力将神经殊异者的视角置于中心位置。

Applications in health and social care

在健康与社会照护领域的应用

Health and social care is another area in which the inequalities based in neurodiversity are both highly visible and severely consequential. Neurodivergent people require healthcare like all of us—for routine health issues, chronic conditions, at key life stages such as puberty, becoming a parent, or at the end of life, and for reasons closely connected to being neurodivergent. For example, lots of neurodivergent people will encounter healthcare providers in the context of seeking a diagnosis. Some forms of neurodivergence, like intellectual disability or autism, are associated with higher rates of health conditions such as hypermobility disorders and epilepsy—and of course the latter is itself a form of neurodivergence. Those with the highest support needs may rely on social care services across the lifespan, while others encounter them only in old age. Finally, largely due to the challenges of being neurodivergent in a society that values neuronormativity, neurodivergent people experience very high rates of mental ill-health. It is therefore imperative that health and social care systems are neurodiversity informed.

健康与社会照护是另一个基于神经多样性的不平等现象既高度可见又后果严重的领域。神经殊异者与我们所有人一样需要医疗保健——无论是为了常规健康问题、慢性疾病，在青春期、成为父母或生命终结等关键人生阶段，还是出于与神经殊异性密切相关的缘由。例如，许多神经殊异者会在寻求诊断的过程中接触医疗服务提供者。某些形式的神经殊异性，如智力障碍或孤独谱系，与较高的健康问题发生率相关，例如关节过度活动症和癫痫——当然，后者本身也是一种神经殊异性形式。那些需要最高程度支持的人可能终生依赖社会照护服务，而其他人则仅在老年时才接触这些服务。最后，主要由于在一个重视神经规范性的社会中作为神经殊异者所面临的挑战，神经殊异者心理健康问题的发生率非常高。因此，医疗保健和社会照护系统必须了解神经多样性。

There is abundant evidence that healthcare is currently failing neurodivergent people. Stark insights come from studies on mortality, which have shown dramatically reduced life expectancy for autistic people. Recent analysis reveals that white people with a learning disability in the UK die on average at 62 years old, 18 years earlier than the general life expectancy for the UK population. Even more shocking is the fact that people with a learning disability who are from minority ethnicities are dying on average at 34 years old.

大量证据表明，当前的医疗体系未能满足神经殊异群体的需求。关于死亡率的研究揭示了严峻的现实，数据显示孤独谱系群体的预期寿命显著缩短。近期分析表明，英国患有学习障碍的白人平均死亡年龄为 62 岁，比英国人口总体预期寿命早 18 年。更令人震惊的是，来自少数族裔的学习障碍患者平均死亡年龄仅为 34 岁。

The causes of early mortality in neurodivergent people can be broadly assigned to three domains, though on the current state of the evidence it is impossible to precisely quantify their contributions. First, neurodivergent people face serious barriers to routine and acute healthcare. The precise details vary depending on the patient and their health needs, but common issues include: clinician/systemic failure to comprehend the impact of neurodiversity on symptom experiences and reporting; inaccessible modes of communication (such as telephone-only appointment booking); lack of processing time in clinical questioning and lack of familiarization time for new procedures; and failure to adapt for sensory needs. All of these phenomena make seeking help in the event of a concern, and attending routine screening appointments, a significant challenge for neurodivergent people.

神经殊异人群的早逝原因大致可归为三个领域，尽管根据现有证据尚无法精确量化其各自的影响。首先，神经殊异人群在常规和紧急医疗保健方面面临严重障碍。具体细节因患者及其健康需求而异，但常见问题包括：临床医生/系统未能理解神经多样性对症状体验和报告的影响；沟通方式不便（如仅限电话预约）；临床问诊中缺乏信息处理时间，对新程序缺乏熟悉时间；以及未能针对感官需求进行调整。所有这些现象使得神经殊异人群在出现健康问题时寻求帮助以及参加常规筛查预约都成为重大挑战。

A second cause of early mortality is related to specific conditions associated with neurodivergence, such as epilepsy, or cardiovascular vulnerabilities in people with Down syndrome. Not only do these conditions directly increase risk of mortality, but they compound the negative impacts of healthcare inaccessibility, because they increase the amount of healthcare support required by neurodivergent people and the severity of outcome if that care is not received. For example, during the Covid-19 pandemic, meta-analysis showed that people with intellectual disabilities were at significantly higher risk of premature mortality, and they were more at risk than any other disabled group. In the most egregious cases, neurodivergent people may be denied life-saving care because their lives are considered lower value or their quality of life is presumed to be inferior.

神经殊异者早逝的第二个原因与某些特定病症相关，例如癫痫，或唐氏综合征患者的心血管脆弱性。这些病症不仅直接增加了死亡风险，还加剧了医疗可及性不足的负面影响，因为它们增加了神经殊异者所需的医疗支持量，以及若得不到相应护理可能导致的严重后果。例如，在新冠疫情期间，荟萃分析显示，智力障碍者面临显著更高的早逝风险，且其风险高于任何其他残障群体。在最恶劣的情况下，神经殊异者可能被拒绝接受挽救生命的治疗，因为他们的生命被认为价值较低，或其生活质量被推定更为低下。

The third and final major cause of early mortality is suicide—as is often the case, the clearest insights come from studies with autistic people showing much higher rates of suicidal thoughts, suicide attempts, and dying by suicide. However, there is also evidence that risk of suicidality is increased for other neurodivergent people too. Moreover, suicidality has been directly related both to internalized ableism and masking of neurodivergence, suggesting that suicide risk in autistic people is not driven by genetic or neurobiological vulnerability, but by neuronormative forces that also apply to non-autistic neurodivergent people.

第三个也是导致早期死亡的主要原因是自杀——正如通常情况所示，最清晰的见解来自对孤独谱系群体的研究，这些研究显示该群体有更高的自杀念头、自杀尝试和自杀死亡比例。然而，也有证据表明，其他神经殊异人群的自杀风险同样有所上升。此外，自杀倾向与内化的能力歧视和神经殊异性的掩饰直接相关，这表明孤独谱系群体的自杀风险并非由遗传或神经生物学上的脆弱性驱动，而是由同样适用于非孤独谱系的神经殊异人群的神经规范性压力所导致。

These neuronormative forces are also apparent when neurodivergent people access healthcare services for reasons more directly related to being neurodivergent—for example when seeking a diagnosis of ADHD or treatment for OCD. Neurodivergent people must first demonstrate that they are sufficiently different from the norm, and disabled by those differences, to quality for the affirmation that can come from a diagnosis. As we have discussed, the diagnostic process frequently serves the needs of the system more than the needs of the patient. One specific aspect of this is that giving a diagnosis is partly predicated on the need to limit access to resources, in denial of the socio-emotional value of diagnosis in a society which holds independent clinical validation in extremely high regard. If an individual is diagnosed, for example with an anxiety disorder, they are then permitted to access a post-diagnostic pathway in which support is provided. This is emphatically not necessarily the case—autistic people diagnosed as adults, for example, frequently report being provided with a few pamphlets and sent on their way. However, if a post-diagnostic support or treatment pathway is available, it will frequently be framed around a neuronormative agenda in which the features used to identify the best-fit diagnosis for an individual are also presumed to be in need of modification. This is a classic error in healthcare, based in the normalcy paradigm whereby anything atypical is also considered undesirable or dysfunctional. Instead, healthcare services that affirm complexity should pivot post-diagnosis, to a process of co-defining support needs and/or treatment targets with the individual. Importantly, this process will be shaped by knowledge of the diagnosis, but will not necessarily target the same behaviours used to make that diagnosis (e.g. atypical eye-contact in autism, hyperactivity in ADHD).

这些神经规范力量在神经殊异群体因与神经殊异状态更直接相关的原因寻求医疗服务时同样显而易见——例如在寻求多动症诊断或强迫症治疗时。神经殊异者首先必须证明自己与常态足够不同，且这些差异造成了功能障碍，才有资格获得诊断可能带来的身份确认。正如我们讨论过的，诊断过程往往更服务于系统需求而非患者需求。其中一个具体表现是：给予诊断部分基于限制资源获取的需要，这否定了诊断在社会情感层面的价值——在一个将独立临床验证置于极高地位的社会中。例如，若个体被诊断为焦虑症，他们便被允许进入提供支持的诊断后路径。但实际情况绝非必然如此——以成年后被诊断的孤独谱系群体为例，他们常反映仅获得几本宣传册便被草草打发。 然而，如果存在诊断后支持或治疗路径，它往往会被置于神经规范性议程的框架内，即用于确定个体最合适诊断的特征也被认为需要修正。这是医疗保健领域的一个典型错误，源于常态范式，该范式认为任何非典型特征都是不可取或功能失调的。相反，肯定复杂性的医疗服务应在诊断后转向一个与个体共同界定支持需求和/或治疗目标的过程。重要的是，这一过程将受到诊断知识的影响，但未必会针对用于做出该诊断的相同行为（例如，孤独谱系中的非典型眼神接触，ADHD 中的多动）。

Social care is also a domain in which neuronormativity has a toxic effect. Neurodivergent people will frequently find themselves using social care services, with people with a learning disability in particular being some of the main long-term recipients of social care provision. In addition, of course, many neurodivergent people will find themselves living in residential social care—nursing homes—as they grow old. The danger here arises from the control the organization and its staff then have over residents. They will make decisions about every aspect of the environment and routine, and this is unlikely to take account of neurodiversity. Indeed, nursing homes for older people have been described as a form of carceral system, given the barriers to leaving these spaces once they have been entered.

社会照护领域同样是神经规范主义产生毒害效应的场域。神经殊异群体常常会发现自己需要依赖社会照护服务，尤其是有学习障碍的人群，他们往往是社会照护服务最主要的长期受助者。当然，随着年岁增长，许多神经殊异者最终也会入住养老院等社会照护机构。这里的风险在于机构及其工作人员对住户形成的全面掌控——他们决定着环境布置与日常作息的每个细节，却很少会考虑神经多样性的需求。事实上，老年人养老院已被描述为一种变相的监禁体系，因为一旦入住，离开这些空间将面临重重障碍。

One key way to affirm complexity in health and social care is to recognize and capture the expertise of neurodivergent staff more effectively. The National Health Service is one of the world’s largest employers, with well over one million staff. Estimates of the collective prevalence of neurodivergence are always hard, but based on figures of 1 in 5 from UK schools, even accounting for underemployment of neurodivergent people, we would therefore expect to see many tens of thousands of neurodivergent people working in public healthcare in the UK. We should not fall into the trap of assuming that all neurodivergent people can automatically and effortlessly ‘click’ with each other at an individual level, nor should we deny the ability of neurotypical people to provide excellent care and support to neurodivergent folk. However, the expertise of neurodivergent practitioners in health and social care can and must be harnessed in leadership roles, quality improvement work, and pathway or service design to maximize neuroinclusion in this life-or-death context.

在健康与社会照护领域肯定复杂性的一个关键方式，是更有效地认可并汲取神经殊异员工的专业知识。国民医疗服务体系是全球最大的雇主之一，员工数量远超百万。神经殊异性的总体流行率估算总是困难重重，但根据英国学校中每五人中有一人的数据，即使考虑到神经殊异人群就业不足的情况，我们仍可预期在英国公共医疗领域有数万名神经殊异人士在工作。我们不应陷入这样的误区：认为所有神经殊异个体都能在个人层面上自动且轻松地“契合”彼此，也不应否认神经典型人群为神经殊异者提供卓越照护与支持的能力。然而，在生死攸关的医疗环境中，神经殊异从业者在健康与社会照护领域的专业知识，能够且必须在领导岗位、质量改进工作以及诊疗路径或服务设计中得到运用，以最大限度地促进神经包容。



---

Chapter 4 Neurodiversity and collective liberation

Chapter 4 Neurodiversity and collective liberation

第四章 神经多样性与集体解放

So far we have covered the basic theory of neurodiversity, how this theory is applied in research, and how adopting a neurodiversity framework allows us to understand the kinds of problems neurodivergent people tend to face in modern capitalist societies. Building on this, here we consider some more general key components of the movement’s political aims. While the neurodiversity movement is sometimes described as a rights movement, it is more appropriate to describe it as seeking justice and liberation for neurodivergent people by changing society in such a way that ends the neuronormative domination we have suggested is a systemic feature of the modern world. To make what we mean clear, we begin this chapter by considering the importance of human rights while also acknowledging the limitations of a rights-based approach. In particular, we suggest that rights still tend to leave the most marginalized neurodivergent people worse off than those who are more privileged. Given this shortcoming, we then turn to consider how neuronormativity is intertwined with other forms of normativity relating to race, social class, gender, and sexuality. This helps us see how neurodivergent liberation is not a single, isolated ideal, but rather an ideal that is intimately bound up with the liberation of all oppressed people everywhere.

至此，我们已经探讨了神经多样性的基本理论、该理论在研究中的应用，以及采用神经多样性框架如何帮助我们理解神经殊异者在现代资本主义社会中往往面临的各种问题。在此基础上，我们在此思考该运动政治目标中一些更普遍的关键组成部分。虽然神经多样性运动有时被描述为一项权利运动，但更恰当的说法是，它旨在通过改变社会来为神经殊异者寻求正义与解放，从而终结我们之前提出的作为现代世界系统性特征的神经规范性支配。为了阐明我们的意思，本章首先探讨人权的重要性，同时也承认基于权利的方法的局限性。特别是，我们认为权利仍然倾向于让最边缘化的神经殊异者比那些更有特权的人处境更糟。鉴于这一缺陷，我们接着探讨神经规范性如何与涉及种族、社会阶层、性别和性取向的其他规范性形式交织在一起。 这有助于我们理解，神经殊异解放并非一个孤立、单一的理念，而是与世界各地所有受压迫人民的解放紧密相连的理想。

Human rights

人权

The disability rights movement is a global collective movement for the recognition and realization of the human rights of disabled people. All around the world, including in countries which would otherwise consider themselves upholders of international human rights legislation, the rights of disabled people are denied in ableist systems. For example, the USA social security system means that many disabled people who marry face a reduction in, or total loss of, a range of benefits including Medicaid and Medicare. Also in the USA, there are still centres where residents with a learning disability receive electric shocks aimed at modifying behaviour. This practice has been plausibly described as ‘torture’ by disability activist groups. In 2019, the UK—another wealthy and would-be progressive nation—was judged particularly inferior when it came to protecting disabled people from poverty. In those nations which have a poor track record on human rights, disabled people can face particular persecution. Disabled people may be subject to imprisonment, seclusion, shackling, starving, and ‘treatment’ via painful and unethical means.

残疾人权利运动是一场全球性的集体运动，旨在承认和实现残疾人的人权。在世界各地，包括那些自认为是国际人权立法维护者的国家，残疾人的权利在健全主义体系中仍被剥夺。例如，美国的社会保障制度意味着许多结婚的残疾人面临一系列福利的减少或完全丧失，包括医疗补助和医疗保险。同样在美国，仍有一些中心对患有学习障碍的居民实施旨在改变行为的电击疗法。这种做法被残疾人活动团体合理描述为“酷刑”。2019 年，英国——另一个富裕且自诩进步的国家——在保护残疾人免于贫困方面被判定为特别不足。在那些人权记录不佳的国家，残疾人可能面临特别的迫害。残疾人可能遭受监禁、隔离、束缚、饥饿以及通过痛苦和不道德手段进行的“治疗”。

The disability rights movement works to challenge and eradicate these practices and thereby uphold both fundamental and universal human rights (e.g. to freedom from torture), but also more disability-specific rights such as the right to reasonable adjustments at work. To the extent that neurodiversity is also a rights-based movement, it also aims to achieve the rights of neurodivergent people (who may or may not also identify as disabled). This correspondence between the disability rights movement—in many ways a ‘parent’ to the neurodiversity movement—and the neurodiversity movement puts paid to any suspicion that the neurodiversity movement denies disability. Importantly, fighting for the rights of neurodivergent people includes fighting for their right to clinical diagnosis, treatment, support, adjustments, accommodations, evidence-based practices, and expert guidance. Not all of these things will be relevant to every neurodivergent person at all times, but they are all part of the panoply of rights to which neurodivergent people are entitled.

残障权利运动致力于挑战并根除这些做法，从而维护基本且普世的人权（例如免于酷刑的权利），同时也维护更具残障针对性的权利，如工作中获得合理调整的权利。就神经多样性同样是一场基于权利的运动而言，它也旨在实现神经殊异者（他们可能认同也可能不认同自己为残障人士）的权利。残障权利运动——在许多方面是神经多样性运动的“母体”——与神经多样性运动之间的这种对应关系，足以打消任何关于神经多样性运动否认残障的疑虑。重要的是，为神经殊异者的权利而战，包括为他们争取获得临床诊断、治疗、支持、调整、便利、循证实践和专家指导的权利。并非所有这些权利在任何时候都与每一位神经殊异者相关，但它们都是神经殊异者有权享有的全部权利的一部分。

However, there is a limitation to positioning the neurodiversity movement simply as the pursuit of these rights. Securing the rights listed above for all neurodivergent people does not ensure justice. In particular, a large majority of mechanisms to deliver the rights of neurodivergent people involve post-hoc modifications to systems which, at heart, fail to affirm complexity. Moreover, rights are often harder to attain for multiply marginalized neurodivergent people—who may not have support or funds to establish the implementation of their rights in practice—and thus can even help reproduce inequality as much as combat it. It is important to recall here bell hooks’s notion of the ‘imperialist white-supremacist capitalist patriarchy’, and to recognize that rights, while necessary, will never be dispensed equally in this system. With these limitations in mind, there is reason to think we should be pursuing the kinds of fundamental socio-political and cultural shifts which mean that neurodivergent people can succeed without having first to prove the degree of need and then request a ‘special’ measure. This includes understanding ableism as a broader global system, but also necessitates understanding how it relates to other systems of domination.

然而，将神经多样性运动简单地定位为追求这些权利存在局限性。为所有神经殊异者争取上述权利并不能确保正义。特别是，实现神经殊异者权利的大多数机制，本质上都是对未能肯定复杂性的系统进行事后修正。此外，对于遭受多重边缘化的神经殊异者来说，权利往往更难获得——他们可能没有支持或资金来在实践中落实自己的权利——因此，权利甚至可能在对抗不平等的同时，同样助长不平等的再生产。在此，有必要回顾贝尔·胡克斯提出的"帝国主义白人至上资本主义父权制"概念，并认识到权利虽然必要，但在这个体系中永远不会被平等分配。考虑到这些局限性，我们有理由认为，我们应该追求那种根本性的社会政治与文化变革，使得神经殊异者无需首先证明需求程度、再申请"特殊"措施就能获得成功。 这包括将体能歧视理解为一个更广泛的全球性体系，但也需要理解它如何与其他支配体系相关联。

Gender, sexuality, and neuroqueering

性别、性取向与神经酷儿化

One area where more fundamental change might be needed is in relation to what might be called cisheteropatriarchy—the broader system of power and domination that centres men, cisgendered, and straight people while oppressing women, queer, and trans people. The relationship between neurodivergence, gender, and sexuality is complex, but there are several things worth drawing attention to in these regards.

一个可能需要更根本性变革的领域，涉及所谓的顺性别异性恋父权制——这种更广泛的权力与支配体系以男性、顺性别者和异性恋者为中心，同时压迫女性、酷儿和跨性别者。神经殊异性、性别与性取向之间的关系错综复杂，但有几个方面值得在此特别关注。

The first thing to note is that neurodivergent people who are also members of oppressed or marginalized gender or sexuality groups tend to experience more complex forms of oppression. For instance, women with intellectual disabilities have experienced sexual abuse at much higher rates than either women without intellectual disability or men with intellectual disability. In the not-so-distant past, women with intellectual disability—especially Black women—have also often been forcibly sterilized to stop them reproducing. To give another example, autistic people who are also transgender often face intersecting forms of stigma, and their gender identity is sometimes dismissed as a ‘symptom’ of being autistic, or their ability to identify their own gender is questioned. These examples illustrate how gender and neurodivergence are often associated with intersecting forms of oppression that manifest in a variety of ways.

首先要注意的是，那些同时属于受压迫或边缘化的性别或性取向群体的神经殊异者，往往经历着更为复杂的压迫形式。例如，智力障碍女性遭受性虐待的比例远高于非智力障碍女性或智力障碍男性。在不太遥远的过去，智力障碍女性——尤其是黑人女性——还常常被强制绝育，以防止她们生育。再举一例，同时是跨性别者的孤独谱系群体常常面临交叉形式的污名化，他们的性别认同有时被当作孤独谱系的“症状”而遭到否定，或者他们识别自身性别身份的能力受到质疑。这些例子说明了性别与神经殊异性如何常常与以多种方式显现的交叉压迫形式相关联。

It is also worth noting here that struggles parents sometimes have with neurodivergent children are also determined partly by gendered and patriarchal norms. For instance, historically children were raised more communally, in extended families and involving other members of local communities. But various complex changes through the 19th and 20th centuries enforced the nuclear family as the core site of reproduction and care, while simultaneously enforcing most of the caring duties on mothers. This has made it harder to raise all children, but can be especially hard when those children have additional needs. Gendered parenting roles mean that the consequences fall on the shoulders of women more than on men, with consequences for their careers and personal well-being.

同样值得注意的是，父母有时在与神经殊异子女相处中遇到的困难，部分也是由性别和父权规范所决定的。例如，历史上，孩子更多是在大家庭和当地社区其他成员的共同参与下集体抚养长大的。但 19 世纪和 20 世纪各种复杂的变化，使得核心家庭成为生育和照顾的核心场所，同时又将大部分照顾职责强加于母亲身上。这使得抚养所有孩子都变得更加困难，而当这些孩子有额外需求时，情况可能尤其艰难。性别化的育儿角色意味着，后果更多地落在女性的肩上，而非男性，这对她们的职业和个人福祉都产生了影响。

Moreover, culturally specific and gendered expectations about how children will behave (e.g. boys are adventurous, energetic, and bold; girls are delicate, gentle, and sweet) can lead to negative judgement on both children and their parents when those children fail to conform. Neurodivergent children may be especially likely to fail against gendered norms of behaviour and interest—girls with ADHD might be considered too active and noisy; boys with dyspraxia might struggle to fit in with activities heavily centred on team sports. Conversely, adherence to gendered expectations can act to mask neurodivergence. For example, a young woman’s interests in make-up or celebrity gossip may be considered ‘appropriate’, and the intensity of their focus—a potential clue that they could be autistic—may be missed. A boy who avoids reading and spends his time outdoors might be thought of as having a typical male preference for rough-and-tumble, his dyslexia going undiagnosed and reading problems unaddressed. In this we see how efforts to challenge patriarchal structures and norms around motherhood and parenting may also be helpful for neurodivergent children.

此外，关于儿童行为方式的文化特定和性别化期望（例如男孩应富有冒险精神、精力充沛、大胆无畏；女孩应娇柔、温和、甜美）可能导致儿童及其父母在未能符合这些期望时受到负面评价。神经殊异儿童尤其可能难以满足性别化的行为和兴趣规范——患有注意力缺陷多动障碍的女孩可能被认为过于活跃和吵闹；患有发育性协调障碍的男孩可能难以融入以团队运动为核心的活动。相反，对性别化期望的遵从可能掩盖神经殊异性。例如，年轻女性对化妆或名人八卦的兴趣可能被视为“恰当的”，而她们专注的强度——这可能是她们属于孤独谱系的潜在线索——可能被忽视。一个回避阅读、将时间花在户外的男孩可能被认为具有典型的男性偏好，喜欢打闹嬉戏，而其阅读障碍未被诊断，阅读问题也未得到解决。由此我们看到，挑战围绕母职和育儿方式的父权结构与规范的努力，也可能对神经殊异儿童有所帮助。

Beyond such intersectional issues, intersecting power dynamics manifest not just in how neurodivergent people are treated and spotted, but also in how different forms of neurodivergence are represented or understood in the first place. For instance, autism has traditionally been represented as a mainly male diagnosis, but in recent decades female and nonbinary autistics have campaigned to gain greater recognition. What has become clearer is that traditional stereotypes of autistic people, and the diagnostic tools that enshrine them, are overly biased towards interests and behaviours socially coded as male—for instance being interested in mathematics or engineering. Not only does this reinforce outdated gendered assumptions, it also does so in a way that contributes to a lack of recognition for female and nonbinary autistic people. Another example is borderline personality disorder. This is a contested yet widely diagnosed condition associated with traits such as fear of abandonment, feelings of emptiness, unstable social relationships, and other related tendencies. Notably, it is mainly diagnosed in women and girls, including many who are queer, often when they break expected gender and sexual norms in ways that are seen as problematic by society. Neurodiversity proponents have thus often noted how the construct is used to reinforce misogynistic and heterosexual norms. However, it should also be noted that there is disagreement among neurodiversity proponents whether it should be abolished or reclaimed through a neurodiversity paradigm perspective.

除了这些交叉性问题，权力动态的交织不仅体现在神经殊异群体如何被对待和识别，还体现在不同形式的神经殊异性最初是如何被呈现或理解的。例如，孤独谱系传统上被描述为一种主要针对男性的诊断，但近几十年来，女性及非二元性别的孤独谱系人士一直在努力争取更多的认可。越来越清楚的是，对孤独谱系群体的传统刻板印象，以及固化这些印象的诊断工具，都过度偏向于被社会编码为男性化的兴趣和行为——例如对数学或工程学的兴趣。这不仅强化了过时的性别假设，还以一种导致女性和非二元性别的孤独谱系人士缺乏认可的方式加剧了这一问题。另一个例子是边缘型人格障碍。这是一种存在争议但被广泛诊断的病症，其特征包括对被抛弃的恐惧、空虚感、不稳定的社会关系以及其他相关倾向。 值得注意的是，它主要被诊断于女性与女孩，其中许多是酷儿群体，往往当她们以社会视为问题的方式打破预期的性别与性规范时。因此，神经多样性的支持者经常指出，这一建构如何被用来强化厌女症和异性恋规范。然而，也应注意，神经多样性支持者之间对于是否应废除它，还是通过神经多样性范式视角重新主张其意义，存在分歧。

When it comes to sexuality, it is worth again considering how homosexuality (to use the historical term) was pathologized as a mental disorder for much of the 20th century. From the 1960s to the 1980s especially, significant efforts were made by psychologists and psychiatrists to develop treatments or cures for same-sex attraction—efforts now known as conversion therapy. In practice, these attempts were incredibly harmful, causing mental health problems rather than healing them. In fact, homosexuality was only depathologized in the UK and USA in 1980, although even then elements of the pathologization have been retained in other diagnoses. For instance, from 1980, the diagnosis of ego dystonic homosexuality was developed and used for some years for queer people who are suffering from mental health problems relating to their sexuality. Moreover, far from being a one-off, other people who break gendered and sex norms have also often been wrongly pathologized, for instance intersex and trans people.

在性取向方面，值得再次审视的是，同性恋（使用历史术语）在 20 世纪大部分时间里如何被病理化为一种精神障碍。特别是从 20 世纪 60 年代到 80 年代，心理学家和精神科医生付出了巨大努力，试图开发针对同性吸引的治疗或治愈方法——这些努力如今被称为“转化疗法”。实际上，这些尝试极其有害，不仅未能治愈，反而引发了心理健康问题。事实上，同性恋直到 1980 年才在英国和美国被去病理化，但即便如此，病理化的某些元素仍保留在其他诊断中。例如，自 1980 年起，“自我失谐型同性恋”这一诊断被提出并使用了多年，用于指代那些因性取向而遭受心理健康困扰的酷儿群体。此外，这绝非孤例，其他打破性别和性规范的人也常常被错误地病理化，例如双性人和跨性别者。

One way of making sense of such cases is to consider how intimately intertwined gendered and sexual norms are with neuronormativity. What is considered ‘normal’ in all of these regards grew together historically, while interacting in complex ways, and this is why they are hard to separate still today. For instance, autism was first pathologized, mainly in boys, in Nazi Germany. Notably this was a period where gender norms were highly restrictive and boys and men were supposed to exhibit a ‘soldier mentality’. In this context, boys who were more solitary were increasingly seen as a problem to be fixed. The Nazis murdered many autistic people—not just boys, but also many girls with intellectual disability—alongside Jews, Sinti, queers, and other targets of Nazi ideology. Once we recognize how closely intertwined neuronormativity is with these other norms, we can see that neurodivergent liberation is intimately intertwined with trans and queer liberation as well as with the liberation of women from patriarchy, and that this will be good for us regardless of which gender or sexuality we have. A commitment to the neurodiversity paradigm’s principle of politicizing neuronormativity thus also requires recognizing how our sexed and gendered norms are, far from being natural, the products of specific historical conditions and can often be oppressive.

理解这些案例的一种方式是思考性别与性规范与神经规范之间有多么紧密地交织在一起。在这些方面被视为“正常”的标准在历史上是共同发展起来的，它们以复杂的方式相互作用，这也是为什么时至今日它们仍难以分离。例如，孤独谱系最初在纳粹德国被病理化，主要对象是男孩。值得注意的是，那是一个性别规范极为严苛的时期，男孩和男性被期望表现出一种“士兵心态”。在这种背景下，那些更孤僻的男孩日益被视为需要纠正的问题。纳粹分子杀害了许多孤独谱系群体——不仅是男孩，还有许多有智力障碍的女孩——同时还有犹太人、辛提人、酷儿群体以及其他纳粹意识形态的迫害对象。一旦我们认识到神经规范与这些其他规范是如何紧密交织的，我们就能明白，神经殊异者的解放与跨性别者和酷儿群体的解放，以及女性从父权制中的解放，是密不可分的，而且无论我们拥有何种性别或性取向，这都将对我们有益。 坚持神经多样性范式将神经规范性政治化的原则，因此也需要认识到，我们的性别规范远非自然产物，而是特定历史条件的产物，并且常常具有压迫性。

One good thing that has begun to come out of this is new ways of pushing back against intersecting axes of oppression, with this activism being led by neurodivergent women, queer, and nonbinary people. One helpful concept and practice that has emerged from the recognition of this, for instance, is that of ‘neuroqueering’. This describes a form of behaving—or performing—that seeks to challenge broader social norms at the point where gender norms and neuronomativity intersect. Neuroqueering is hard to define, but one way of understanding it is as committing to living in ways that playfully resist the ways in which these norms constrain all of us, to seek out new and healthier ways of living. In line with this, new forms of neurodivergent feminist and queer organizing will most likely be necessary for neurodivergent liberation in the long run.

由此开始出现的一个积极进展是，出现了新的方式来抵制交叉的压迫轴心，这一行动由神经殊异女性、酷儿和非二元性别者领导。例如，从这一认识中产生的一个有益概念和实践是“神经酷儿化”。这描述了一种行为或表演形式，旨在挑战性别规范和神经规范性相交汇处的更广泛社会规范。神经酷儿化很难定义，但一种理解方式是致力于以游戏性的方式抵抗这些规范对我们所有人的束缚，寻求新的、更健康的生活方式。与此相一致，从长远来看，新的神经殊异女权主义和酷儿组织形式很可能对神经殊异的解放是必要的。

Race, decolonization, and neuroexpansiveness

种族、去殖民化与神经扩展性

Like the relationship between neurodivergence and gender, we also see similarly complex relations and interactions when it comes to neurodiversity and race. The first thing to note here is that, historically, conceptions of normal mental functioning, intelligence, and so forth grew along with the rise of white supremacy and have remained intimately intertwined with them. As European empires colonized parts of Africa and as the field of psychiatry was beginning to emerge, for instance, psychiatrists in Britain wrote about the inferiority of African and indigenous peoples around the world, comparing non-disabled members of oppressed races to mentally disabled white Brits. European empires also brought psychiatric institutions to many colonies globally, where Black and indigenous peoples were often pathologized and treated in uniquely cruel and dehumanizing ways. As such the normalcy paradigm was not just enforced on neurodivergent people in the imperial core, but also used as a tool of colonization around the globe.

正如神经殊异性与性别之间的关系一样，在神经多样性与种族问题上，我们也观察到同样复杂的关系与互动。首先需要指出的是，从历史角度看，关于正常心理功能、智力等概念的形成，与白人至上主义的兴起同步发展，且始终与之紧密交织。例如，当欧洲帝国殖民非洲部分地区、精神病学领域开始萌芽时，英国精神病学家曾撰文贬低非洲及全球原住民，将受压迫种族的非残障成员与心智残障的英国白人相提并论。欧洲帝国还将精神病机构推广至全球众多殖民地，黑人与原住民在那里常被病理化，并遭受独特而残酷的非人对待。由此可见，常态范式不仅被强加于帝国核心地带的神经殊异者，更成为全球殖民统治的工具。

This is not just a historical problem. Today, Black and Brown neurodivergent people in white majority nations such as the UK and USA are more likely to encounter a range of issues such as police violence, discrimination, and hate crimes. Consider, for instance, how a white neurodivergent person acting in ways seen as odd in public might be seen as merely eccentric, while a Black neurodivergent person acting the same way might be seen as dangerous. In such an instance, (probably white) members of the public might call the police, and once this happens the chances of violence against the Black neurodivergent person escalate dramatically. Beyond the imperial core, writers such as Frantz Fanon have emphasized how colonialism and racism impact the mental health, and individual and collective psyches, of colonized peoples in complex and insidious ways. Thus white supremacy and colonialism are intertwined with neuronormativity in different ways in different contexts.

这不仅是历史遗留问题。如今，在英国和美国等白人占多数的国家中，黑人和棕色人种的神经殊异者更可能遭遇一系列问题，如警察暴力、歧视和仇恨犯罪。试想，一个白人的神经殊异者在公共场合做出被视为怪异的行为时，可能只会被看作古怪；而一个黑人的神经殊异者做出同样的行为时，却可能被视为危险。在这种情况下，（可能为白人的）公众成员可能会报警，而一旦报警，针对黑人神经殊异者的暴力风险便会急剧上升。在帝国核心之外，像弗朗茨·法农这样的作家强调，殖民主义和种族主义以复杂而隐蔽的方式影响着被殖民人民的心理健康以及个人和集体心理。因此，白人至上主义和殖民主义在不同情境下以不同方式与神经规范性相互交织。

As with gender, our dominant representations of neurodivergence also tend to have racialized biases. For instance, autism has often been represented as not just male, but also white and middle class. This has stifled recognition and state support for Black autistics, especially those who are female or nonbinary. Further back, in the 1960s Black civil rights protesters in the United States were pathologized as having a ‘protest psychosis’ to dismiss their anti-racist activism. Thus, people from marginalized racial or ethnic groups can either be excluded from useful diagnoses or given harmful ones, in ways that uphold economic inequality.

与性别一样，我们对神经殊异性的主流描述也往往带有种族化的偏见。例如，孤独谱系不仅常被描绘为男性特征，还常被描绘为白人和中产阶级特征。这阻碍了对黑人孤独谱系人士，尤其是女性或非二元性别者的认可和国家支持。更早之前，在 20 世纪 60 年代，美国的黑人民权抗议者被病理化为患有“抗议精神病”，以否定他们的反种族主义行动。因此，来自边缘化种族或族裔群体的人要么被排除在有用的诊断之外，要么被给予有害的诊断，这些方式都助长了经济不平等。

Recognition of such issues has led to decolonial work by neurodivergent scholars of colour. For instance, Arya Thampuran’s work examines mental health by drawing on a range of resources from across the majority world that offer alternatives to dominant biomedical framings. At the same time, it is worth considering how the neurodiversity movement needs to focus more on decolonial efforts. In a recent article, neurodiversity proponents Vishnu KK Nair, Warda Farah, and Mildred Boveda identify how the neurodiversity paradigm has retained an epistemic whiteness and focus on the Global North that needs to be overcome for the liberatory goals of the movement to be realized.

对这些问题的认识，促使有色人种的神经殊异学者开展了去殖民化工作。例如，Arya Thampuran 的研究借鉴了来自多数世界各地的多种资源，这些资源为主流的生物医学框架提供了替代方案，从而审视心理健康问题。与此同时，值得思考的是，神经多样性运动需要如何更多地聚焦于去殖民化努力。在一篇近期的文章中，神经多样性的倡导者 Vishnu KK Nair、Warda Farah 和 Mildred Boveda 指出，神经多样性范式如何保留了认知上的白人中心主义，并聚焦于全球北方，而为了实现该运动的解放目标，这些都需要被克服。

Because of how closely neuronormativity and racialized norms are intertwined, Ngozi Alston, a Black autistic writer, has proposed the term ‘neuroexpansive’ rather than ‘neurodivergent’ specifically as a term for Black people (and Black people only) to use. This emphasizes, in Alston’s words, how ‘neurotypical’ will ‘never be able to accurately describe Black bodyminds’ on the grounds that Black people have never been considered neurotypical. This kind of new, historically informed theoretical work seeks to help build an analysis for autonomous Black communities seeking to resist white supremacy and colonialism from a neurologically disabled perspective. In line with this example, it seems imperative for neurodiversity advocates to recognize how closely intertwined neuronormativity and white supremacy are when understood as systemic global forces. As with gender and sexuality, liberation for neurodivergents is also intimately bound up with liberation from racial inequality and the global systems that underpin it.

鉴于神经规范性与种族化规范紧密交织，黑人孤独谱系作家恩戈齐·阿尔斯顿提出了"神经拓展"而非"神经殊异"这一术语，专门供黑人（且仅限黑人）使用。用阿尔斯顿的话说，这强调"神经典型性"永远无法准确描述黑人的身心状态"，因为黑人从未被视为神经典型群体。这类融合历史认知的新理论工作，旨在为寻求从神经残障视角抵抗白人至上主义与殖民主义的黑人自治社群构建分析框架。遵循此例，神经多样性倡导者必须认识到：当被理解为系统性全球力量时，神经规范性与白人至上主义存在着何等紧密的共生关系。正如性别与性向解放运动，神经殊异者的解放亦与挣脱种族不平等及其全球支撑体系的斗争血脉相连。

Finally, it is crucial to note that the roots of the neurodiversity movement lie largely in the Global North, and much of the work contributing to arguments in this book has been generated by scholars in Europe and North America, drawing on research samples with limited racial, ethnic, and cultural diversity. Recently, neurodiversity activists have written about the global potential of the neurodiversity paradigm, while also noting that there is a danger that exporting this theoretical model unthinkingly from WEIRD (Western, Educated, Industrialized, Rich, Democratic) to non-WEIRD societies risks recapitulating the harms of colonialism. One challenge for the movement as it stands is to learn from culturally diverse ways of conceptualizing what we are calling neurodiversity and cultivate space for those to contribute to our understanding and socio-political goals. We must work collectively to uplift those of us from low- and middle-income countries and the Global South, recognizing the dangers such pioneers may face in societies which reject neurodivergence particularly powerfully. Efforts towards this can be seen in projects such as the ‘Fund for Community Reparations for Autistic People of Color’s Interdependence, Survival, and Empowerment’, which is based in the USA but has global reach. At the same time, those of us in the Global North must be vigilant against the risk of presuming our largely Western conceptions of neurodivergence are the only or best way of achieving neurodivergent liberation.

最后，必须指出的是，神经多样性运动的根源主要在于全球北方，本书中诸多论点所依据的研究成果大多由欧美学者贡献，其研究样本在种族、民族和文化多样性方面存在局限。近来，神经多样性活动家们探讨了这一范式在全球范围内的潜力，同时也指出，若不加思索地将这一理论模型从 WEIRD（西方、受过教育、工业化、富裕、民主）社会照搬到非 WEIRD 社会，恐有重蹈殖民主义覆辙的风险。当前运动面临的一项挑战是，需从文化多元的视角汲取智慧，重新审视我们称之为"神经多样性"的概念，并为这些多元视角参与我们的认知体系和社会政治目标创造空间。我们必须共同努力，提升来自中低收入国家和全球南方地区群体的声音，同时清醒认识到，在那些对神经殊异性排斥尤为强烈的社会中，这些先驱者可能面临的危险。 在美国发起但具有全球影响力的"有色人种孤独谱系群体互助、生存与赋权社区补偿基金"等项目，正体现了这方面的努力。 与此同时，我们这些身处全球北方的人必须警惕一种风险：不能想当然地认为我们主要源自西方的神经殊异性观念是实现神经殊异解放的唯一或最佳途径。

Neurodiversity and anti-capitalism

神经多样性与反资本主义

A related question regards whether neurodivergent people can be liberated from the normalcy paradigm and oppressive norms under capitalism at all. At the moment capitalism is a global economic system that—aside from a few pockets of resistance—none of us can escape. As such, a fair amount of neurodiversity advocacy has sought to attain rights within capitalism rather than challenging that system itself. Much diversity and inclusion work, for instance, is about getting more neurodivergent people into work through recognizing neurodivergent ‘strengths’. This does help some individuals, but leaves the deeper structure of capitalist society wholly intact.

一个相关的问题是，神经殊异者能否真正从常态范式和资本主义下的压迫性规范中解放出来。目前，资本主义是一个全球经济体系——除了少数抵抗的角落——我们无人能够逃脱。因此，相当一部分神经多样性倡导活动旨在在资本主义内部争取权利，而非挑战这一体系本身。例如，许多多元化和包容性工作的重点是通过认可神经殊异者的“优势”，让更多神经殊异者进入职场。这确实帮助了一些个体，却让资本主义社会的深层结构完全保持不变。

However, a view from anti-capitalist neurodiversity advocates is that neuronormativity and the normalcy paradigm are products of capitalism itself and reflect the workings of this broader system in important ways. Note for instance that within capitalism each person has to compete against all others to work, and—when it comes to work—we are primarily defined by our perceived or actual potential for productivity. Within this system, our neurological and bodily norms have restricted considerably, especially following the industrial revolution and then more recent shifts towards service industry and information-based jobs that require greater emotional and attentive capacities. These shifts have meant that, instead of working as family units or with local communities, each individual is increasingly measured against everyone else in terms of their emotional and cognitive performance. Hence many job application processes now include cognitive and personality tests that do not just discriminate against neurodivergent people, but also are part of what constitutes our cultural neuronormativity.

然而，反资本主义的神经多样性倡导者认为，神经规范性与常态范式本身就是资本主义的产物，并在重要方面反映了这一更广泛体系的运作方式。例如，请注意，在资本主义制度下，每个人都必须与他人竞争工作机会，而在工作方面，我们主要被定义为基于感知或实际的生产力潜力。在这一体系中，我们的神经和身体规范受到了极大限制，尤其是在工业革命之后，以及最近向服务业和信息型工作的转变，这些工作对情感和注意力的要求更高。这些转变意味着，个人不再以家庭单位或地方社区的形式工作，而是越来越多地根据其情感和认知表现与他人进行比较。因此，许多求职流程现在包含了认知和人格测试，这些测试不仅歧视神经殊异者，也是构成我们文化神经规范性的一部分。

Looked at this way, the normalcy paradigm can be seen as having arisen in part to reinforce the norms of capitalism. But if this is so, then it’s not clear to what extent it will be possible to truly overcome the normalcy paradigm while we remain in this economic system. If this is convincing, then efforts to promote diversity initiatives, get more neurodivergent people into work, and reduce stigma will only have limited impact without changing the deeper economic structures of society. Thus, for proponents of anti-capitalist neurodiversity, neurodivergent liberation is intimately intertwined with the liberation of the working class from an unjust economic system. This requires neurodivergent people organizing as workers—or would-be workers—in unions, as voting blocks, or in revolutionary activism and protest to make demands on the state and ultimately to change the nature of the state in order to work towards neurodivergent—and collective—liberation.

从这个角度来看，正常性范式的形成在一定程度上可被视为是为了强化资本主义的规范。但若果真如此，那么在我们仍处在这个经济体系中的情况下，能在多大程度上真正克服正常性范式，尚不明确。如果这一观点具有说服力，那么在不改变更深层社会经济结构的前提下，推动多元化倡议、让更多神经殊异人士就业以及减少污名化的努力，其影响将十分有限。因此，对于反资本主义神经多样性的支持者而言，神经殊异者的解放与工人阶级从不公正的经济体系中获得解放是紧密交织的。这要求神经殊异者作为工人——或潜在的工人——通过工会组织、投票群体，或参与革命行动和抗议活动，向国家提出诉求，并最终改变国家的性质，从而为实现神经殊异者乃至集体的解放而奋斗。



---

Chapter 5 Current debates

Chapter 5 Current debates

第五章 当前争议

Throughout this book we have explored the meaning and potential of the concept of neurodiversity, and the neurodiversity paradigm, to reimagine systems. The nature of the arguments and evidence presented will have made clear how early we are on the journey to neurodivergent liberation, and how much is still to be determined. In that context, we review here some key areas for open debate which have not yet been directly addressed in the preceding chapters.

在本书中，我们探讨了神经多样性概念及其范式在重塑社会体系方面的意义与潜力。所呈现的论点与证据的性质已清楚表明，我们距离实现神经殊异解放的征程尚处早期阶段，仍有诸多问题亟待厘清。在此背景下，本章将审视几个尚未在前文直接讨论的关键开放辩论领域。

Neurodiversity and learning disability

神经多样性与学习障碍

In the preceding discussions, we have often drawn attention to the specific inequalities to which people with a learning disability are vulnerable. A common accusation levelled against the concept of neurodiversity and its proponents in the neurodiversity movement is that it excludes people with a learning disability. As a reminder, we use the term ‘learning disability’ as it is used in the UK, to describe a specific diagnosis made when an individual has significant difficulty understanding complex information or learning new skills, often diagnosed in the presence of an IQ test score below 70. It is worth taking a moment to examine the validity of this idea and why it arises so often.

在前面的讨论中，我们时常关注学习障碍人士所面临的特定不平等现象。针对神经多样性概念及其在神经多样性运动中的支持者，一种常见的指责是它排除了学习障碍人士。需要说明的是，我们采用英国对"学习障碍"这一术语的用法，用以描述当个体在理解复杂信息或学习新技能方面存在显著困难时作出的特定诊断，通常以智商测试分数低于 70 作为诊断依据。我们有必要花些时间审视这种观点的合理性及其频繁出现的原因。

Learning disability is a naturally occurring form of neurodivergence, sometimes linked to heritable genetic variants (e.g. fragile x syndrome), sometimes arising de novo (e.g. Down syndrome), but often having no known biological cause. While there is no good reason for people with a learning disability to not have equal value in our society, this principle is rarely true in practice. In many Western societies, a historic value system that placed a premium on the lives of the wealthy has been seamlessly replaced by a value system based on intelligence—if not formally tested then informally judged. We have allowed ourselves to think that valuing intelligence, or some correlate of that (educational qualifications, verbal fluency, business acumen, income), is a fair system. Since intelligence is distributed equally between people of different genders, races, ethnicities, and sexualities, we can argue that a focus on intelligence can help to combat inequalities of opportunity in schools and workplaces, where attainment is both measured and highly prized. However, by definition a focus on intelligence as a value system excludes people with a learning disability, just as reliably and unacceptably as a focus on height would disadvantage women. Thus, adoption of a neurodiversity model entails a rejection of the supremacy of IQ as a marker of human worth. Until we understand and apply this manifestation of the neurodiversity paradigm, we will not be inclusive of people with a learning disability.

学习障碍是一种自然发生的神经殊异性形式，有时与可遗传的基因变异有关（如脆性 X 染色体综合征），有时是新发产生的（如唐氏综合征），但通常没有已知的生物学原因。尽管没有充分的理由认为学习障碍者不应在我们的社会中享有同等价值，但这一原则在实践中很少成立。在许多西方社会，历史上重视富人生命价值的体系，已悄然被一种基于智力的价值体系所取代——即使没有经过正式测试，也会被非正式地评判。我们让自己相信，重视智力或其相关特质（教育资历、语言流利度、商业头脑、收入）是一种公平的体系。由于智力在不同性别、种族、民族和性取向的人群中分布均等，我们可以认为，关注智力有助于对抗学校和工作场所中的机会不平等，因为在这些地方，成就既被衡量又备受重视。 然而，根据定义，将智力作为价值体系的核心，必然会排斥有学习障碍的人，其排斥的确定性和不可接受性，就如同以身高为标准会不利于女性一样。因此，采纳神经多样性模式，就意味着要摒弃将智商作为衡量人类价值至高标准的做法。除非我们理解并应用神经多样性范式的这一体现，否则我们将无法真正包容有学习障碍的人。

One reason why this mismatch—between many public accounts of the neurodiversity movement and the inclusion and liberation of people with a learning disability—might arise is because for many neurodivergent people, advocating for their rights entails highlighting their intellectual capacities. Individuals should clearly be allowed, and in fact enabled and encouraged, to understand their abilities, to develop them to their full potential, and to make these apparent to others—particularly teachers and employers. We can all draw self-esteem, joy, and opportunity from identifying the things we are good at, and doing those things. However, we need to guard against the conflation of these talents with our value as human beings. While a facility with written language might be highly valuable for a journalist, or mathematical skills may be valued in the financial services industry, such contextualized value does not apply when considering the fundamental equal value, and rights, of every member of the human race. Individual neurodivergent people have every right to advertise their talents and push back against assumptions that they lack ability, but we must collectively be careful to do this in a way that doesn’t make talent or intellect a proxy for individual worth.

许多关于神经多样性运动的公开描述与学习障碍者的包容和解放之间存在脱节，其中一个原因可能是，对于许多神经殊异者而言，争取自身权利往往需要强调他们的智力能力。显然，个体应当被允许——事实上是被赋能和鼓励——去了解自己的能力，充分发展潜力，并向他人（尤其是教师和雇主）展示这些能力。我们都能从发现并从事自己擅长的事情中获得自尊、快乐和机遇。然而，我们需要警惕将这些才能与作为人的价值混为一谈。虽然书面语言能力对记者可能极具价值，数学技能在金融服务业可能受到重视，但在考量人类每个成员的根本平等价值和权利时，这种情境化的价值并不适用。 每个神经殊异的个体都有充分的权利展示自己的才能，并反驳那些认为他们缺乏能力的假设，但我们必须共同注意，在这样做时，不应将才能或智力作为衡量个人价值的替代标准。

In order to politicize neuronormativity, neurodiversity must be understood in relation to societal and interpersonal phenomena such as stereotypes, stigma, prejudice, and discrimination. The experience of neurodivergent people is heavily dictated by these forces. This is undoubtedly specifically true for people with a learning disability, but rarely recognized as such. In particular, an unthinking adherence to the legitimacy of intelligence-as-value can justify a failure to facilitate people with a learning disability to have paid employment, opportunities for friendship, romance, and a sex life, or autonomy in a general sense. This is an example of social injustice at work, and yet is rarely perceived as such. It is true that the facilitation of autonomy may require intensive resourcing and skilled support. There will be some individuals for whom making choices will always be dependent on the close observations of others, reading and interpreting subtle signs and signals, with a degree of trial and error involved. As such, achieving the liberation of people with a learning disability is a test for the neurodiversity movement, but one which must be attempted.

为了将神经规范性政治化，必须将神经多样性置于刻板印象、污名、偏见和歧视等社会与人际现象的关联中来理解。神经殊异者的体验在很大程度上由这些力量所决定。这对于有学习障碍的人来说无疑是特别真实的，却很少被如此认知。尤其是一种对“智力即价值”之合法性的不加思索的遵从，可以为未能支持有学习障碍者获得有偿就业、友谊机会、浪漫与性生活，或广义上的自主性提供辩护。这是社会不公在运作中的一个例子，却很少被如此看待。诚然，支持自主性可能需要密集的资源投入和专业的支持。对于某些个体而言，做出选择将始终依赖于他人细致的观察，解读微妙的迹象和信号，并涉及一定程度的试错。因此，实现有学习障碍者的解放是对神经多样性运动的一次考验，但这是一次必须进行的尝试。

The final way in which the neurodiversity movement can be seen to exclude people with a learning disability concerns leadership and advocacy. A great deal of thinking and writing about neurodiversity has come from autistic people, often those with postgraduate degrees, confident and fluent writers and speakers. All too often, their voices are pitched against neurotypical parents of people with a learning disability, as if only these two possible advocate groups exist. Autistic academic and community leader Mary Doherty calls this ‘weaponized heterogeneity’—when the variability among neurodivergent people is used to negate their ability to advocate for each other. Of course, attempts to divide advocates on behalf of people with a learning disability into two groups are falsely based. First, there are many neurodivergent people who are parents or carers of people with a learning disability—these numbers are inflated beyond population averages due to genetics and the particularly common overlap of autism and learning disability. More profoundly, it is wrong to presume that there exist two separate categories of autistic people, with a clear space between on the one hand autistic people who are community leaders and activists with no learning disability, and on the other those with a learning disability who are supported in institutions—Mel Baggs’s shared experience provides a powerful challenge to this crude dichotomy. And finally, many people with a learning disability can advocate for themselves, especially if provided with suitable facilitation and a platform.

神经多样性运动可能将学习障碍者排除在外的最后一种方式，涉及领导权和倡导工作。大量关于神经多样性的思考和著述来自孤独谱系群体，其中许多人拥有研究生学位，是自信且表达流畅的写作者和演说者。他们的声音常常与学习障碍者的神经典型性父母形成对立，仿佛只有这两个可能的倡导群体存在。孤独谱系学者兼社区领袖玛丽·多尔蒂将这种现象称为“武器化的异质性”——即利用神经殊异者之间的差异性来否定他们为彼此发声的能力。当然，试图将代表学习障碍者的倡导者划分为两个群体的做法是站不住脚的。首先，许多神经殊异者本身就是学习障碍者的父母或照顾者——由于遗传因素以及孤独谱系与学习障碍特别常见的重叠，这一群体的数量远超人口平均水平。 更深刻地说，认为存在两个截然不同的孤独谱系群体类别是错误的——一边是那些没有学习障碍、作为社区领袖和活动家的孤独谱系群体，另一边则是那些有学习障碍、在机构中得到支持的孤独谱系群体，两者之间泾渭分明。梅尔·巴格斯的共同经历有力地挑战了这种粗糙的二分法。 最后，许多有学习障碍的人能够为自己发声，尤其是在获得适当的协助和平台的情况下。

What all this means is that when leaders in the neurodiversity movement campaign for change and draw attention to the inequalities that need to be broken down, it is both easy and common for others to claim that people with a learning disability are not being represented in those arguments. We contend that such claims reinforce the need for the neurodiversity movement. Application of the neurodiversity paradigm to the specific case of people with a learning disability is required to emphasize a legitimate basis for equal value, rejecting the hegemony of intellect, and to draw attention to the inequalities that mean their own perspectives are so rarely heard and their autonomy is so rarely realized.

这一切意味着，当神经多样性运动的倡导者们推动变革并提请关注那些需要打破的不平等时，其他人很容易且常常声称，学习障碍者并未在这些论述中得到代表。我们认为，这类主张恰恰强化了神经多样性运动的必要性。将神经多样性范式应用于学习障碍者这一具体案例，正是为了强调平等价值的合法基础，拒绝智力霸权，并提请关注那些导致他们自身观点极少被倾听、其自主性极少得以实现的不平等现象。

Neurodiversity-lite

庸俗版神经多样性

The neurodiversity movement is still relatively young and, as such, vulnerable to misinterpretation and wilful exploitation. We refer to the deployment of neurodiversity language, or partial adoption of some neurodiversity concepts, without deep engagement with the scholarship and principles of the movement, as ‘neurodiversity-lite’. This name, however, belies the deeply toxic potential of this flavour of discourse and action.

神经多样性运动仍相对年轻，因此容易遭到误解和蓄意利用。我们将那种仅使用神经多样性语言，或部分采纳某些神经多样性概念，却未深入理解该运动的学术基础和原则的做法，称为“庸俗版神经多样性”。然而，这一名称掩盖了此类话语和行动潜在的严重危害性。

The first form of neurodiversity-lite is most commonly observed when terminology from the movement is adopted, but overlaid on existing practices without underlying change taking place. It is surprisingly easy to adopt phrases like ‘neurodiversity-informed’ within systems which follow the normalcy paradigm. For example, a new clinical pathway for broad-based neurodevelopmental assessment of adults, which provides concurrent assessment for and diagnosis of autism and ADHD, might call itself a neurodiversity-informed pathway, because it recognizes the frequent co-occurrence of these two diagnostic categories. To some degree, such a system is working to affirm complexity, but there are many ways that same system may fail to be fully neurodiversity affirmative. For instance, there might also be efforts to limit the number of diagnoses given based on an erroneous concern about there being ‘too many’ adults seeking a diagnosis. Post-diagnosis, the clinical pathway might offer a neuronormative treatment pathway, rather than challenging this model. While this example is fictional, our point here is to note how straightforward it is to adopt neurodiversity language in a manner which passes superficial inspection without deeply engaging with the tenets of the movement.

第一种形式的"庸俗版神经多样性"最常见于这样一种情况：运用运动中的术语，却只是覆盖在现有实践之上，而未发生根本性的改变。在遵循常态范式的体系内采用诸如"神经多样性知情"这样的短语，这种方式简单无比。例如，一项针对成人进行广泛性神经发育评估的新临床路径，能够同时提供孤独谱系和 ADHD 的评估与诊断，可能就会自称为一条神经多样性知情的路径，因为它承认了这两种诊断类别经常同时出现。在某种程度上，这样的体系确实在努力确认复杂性，但同一个体系也可能在许多方面未能完全做到肯定神经多样性。例如，可能还会基于一种错误的担忧——即担心寻求诊断的成人"太多"——而试图限制给出的诊断数量。在诊断之后，该临床路径可能提供一条神经规范性的治疗路径，而不是去挑战这一模式。 虽然这个例子是虚构的，但我们的目的是指出，采用神经多样性语言的方式可以如此轻易地通过表面审查，而无需深入理解该运动的核心原则。

Similar cosmetic changes are possible in schools, universities, workplaces, and social care settings. In most cases, our informal analysis suggests that this kind of neurodiversity-lite occurs in two scenarios. One is when progressive people, perhaps recognizing that current systems are flawed, come across the word ‘neurodiversity’ and attempt to apply it in the mistaken (and doubtless subconscious) belief that a combination of positive intentions and the latest terminology is equivalent to meaningful change. Such people could be open to deeper shifts in practice, but may fail to recognize that these have not occurred. The other is when organizations feel under pressure to ‘move with the times’, while fundamentally uncritical of their existing modes of operation. They may more consciously choose to make the minimum possible concession to the growing neurodiversity movement by relabelling systems, while actively avoiding more profound changes.

类似的表面改变在学校、大学、工作场所和社会照护环境中都可能发生。根据我们的非正式分析，这种"庸俗版神经多样性"现象大多出现在两种情境中。一种情况是，进步人士可能意识到现有体系存在缺陷，偶然接触到"神经多样性"这个词，便试图将其应用，错误地（且无疑是潜意识地）认为积极的意图加上最新的术语就等同于有意义的变革。这类人可能对实践中的深层转变持开放态度，但未能意识到这种转变尚未发生。另一种情况是，组织迫于"与时俱进"的压力，却对其现有运作模式缺乏根本性的批判。他们可能更有意识地选择通过重新贴标签的方式，对日益壮大的神经多样性运动做出最小限度的让步，同时积极避免更深刻的变革。

A second form of neurodiversity-lite is found when bad actors manipulate and wilfully misrepresent the ideas associated with neurodiversity, to their own selfish ends. A private practitioner might refer to their clients as ‘neurodiverse’ and reframe exploitative or damaging ‘therapeutic’ practices as neurodiversity informed, in order to make them seem more acceptable to worried parents. Worse still are cases where people reject the neurodiversity movement on the basis of false statements, such as the contention that the neurodiversity movement is not inclusive of people with a learning disability. In the most concerning scenarios neurodiversity advocates may be positioned as a powerful lobby, rather than as a marginalized minority, as a way to resist their advocacy.

庸俗版神经多样性的第二种形式出现在不良行为者为了自身私利而操纵并蓄意曲解与神经多样性相关的理念时。一位私人执业者可能会将他们的客户称为"神经多元"，并将剥削性或有害的"治疗"实践重新包装为基于神经多样性的方法，以使其在焦虑的家长眼中显得更可接受。更糟糕的是，有些人基于虚假陈述拒绝神经多样性运动，例如声称神经多样性运动不包含学习障碍者。在最令人担忧的情况下，神经多样性倡导者可能被塑造成一个强大的游说团体，而非边缘化的少数群体，以此作为抵制他们倡导的手段。

Neurodiversity-lite thrives in part because of a general lack of knowledge about neurodiversity activism and scholarship. In 2023, a search on PubMed—a database for academic biomedical research—revealed just 403 results when seeking papers that use neurodiverse, neurodiversity, neurodivergent, or neurodivergence in the abstract or title. Of these, 85 per cent were published in 2021 or later. In reality, this paltry number is a massive underestimate of the wider corpus of neurodiversity scholarship, and also an unrepresentative selection. Much of the most important writing on neurodiversity is unlikely to appear in such a search, because it is published on blogs, in books, or delivered in speeches. Academics in neurodiversity-adjacent fields (e.g. developmental psychology, neuropsychiatry) searching via conventional methods will miss this work as they attempt to bring the topic into the leading outlets of the academic establishment. The result is the absence of the writing of leading thinkers in the neurodiversity movement from reference lists of influential journal articles. The alternative of citing websites or social media posts risks inadvertently reinforcing the misapprehension of neurodiversity as an unscientific, cultural trend rather than a philosophical, political, and scientific construct based in decades of thought and writing. Nonetheless, academics writing about neurodiversity and examining its applications have a responsibility to engage with the underlying scholarship on the topic.

庸俗版神经多样性之所以盛行，部分原因在于大众普遍对神经多样性运动及其学术研究缺乏了解。2023 年，在学术生物医学研究数据库 PubMed 上搜索标题或摘要中包含"神经多元"、"神经多样性"、"神经殊异"或"神经殊异性"的论文，仅得到 403 条结果。其中 85%发表于 2021 年或更晚。实际上，这个微不足道的数字严重低估了神经多样性学术研究的整体规模，且样本代表性不足。许多关于神经多样性的重要论述很可能不会出现在此类检索中，因为它们发表于博客、书籍或演讲中。从事神经多样性相关领域（如发展心理学、神经精神病学）的学者若采用传统检索方式，在试图将该主题引入主流学术期刊时便会遗漏这些成果。这导致神经多样性运动先驱思想家的著作未能出现在权威期刊文章的参考文献列表中。 如果引用网站或社交媒体帖子，则可能无意中强化一种误解，即认为神经多样性是一种非科学的、文化上的潮流，而非基于数十年思考和著述的哲学、政治和科学建构。尽管如此，研究神经多样性并探讨其应用的学者有责任深入了解该主题的学术基础。

Meanwhile, practitioners and families of neurodivergent people face different barriers to understanding, familiar when it comes to translation of all sorts of academic ideas and research findings into practice: paywalled journal articles, academic jargon, and lack of time and resources to engage with research. In this context, a range of people who play crucial roles in relation to neurodivergent people—researchers, teachers, clinicians, social workers—lack the knowledge they need to spot neurodiversity-lite and guard against it.

与此同时，神经殊异者的从业者和家人在理解方面面临着不同的障碍，这在将各类学术思想和研究发现转化为实践时是常见的：付费墙后的期刊文章、学术术语，以及缺乏时间和资源去接触研究。在此背景下，许多在神经殊异者生活中扮演关键角色的人——研究人员、教师、临床医生、社会工作者——缺乏识别"庸俗版神经多样性"并加以防范所需的知识。

Why is such vigilance necessary? We contend that neurodiversity-lite is excessively damaging to the goals of the neurodiversity movement and to the lives of neurodivergent people. Superficial adoption of language actually hinders deeper change, by giving the impression that change has already taken place. Neurodivergent people using services or working in environments that claim to be neurodiversity informed (but are not) will not experience the benefits that come from affirming complexity and politicizing neuronormativity. Collectively, the false claims of critics of the movement may start to look plausible when judged against systems that have failed to engage deeply with neurodiversity. For example, organizations that claim that neurodiversity is about recognizing superpowers and celebrating special talents can reinforce the critique that the movement excludes people with a learning disability.

为何需要如此警惕？我们认为，这种"庸俗版神经多样性"对神经多样性运动的目标以及神经殊异人士的生活造成了过度损害。对语言的表面接纳实际上阻碍了更深层的变革，因为它给人留下变革已经发生的印象。神经殊异人士在使用声称"了解神经多样性"（实则不然）的服务或在此类环境中工作时，将无法体验到那些因肯定复杂性、将神经规范性政治化而带来的益处。当面对那些未能深入践行神经多样性的体系时，批评者对运动提出的错误主张，整体上可能开始显得言之成理。例如，那些声称神经多样性就是认可超能力、颂扬特殊天赋的组织，可能会强化一种批评，即该运动排斥有学习障碍的人士。

Another mirror-image issue is the case of organizations that are doing powerful work that treats neurodivergent ways of being as equal and valid, and destigmatizes neurodiversity-related differences, without using neurodiversity language. In this scenario, an over-focus on terminology rather than attending to core beliefs and principles can result in excellent practice being overlooked. Less mainstream approaches to education, such as Montessori or Steiner schools, may be deeply neurodiversity affirming, without ever using the language of neurodiversity. Formal structures may promote specific types of approach, making it even harder to distinguish between practices. For example, until recently Applied Behaviour Analysis was singled out for special mention in the guidelines of the American Medical Association, and this directly led to ABA—a behaviourist intervention widely seen as a form of abuse or conversion therapy by many autistic people—having a privileged status in relation to coverage under private health insurance policies. This drives autism support providers to brand what they are doing as ABA regardless of the detail of the practice, creating an ABA-monolith which disguises wide variations in specifics and ethos. Similarly in the UK, inspection of social care services virtually requires the use of Positive Behaviour Support, again driving a range of practices to be collected under that single label and masking variability in quality and underlying principles.

另一个镜像问题是，有些组织正在开展强有力的工作，将神经殊异的生存方式视为平等且有效的，并消除与神经多样性相关差异的污名，但它们并未使用神经多样性语言。在这种情况下，过度关注术语而非关注核心信念和原则，可能导致优秀的实践被忽视。一些不那么主流的教育方法，如蒙台梭利或斯坦纳学校，可能在深层意义上肯定神经多样性，却从未使用神经多样性的语言。正式结构可能会推崇特定类型的方法，这使得区分实践变得更加困难。例如，直到最近，应用行为分析在美国医学会的指南中被特别提及，这直接导致 ABA——一种被许多孤独谱系群体广泛视为虐待或转化治疗的行为主义干预——在私人健康保险政策的覆盖范围内享有特权地位。 这导致孤独谱系支持服务提供者无论其具体实践细节如何，都倾向于将所做之事标榜为 ABA，从而形成了一个掩盖了具体方法和理念广泛差异的 ABA 单一实体。同样，在英国，对社会护理服务的检查几乎要求使用积极行为支持，这再次促使一系列实践被归入这一单一标签之下，掩盖了其质量和基本原则的多样性。

The reverse phenomenon occurs often in research, where there can be a worrying disconnect between performance of progressive ideals and delivery of methodological excellence. All too often, research reports are judged as neurodiversity informed simply because they use the ‘correct’ language, without attention paid to the rigour and quality of the methods (whether qualitative or quantitative). Meanwhile, clinical trials and systematic reviews that deploy traditional medical research methods and perhaps also terminology (intervention, patient, symptom) may be written off without a more careful exploration of the underlying assumptions and purpose of the work. It is essential to recall that critiques of the medical model of disability do not automatically apply to all research conducted by medics, nor to all research using clinical methods.

在研究领域，反向现象时有发生，即进步理念的宣扬与方法论严谨性之间常存在令人担忧的脱节。许多研究报告仅因使用了"正确"的术语就被视为具备神经多样性意识，却忽视了方法（无论是定性还是定量）的严谨性与质量。与此同时，那些采用传统医学研究方法（可能还包括术语，如干预、患者、症状）的临床试验和系统综述，若未经对其基本假设和研究目的更审慎的审视，便可能被轻易否定。必须谨记，对残疾医学模型的批评并不自动适用于所有医学研究者进行的研究，也不适用于所有采用临床方法的研究。

We call for anyone seeking to understand and adopt a neurodiversity-affirmative approach to be thoughtful in their appraisal of practices and discourse in this space. Vocabulary alone is neither an indicator of beneficence nor of harm, and an examination of the fundamental principles and beliefs that shape the activity in question is essential.

我们呼吁任何试图理解并采纳神经多样性肯定立场的人，在评估该领域的实践和论述时保持审慎。词汇本身既非善意的标志，亦非危害的指标，审视塑造相关活动的基本原则和信念至关重要。

Neurodiversity and anti-psychiatry

神经多样性与反精神病学

Another common critique of the neurodiversity movement is that it is a form and continuation of the anti-psychiatry movement from the 1960s and 1970s, and that it reproduces all the same issues as this important but, in some ways, now outdated analysis. In this view, neurodiversity proponents are seen as denying that mental illness or disorder exists, in ways that may be harmful for patients who want clinical research and support.

对神经多样性运动的另一个常见批评是，它属于 20 世纪 60 年代和 70 年代反精神病学运动的一种形式及其延续，并且复制了这一重要但在某些方面现已过时的分析所存在的所有问题。在这种观点看来，神经多样性的支持者被视为否认精神疾病或障碍的存在，这可能对那些希望获得临床研究和支持的患者造成伤害。

The first thing to say here is that the term ‘anti-psychiatry’ is itself highly contested and is rejected by many of those to whom it is applied. But historically it was primarily used to refer to a cluster of rogue psychiatrists and social theorists who in various ways came to see psychiatry as a form of social control, and who contested this, in the mid to late 20th century. This includes people such as Thomas Szasz, the libertarian US psychiatrist who argued that mental illness is a myth; Ronald Laing, the Scottish psychiatrist who suggested that madness is produced in families and social contexts rather than merely being biological; the Canadian sociologist Erving Goffman, who argued that asylums are social institutions and psychiatric diagnoses mere ‘labels’; and Franco Basaglia, the Italian anti-fascist psychiatrist who fully believed in mental illness, but saw asylums as carceral systems and worked towards developing a more humane healthcare with no locked doors in Italy.

首先需要说明的是，“反精神病学”这一术语本身极具争议性，许多被归入该阵营的人士也拒绝接受此标签。但从历史脉络来看，该术语主要用以指代二十世纪中后期一群特立独行的精神病学家与社会理论家——他们以不同方式将精神病学视为社会控制的手段，并对此展开批判。其中包括：美国自由派精神病学家托马斯·萨兹，他主张“精神疾病是一种迷思”；苏格兰精神病学家罗纳德·莱恩，他认为疯狂源于家庭与社会环境而非单纯的生物学因素；加拿大社会学家欧文·戈夫曼，他指出精神病院本质是社会机构，而精神诊断不过是“标签”；以及意大利反法西斯精神病学家佛朗哥·巴萨利亚，他虽坚信精神疾病的存在，却将精神病院视作监狱体系，并在意大利推动建立没有上锁病房的更人性化医疗系统。

The dominant version of anti-psychiatry in the Anglo-American world stems primarily from Szasz, and is often associated with a blanket rejection of the very concept or idea of mental illness or the various diagnoses associated with psychiatry. While this is seen as potentially liberating by some clinicians and psychiatric survivors, it is seen by many others as a dangerous and ultimately offensive denial of the reality of mental illness and disability, which if taken seriously would undermine the rights people have to treatment through either socialized medicine systems such as the NHS or through insurance claims. Critics of neurodiversity who dismiss it as a form of this kind of anti-psychiatry see it as conceptually confused and ultimately incompatible with the liberatory aims of the movement.

英美世界主流的反精神病学观点主要源于萨斯，通常与全盘否定精神疾病概念或精神病学相关诊断联系在一起。虽然一些临床医生和精神病幸存者认为这具有潜在的解放意义，但许多人视其为对精神疾病和残疾现实的危险且最终具有冒犯性的否认——若认真对待这种观点，将损害人们通过国民医疗服务体系等社会化医疗系统或保险理赔获得治疗的权利。批评神经多样性运动的人将其视为这类反精神病学的变体，认为它在概念上混乱不清，最终与运动的解放目标背道而驰。

There are a few things to say in response to this. First, while a small number of neurodiversity proponents do hold these views, most do not. Moreover, in fact, the neurodiversity movement did not grow out of the anti-psychiatry movement at all, and rather grew out of a quite different tradition, that of the broader disabled persons’ movement and the theories of disability studies covered earlier in this book. As we have seen, in this view, even in those cases where pathologization is challenged, the concept of disability is used instead, thus retaining the demand for healthcare rights and clinical support where this is needed. Moreover, most neurodiversity proponents do seem to adopt at least some conception of mental illness or disorder for at least some conditions (e.g. eating disorders) where treatment can be helpful and indeed literally life-saving. As such, it is wrong to conflate neurodiversity with the Szaszian version of the anti-psychiatry tradition, and those who do this tend to lack sufficient knowledge of the history and theoretical commitments of each movement. As we have seen, neurodiversity proponents lean towards more democratic approaches to concepts and practice rather than making blanket statements (such as that mental illness is a myth) and enforcing them from above.

对此，有几点需要说明。首先，虽然少数神经多样性的支持者确实持有这些观点，但大多数人并非如此。实际上，神经多样性运动并非源自反精神病学运动，而是源于一个截然不同的传统——即更广泛的残疾人运动以及本书前面提到的残疾研究理论。正如我们所看到的，在这种观点中，即使在某些情况下病理化受到质疑，也会使用残疾的概念，从而保留了对必要时的医疗保健权利和临床支持的需求。此外，大多数神经多样性的支持者似乎确实对至少某些情况（如饮食障碍）采纳了某种心理疾病或障碍的概念，在这些情况下，治疗可能是有益的，甚至确实是挽救生命的。因此，将神经多样性与萨兹式的反精神病学传统混为一谈是错误的，这样做的人往往对每个运动的历史和理论承诺缺乏足够的了解。 正如我们所看到的，神经多样性的支持者倾向于采用更民主的概念和实践方法，而非自上而下地推行一刀切的论断（例如声称精神疾病是一种迷思）。

That said, other thinkers associated with the anti-psychiatry movement are more compatible with the neurodiversity paradigm. Franco Basaglia had no patience for wholesale denial of mental illness and instead worked closely with his patients to help collectively build a more liberatory approach to mental healthcare that was anti-carceral in its approach. Today this system still exists in Trieste, the city where the Basaglians worked, and is widely acknowledged as providing some of the best mental health services in the world. While Basaglia was working prior to the rise of the neurodiversity movement and would most likely not have been aware of the social model of disability, we suggest that his more democratic approach—which he referred to as ‘democratic psychiatry’—was broadly compatible with the commitments of the neurodiversity movement. This however is no reason to dismiss the neurodiversity approach.

话虽如此，反精神病学运动的其他思想家与神经多样性范式更为契合。弗朗哥·巴萨利亚对全盘否定精神疾病的做法毫无耐心，而是与患者密切合作，共同构建了一种更具解放性的精神健康照护方式，其方法本质上是反监禁的。如今，这套体系仍在巴萨利亚学派曾工作的城市——的里雅斯特——存续，并被广泛认为提供了全球最优质的精神健康服务之一。尽管巴萨利亚的工作早于神经多样性运动的兴起，他很可能并不了解残疾的社会模式，但我们认为，他所倡导的"民主精神病学"这一更民主的方法，与神经多样性运动的核心理念大体相容。然而，这并不构成否定神经多样性方法的理由。

Similarly, R. D. Laing also has some overlap with the neurodiversity approach. He argued for an acknowledgement that madness could sometimes lead to what he called breakthrough as well as breakdown. This did not deny the struggles or need for support of people considered mad, but sought to acknowledge that the processes of madness could manifest in different ways, and were not always or necessarily bad. While Laing was writing before the invention of the social model of disability, let alone neurodiversity theory, his work also seems more compatible with the neurodiversity approach.

同样，R. D. 莱恩的观点也与神经多样性方法存在一定交集。他主张承认疯狂有时既能导致他所谓的"崩溃"，也可能带来"突破"。这并非否认被视为疯狂者所面临的挣扎或对支持的需求，而是试图承认疯狂的过程可能以不同方式显现，且并非总是或必然有害。尽管莱恩的写作早于残疾社会模型乃至神经多样性理论的提出，但他的工作似乎与神经多样性方法更为契合。

One reason why the neurodiversity movement may sometimes be conflated with Szaszian anti-psychiatry is because of the depathologization agenda inherent to our position. It is worth, then, being explicit about the important role of expert clinicians in neurodivergent liberation. The 2023 case of an Australian woman with symptoms of depression who was then found to have literal worms in her brain is a stark example of how bad it could be if all mental illness was attributed to non-medical factors and wholly removed from the jurisdiction of the healthcare system. In her case, having access to doctors (rather than, say, a psychotherapist) turned out to be vital for discovering that she had a worm in her brain that was causing her psychiatric symptoms. In other, more common cases, we can see how nuanced the balance between medical intervention and disability rights can be. Worldwide, pregnant people take folic acid supplements to promote healthy development of the neural tube in the early post-conception weeks—failure to do so can result in children being born with conditions such as spina bifida. This nutritional public health intervention to prevent disability is widely accepted and crucially distinct from those efforts to prevent disabled children from being born which rest on termination of pregnancy. It provides a clear example of how preventative medical intervention can be welcomed when it rests on solid ethical foundations. Doctors, nurses, neuro-psychologists, and surgeons are all central to delivering good physical and mental health outcomes to their neurodiverse patients.

神经多样性运动有时可能与萨兹式的反精神病学相混淆，其中一个原因在于我们立场中固有的去病理化议程。因此，有必要明确专家临床医生在神经殊异解放中的重要作用。2023 年，一名澳大利亚女性出现抑郁症状，随后被发现在大脑中实际存在蠕虫，这一案例鲜明地展示了如果将所有精神疾病都归因于非医学因素，并完全脱离医疗系统的管辖范围，情况会有多糟糕。在她的案例中，能够接触到医生（而非心理治疗师）对于发现她大脑中的蠕虫——正是它导致了她的精神症状——至关重要。在其他更常见的情况下，我们可以看到医疗干预与残障权利之间的平衡是多么微妙。全球范围内，孕妇服用叶酸补充剂以促进受孕后早期几周内神经管的健康发育——若不这样做，可能导致儿童出生时患有脊柱裂等疾病。 这项旨在预防残疾的营养公共卫生干预措施被广泛接受，且与那些通过终止妊娠来防止残障儿童出生的做法有着至关重要的区别。它提供了一个清晰的例证，说明当基于坚实的伦理基础时，预防性医疗干预可以受到欢迎。医生、护士、神经心理学家以及外科医生，都在为他们的神经多元患者实现良好的身心健康结果中扮演着核心角色。

Overall, then, neurodiversity should not be equated with anti-psychiatry, and its distinct history should be recognized. Neurodiversity theory tends to avoid the now outdated views associated with some forms of anti-psychiatry, such as Szasz’s view that mental illness is simply a myth, and his further proposal that all state-funded healthcare relating to mental distress should thus be abolished. At the same time, many neurodiversity proponents do share important concerns with anti-psychiatry proponents, and the movement is broadly compatible with the more radically progressive anti-psychiatrists such as Basaglia, not to mention various historic and contemporary psychiatric survivor groups committed to collective liberation more broadly. Many neurodiversity proponents also work towards alternatives to psychiatry and psychology in many instances, with the hope of undermining the disciplinary power of these fields in the long run. But critique of psychiatry and rejection of its coercive power is not the same as denying the reality of mental illness or disability.

总的来说，神经多样性不应等同于反精神病学，其独特的历史应当得到承认。神经多样性理论倾向于避免与某些反精神病学形式相关的、现已过时的观点，例如萨斯认为精神疾病纯属神话的观点，以及他进一步提出的应废除所有与精神困扰相关的国家资助医疗服务的建议。与此同时，许多神经多样性支持者确实与反精神病学支持者有着重要的共同关切，并且这场运动与巴西利亚等更为激进进步的反精神病学家广泛兼容，更不用说致力于更广泛集体解放的各种历史和当代的精神病学幸存者团体。在许多情况下，许多神经多样性支持者也致力于寻求精神病学和心理学的替代方案，以期从长远上削弱这些领域的规训权力。但对精神病学的批判及其强制权力的拒斥，并不等同于否认精神疾病或残疾的现实。

Identity politics

身份政治

Another common critique of the neurodiversity movement is that it is built on a form of identity politics that is needlessly divisive, leading to an ‘us and them’ narrative that could hinder organizing and collaboration in practice. As such the movement is dismissed as a distraction from real political issues such as poverty, homelessness, and so on.

对神经多样性运动的另一种常见批评是，它建立在一种不必要的分裂性身份政治之上，导致了一种"我们与他们"的叙事，在实践中可能阻碍组织与合作。因此，该运动被斥为一种分散注意力的行为，偏离了贫困、无家可归等真正的政治议题。

Overall this is a deeply misleading and unhelpful narrative. It may be the case that there is some divisiveness associated with neurodiversity activism, but it is wrong to locate the fault of this with neurodiversity proponents. Rather, as we have detailed here, the underlying issue is that neurodivergent people are actually oppressed. As such, naming the hierarchical nature of this oppression with terms such as ‘neuronormative’ and ‘neurodivergent’ is not the genesis of this divisiveness. Rather, it is a first step towards overcoming it. And this includes overcoming things such as poverty and homelessness, which are precisely problems that disproportionately impact neurodivergent people.

总体而言，这是一种极具误导性且无益的叙事。神经多样性行动主义可能确实伴随着某种分裂性，但将这种过错归咎于神经多样性的倡导者是错误的。相反，正如我们在此详述的，根本问题在于神经殊异者实际上正遭受压迫。因此，使用"神经规范性"和"神经殊异"等术语来指称这种压迫的等级性质，并非分裂性的根源。恰恰相反，这是克服分裂的第一步。而这包括克服贫困和无家可归等问题——这些问题恰恰对神经殊异者造成了不成比例的影响。

That said, we do acknowledge that occasionally terms such as ‘autistic’ or ‘neurotypical’ can be used in overly essentialist ways—as if these were fixed, eternal kinds of groupings—and that this can relate to individual commitments to identities.
