In such cases, this may undermine efforts towards liberation, which are ultimately about building a world where many such diagnoses would no longer be needed. That said, this is certainly not an issue specific to neurodiversity advocacy. Rather, this is a much more general problem, perhaps especially in a neoliberal era, that impacts all social movements.

尽管如此，我们确实承认，诸如"孤独谱系"或"神经典型"这类术语有时可能被过度本质化地使用——仿佛它们是固定不变、永恒的分类——而这可能与个体对身份的认同有关。在这种情况下，这可能会削弱解放的努力，而解放的最终目标是建立一个不再需要许多此类诊断的世界。话虽如此，这当然不是神经多样性倡导特有的问题。相反，这是一个更为普遍的问题，或许在新自由主义时代尤为突出，影响着所有的社会运动。

To those worried about overly essentialist conceptions of neurodivergent and neurotypical identity, we can direct them towards neurodiversity scholarship from Marxian and queer perspectives, which clarifies the historically contingent basis of these disabilities, and which does so in a way that avoids neuro-essentialism and the kind of limited political efforts sometimes associated with that.

对于那些担心神经殊异和神经典型身份被过度本质化理解的人，我们可以引导他们关注从马克思主义和酷儿视角出发的神经多样性研究。这些研究阐明了这些障碍的历史偶然性基础，并以一种避免神经本质主义及其有时伴随的有限政治努力的方式来进行阐述。

Ultimately, while we think essentialist conceptions of neurodivergent or neurotypical identity are unhelpful, we support neurodiversity activism being confrontational, since this will be necessary for working towards genuine liberation. Neurodiversity politics is not supposed to leave the world as it is, but rather to change it, and this will require disruption, divisiveness, and confrontation in certain respects, whether in terms of how research is carried out to national policies, and everything in between.

最终，尽管我们认为对神经殊异或神经典型身份的本质主义理解并无助益，但我们支持神经多样性运动采取对抗姿态，因为这对于实现真正的解放是必要的。神经多样性政治的目的并非维持现状，而是要改变世界，而这将需要在某些方面引发破坏、分歧和对抗——无论是从研究开展方式到国家政策，乃至其间的所有环节。

The rise in self-identification

自我认同的兴起

A common way experiences of neurodivergent disablement are dismissed is for critics to focus on the way diagnoses such as autism and ADHD have skyrocketed in recent decades. Such critics often focus on self-identification, which has driven part of this increase. They variously claim that only identification from a medical professional is valid, and that self-diagnosis is not reliable. They also often complain that it increasingly seems that ‘everyone is neurodivergent these days’, which they see as a sign of over-inflation of diagnostic categories. This kind of reasoning takes a valid concern—trying to understand the rise in diagnoses—but uses it to wrongly dismiss the reality of neuronormative domination experienced by all neurodivergent people.

一种常见的否定神经殊异致残经历的方式，是批评者聚焦于孤独谱系和 ADHD 等诊断在近几十年来激增的现象。这类批评者常常关注自我认同，而这正是推动诊断数量增长的部分原因。他们以不同方式声称，只有医疗专业人士的鉴定才有效，自我诊断并不可靠。他们还常常抱怨，如今似乎“人人都是神经殊异者”，他们视此为诊断类别过度膨胀的标志。这种推理方式虽然抓住了对诊断数量上升的合理关切，却错误地利用它来否定所有神经殊异者所经历的神经规范性支配的现实。

There are many issues with such lines of reasoning. In fact, self-identification is not obviously less reliable than medical diagnosis. After all, psychiatric diagnosis is notoriously unreliable, so the bar to match it is not very high. But beyond this, such critiques fully rely on the assumptions of the pathology paradigm, for example that when it comes to disability, the true experts are always doctors and other clinicians, or that diagnostic rates of genetically based neurodevelopmental disabilities should remain roughly stable. But as we have seen, these assumptions are precisely part of what the neurodiversity paradigm challenges. Adopting the standpoint of the neurodivergent person challenges clinical authority, and viewing disablement as relationally produced between individual and environment means we should expect rates of disability to fluctuate as our environments change. So it is unclear why neurodiversity proponents should worry about those who disagree on these grounds.

这类推理存在诸多问题。事实上，自我认同的可靠性并不明显低于医学诊断。毕竟，精神科诊断的不可靠性是众所周知的，因此与之匹配的门槛并不高。但除此之外，这类批评完全依赖于病理学范式的假设，例如在涉及残疾问题时，真正的专家总是医生和其他临床医生，或者基于遗传的神经发育障碍的诊断率应大致保持稳定。然而正如我们所看到的，这些假设恰恰是神经多样性范式所挑战的内容。采纳神经殊异者的立场挑战了临床权威，而将残疾视为个体与环境之间关系性产生的现象，意味着我们应预期残疾率会随着环境变化而波动。因此，神经多样性的支持者为何要担心那些基于这些理由持不同意见的人，这一点并不明确。

Another way of thinking about the mass increase in self-identification is viewing it as a matter of consciousness raising among populations who are increasingly disabled in a world of intensifying capitalism, falling living standards, longer work hours, and impending environmental collapse. It can also be seen as part of a mass collective project of taking power back from a paradigm that gives clinicians too much power over neurodivergent people. From this view, while there remains good reason to seek medical evaluation in certain cases (e.g. when there is a parasitic worm in your brain), and while mis-identification still remains a potential issue, the mass increase in self-identification should not be seen as a problem in itself. Rather, it is a sign that our society is disabling more and more people, and thus needs to be radically changed.

思考自我认同人数激增的另一种方式，是将其视为在资本主义日益加剧、生活水平下降、工作时间延长、环境崩溃迫在眉睫的世界中，越来越多陷入失能状态的人群意识觉醒的表现。这也可以被看作是一场大规模集体行动的一部分，旨在从赋予临床医生过多权力以支配神经殊异者的范式中夺回权力。从这个角度看，尽管在某些情况下（例如大脑中有寄生虫时）寻求医学评估仍有充分理由，尽管错误认同仍是一个潜在问题，但自我认同的激增本身不应被视为一个问题。相反，它表明我们的社会正在使越来越多的人陷入失能状态，因此需要进行彻底变革。

In this context it is also possible to imagine a future in which diagnostic and/or self-identification rates also decrease. Neurodivergent people self-identifying or seeking a clinical diagnosis are often trying to solve a problem in their lives. This might be fairly universally conceptualized as a mismatch between expectation and reality. Neurodivergent people regularly confound others and even themselves by failing to adhere to narrow, normative expectations of behaviour and ability. If we are successful in widening those expectations again—in creating more inclusive schools, workplaces, and communities, and in having greater patience with and understanding of each other—some of those motivations to seek a diagnosis could dissipate. Our point here is not to suggest that those seeking a diagnosis today don’t really need it, or that some neurodivergent people are more ‘real’ than others. Rather we wish simply to acknowledge that divergence is necessarily referenced against typicality and social norms. Systems that widen our understanding of what is typical, affirming complexity and accommodating neurodiversity, may result in a lessening drive for categorization.

在此情境下，我们同样可以设想一个诊断率和/或自我认同率下降的未来。神经殊异者选择自我认同或寻求临床诊断，往往是为了解决生活中的某个问题。这个问题或许可以普遍地理解为期望与现实之间的不匹配。神经殊异者常常因为未能遵循狭隘的、规范性的行为与能力期望，而令他人乃至自己感到困惑。如果我们能够成功拓宽这些期望——创建更具包容性的学校、工作场所和社区，并对彼此抱有更多的耐心与理解——那么，寻求诊断的部分动机便可能消散。我们在此并非要暗示，今天寻求诊断的人并非真正需要它，或者某些神经殊异者比其他人更“真实”。相反，我们只是想指出，殊异性必然是以典型性和社会规范为参照的。那些拓宽我们对何为典型的理解、肯定复杂性并接纳神经多样性的体系，或许会减弱人们对分类的驱动力。

Co-production as a method of neurodiversity-informed change

神经多样性视角下的变革方法：协同共创

Throughout this book we have argued for the need for change. Frequently, the requirements are radical and fundamental. For readers feeling helpless in the face of such intimidating ambitions, we advocate for the adoption of co-production—both as a mechanism of change, but also as an end, in and of itself. Co-production here is used as an umbrella term referring to a range of ways of working together, across traditional boundaries. This could mean neurodiverse teams of people in any setting; academics working with partners outside the ivory tower; clinicians partnering with patients; or teachers collaborating with pupils and parents.

在本书中，我们始终主张变革的必要性。这些变革要求往往具有根本性和彻底性。对于面对如此宏图伟业感到力不从心的读者，我们倡导采用协同共创——既作为变革的机制，其本身也是一种目的。此处的"协同共创"是一个统称，指代跨越传统界限的多种合作方式。这可能意味着任何环境中的神经多元团队；学术界与象牙塔外的伙伴合作；临床医生与患者携手；或教师与学生及家长协作。

Co-production offers a number of immediate advantages in line with the principles of the neurodiversity movement. Bringing different perspectives together honours the requirement to affirm complexity. Diverse teams working together harness the key strength inherent in neurodiversity—the fact that we bring different experiences to the table. In doing so, we each challenge our worldview, expand our understanding, and increase our empathy. At a functional level, diverse teams have greater potential to anticipate challenges and identify solutions to them. Co-production also holds potential for emancipation of those involved, in particular when less powerful cohorts gain new skills through their co-working, and adopt leadership roles in the process.

共同创作遵循神经多样性运动的原则，提供了诸多直接优势。汇集不同视角体现了对复杂性的尊重要求。多元团队协同合作，发挥了神经多样性固有的核心优势——即我们各自带来不同的经验。通过这种方式，我们每个人都在挑战自己的世界观，拓展理解力，并增强同理心。在功能层面，多元团队更有可能预见挑战并找到解决方案。共同创作还具有解放参与者的潜力，尤其是当相对弱势的群体通过合作获得新技能，并在此过程中承担领导角色时。

Longer term, co-production must be central to our plans to democratize systems. Simply put, we cannot entrust neurodivergent liberation to one group, however well educated or thoughtful they may be. Transfer of power from one group to another is no guarantee of benign results, as starkly illustrated in Orwell’s Animal Farm. By working together we can continue to learn from each other, checking and balancing as we go, distributing rather than merely transferring power.

长远来看，共同创造必须成为我们实现系统民主化计划的核心。简而言之，我们不能将神经殊异者的解放事业委托给单一群体，无论他们多么博学或深思熟虑。权力从一个群体转移到另一个群体并不能保证产生良性的结果，正如奥威尔在《动物农场》中所鲜明揭示的那样。通过携手合作，我们可以持续相互学习，在进程中制衡与协调，实现权力的分散而非简单的转移。

The neurodiversity movement and its ongoing attempt at a paradigm shift has great liberatory capacity, and should be understood as part of a broader intersectional struggle for liberation. In this, it has particular potential to revolutionize research and practice. In turn, this should impact how we organize society more generally, from education, through the workplace, to criminal justice, healthcare, and beyond. As an ideal the neurodiversity paradigm is worth fighting for.

神经多样性运动及其持续推动的范式转变具有巨大的解放潜力，应被理解为更广泛的交叉性解放斗争的一部分。在这方面，它尤其具备革新研究和实践的潜能。相应地，这也将更广泛地影响我们组织社会的方式，从教育、职场到刑事司法、医疗保健等各个领域。作为一种理想，神经多样性范式值得我们为之奋斗。

Yet at the same time, it remains far from clear that this potential will be realized. To do so will take great collective effort and organization, across borders and in tandem and solidarity with other movements, over many decades. It requires great sacrifice from many and needs a vast change in the power structures that govern neuronormativity.

然而，与此同时，这种潜力能否实现还远未可知。要实现它，需要跨越国界的巨大集体努力和组织，并与其他运动同步团结，持续数十年。这需要许多人做出巨大牺牲，并需要对支配神经规范性的权力结构进行巨大变革。

Without this mass, collective effort, it seems likely that neurodiversity-lite will become the dominant variant of the approach. This may help some people in particular ways, but will ultimately just reform the normalcy paradigm rather than bringing a revolution towards the neurodiversity paradigm. For those who see the neurodiversity paradigm as worth fighting for, it will be up to each and all of us to work towards not just neurodiversity affirmation, but also collective liberation.

如果没有这种大规模的集体努力，庸俗版神经多样性似乎很可能成为该方法的主导变体。这或许能在特定方面帮助一些人，但最终只会改革常态范式，而不是带来向神经多样性范式的革命。对于那些认为神经多样性范式值得为之奋斗的人来说，我们每个人和所有人都有责任努力争取的不仅是神经多样性的肯定，还有集体的解放。

Preface

Preface

前言

This book is about neurodiversity. Neurodiversity is a relatively new term, being coined in the 1990s by a community of autistic activists. Part of their idea was that, just as the ecosystem is enriched by biodiversity, so too is human society enriched by a diversity of ways of thinking. And just as biodiversity requires our collective effort to support and conserve, so too does neurodiversity. Based on this, these activists began to work towards a new civil rights and justice movement led by people with social and communication disabilities. They hoped this movement would advocate for social and legal reforms for autistic people as well as others whose sensory, cognitive, or neurological profiles set them apart from the norm.

本书探讨的是神经多样性。神经多样性是一个相对较新的术语，由一群孤独谱系行动者在 20 世纪 90 年代提出。他们的部分理念是，正如生态系统因生物多样性而丰富，人类社会也因思维方式的多样性而更加丰富。正如生物多样性需要我们共同努力来支持和保护，神经多样性也是如此。基于此，这些活动家开始致力于推动一项由社交和沟通障碍者领导的新民权与正义运动。他们希望这项运动能够为孤独谱系群体以及其他感官、认知或神经特征与常人不同的人士，倡导社会和法律改革。

Since these early days, the movement has grown rapidly. Now it includes not just autistic people, but people with all kinds of disabilities and divergences around the globe. Neurodiversity advocates include people who identify as anything from bipolar to dyspraxic and everything in between. We can describe them as neurodivergent. As such, there is now a large and still-growing movement of loosely connected individuals and groups usually known simply as the neurodiversity movement. This movement precisely seeks to change the world in the kinds of ways those early advocates specified.

自这些早期岁月以来，这场运动迅速发展壮大。如今它不仅包括孤独谱系群体，更涵盖了全球范围内各类残障与差异人士。神经多样性的倡导者中，既有识别为双相障碍者，也有发展性协调障碍者，乃至其间所有不同类型的人们。我们可以将他们描述为神经殊异者。由此，一个规模庞大且仍在持续扩展、由松散联结的个人与团体构成的运动已然形成，通常被简称为神经多样性运动。这场运动正专门致力于以早期倡导者所规划的方式改变世界。

The autistic scholar Nick Walker distinguished the neurodiversity movement from the emerging neurodiversity paradigm. This refers to the underlying assumptions or principles contingent upon neurodiversity’s existence that represent a change in thinking, theory, and research necessary for the future that proponents of the movement have been collectively building. The point of this paradigm, for Walker, is to move away from framing minds or brains as either ‘normal’ or ‘abnormal’, and instead to begin with an embrace of neurological diversity as itself normal. For Walker, this shift will be relevant both for scientific research and for cultural representation of neurological variations. It will help move away from the prevalent assumption that neurodivergent people are necessarily broken or deficient, and towards a more inclusive framework for understanding, researching, and supporting mental variation.

孤独谱系学者尼克·沃克将神经多样性运动与新兴的神经多样性范式进行了区分。后者指的是基于神经多样性的存在而衍生的基本假设或原则，这些原则代表着运动支持者共同构建的未来所必需的思维、理论和研究方式的转变。对沃克而言，这一范式的核心在于摆脱将心智或大脑简单归类为“正常”或“异常”的框架，转而从接纳神经多样性本身即为常态这一起点出发。他认为，这种转变对于科学研究以及神经变异的文化呈现都具有重要意义。神经多样性范式将有助于摒弃当前普遍存在的、认为神经殊异者必然存在缺陷或不足的预设，进而推动建立一个更具包容性的框架，以理解、研究并支持心理层面的多样性。

From this view, a key point is that disablement is seen as related to politics and power rather than being a natural fact determined by individual ability alone. For instance, dyslexia is a disability largely because written text has become such a pivotal source of information and mode of communication. Similarly, insofar as autism is a matter of sensory-processing differences, the extent to which an autistic person is disabled will be determined by sensory environments such as the lights we use, sound levels, and so forth. This is an important insight since, if accepted, it has significant implications for how we should design schools, workplaces, and so forth. As such the neurodiversity movement seeks to challenge not just how we think about and study neurological variations, but also how we organize society in a variety of ways.

从这个视角来看，一个关键点在于，残障被视为与政治和权力相关，而非仅由个人能力决定的自然事实。例如，阅读障碍之所以成为一种残障，很大程度上是因为书面文本已成为信息和交流的关键载体。同样地，就孤独谱系涉及感官处理差异而言，孤独谱系人士的残障程度将由感官环境决定，比如我们使用的灯光、声音水平等等。这是一个重要的洞见，因为接受这一视角将对我们设计学校、工作等场所的方式产生深远影响。因此，神经多样性运动不仅挑战我们如何看待和研究神经系统的变异，也挑战我们以多种方式组织社会的方式。

This book aims to introduce and synthesize a range of key themes in the theory, history, politics, and practice of neurodiversity. Here we describe, in simple terms, the history of the movement and its key innovations, concepts, controversies, and debates. This then allows us to cover the significance of the movement for politics, policy, and practice. In turn, this should help readers gain a basic understanding of what neurodiversity is all about, and then to decide what they want to explore further.

本书旨在介绍并整合神经多样性理论、历史、政治及实践中的一系列关键主题。我们将以简明的方式描述该运动的历史及其核心创新、概念、争议与辩论。由此，我们得以探讨该运动对政治、政策及实践的重要意义。这反过来应能帮助读者对神经多样性的基本内涵形成初步理解，进而决定他们希望进一步探索的方向。

It is important to say up front that we recognize that there are different neurodiversity stakeholders and have worked to build this into our writing. We have written this book with at least three key groups in mind. First and foremost, we have written it for neurodivergent people, as well as their friends and families. To be clear, this is not a self-help book nor one which gives practical advice. Rather, it is meant to introduce readers to a new way of thinking about things usually called mental or neurodevelopmental ‘disorders’ and to help people navigate the various positions and debates within the neurodiversity movement. It also helps us think critically about concepts such as ‘intelligence’, ‘ability’, ‘illness’, and associated notions in new ways, and how these relate to forms of political domination. While we do not offer practical advice, we therefore hope this book will be valuable for developing a deeper understanding of self, others, and society. This in turn can be empowering through informing understanding of challenges that arise in day-to-day life as well as wider social and political issues.

首先需要说明的是，我们认识到神经多样性涉及不同的利益相关方，并努力将这一点融入我们的写作中。我们撰写本书时，心中至少有三个关键群体。首要且最重要的是，我们为神经殊异人士及其亲友而写。需要明确的是，这并非一本自助指南，也不提供实用建议。相反，本书旨在向读者介绍一种全新的视角，来审视通常被称为心理或神经发育“病症（disorder）”的现象，并帮助人们理解神经多样性运动中的各种立场与争论。同时，它也引导我们以新的方式批判性思考“智力”、“能力”、“疾病”等概念及其相关观念，以及这些概念如何与政治支配形式相关联。尽管我们不提供实用建议，但我们希望本书能帮助读者深化对自我、他人及社会的理解，从而获得启发。这种理解进而能赋予人们力量，使其更好地应对日常生活中出现的挑战以及更广泛的社会政治议题。

Second, we have also written this book with researchers and practitioners in mind. We recognize that many people who study neurodivergence or work with neurodivergent people want to learn about the neurodiversity approach. However, most are trained in a more traditional medicalized approach grounded in the normalcy paradigm (a term indicating the currently dominant, medicalized approach, which we explain below). Moreover, they may not be able to find adequate resources for learning to update their understanding or may be met with conflicting advice or information where they find it. Of greatest concern is the large volume of misinformation we cover later in the section in Chapter 5 on Neurodiversity-lite. By providing an overview and synthesis of the theories and implications of the neurodiversity paradigm, we hope this book will be useful for researchers and professionals who wish to update their practice to incorporate the insights of the neurodiversity paradigm and support the goals of the neurodiversity movement.

其次，我们在撰写本书时也考虑到了研究人员和实践者的需求。我们认识到，许多研究神经殊异性或与神经殊异人群共事的专业人士都希望了解神经多样性理念。然而，大多数人接受的是基于常态范式（这个术语指当前主流的医学化路径，我们将在下文详述）的传统医学化训练。此外，他们可能难以找到足够的学习资源来更新认知，或在获取信息时遭遇相互矛盾的建议。最令人担忧的是第五章“庸俗版神经多样性（Neurodiversity-lite）”章节中我们将讨论的大量错误信息。通过对神经多样性范式的理论框架与实践意义进行系统性梳理，我们希望本书能帮助研究人员和从业者更新实践方法，融入神经多样性范式的洞见，并支持神经多样性运动的目标。

Third, we have written this with students in mind. Neurodiversity theory is relevant to a wide range of fields, from sociology to psychology, education to philosophy. As such it is increasingly being brought into a range of both academic and vocational university courses. We have written this book in part to be useful to students who are seeking clarity on the neurodiversity approach. While our book is, we stress, a short introduction and therefore not comprehensive, we have developed it as a basis for further study.

第三，我们写作时也考虑到了学生群体。神经多样性理论与众多领域相关，从社会学、心理学到教育学、哲学皆是如此。因此，它正日益被纳入各类大学学术课程与职业课程中。我们撰写本书的部分目的，正是为了帮助那些希望厘清神经多样性方法的学生。虽然必须强调，本书作为通识读本无法面面俱到，但我们将其设计为进一步研究的基础框架。

Who are we?

我们是谁？

Given our subject matter, we think it is important to be open about who we are and what each of us brings as well as the limitations of our knowledge and understanding. We are two academics from the UK who have both worked on neurodiversity theory and research for some time.

基于本书的主题，我们认为有必要坦诚说明我们的身份背景、各自的研究贡献以及我们认知的局限。我们是两位来自英国的学者，长期从事神经多样性理论与研究工作。

One author, Robert Chapman (they/them), is Assistant Professor in Critical Neurodiversity Studies at Durham University. They are autistic and also have first-hand experience of other neurodivergent disabilities and mental health conditions. They are white, nonbinary, and come from a working-class background and the foster care system. They began blogging on neurodiversity in the early 2010s while studying philosophy, before carrying out doctoral research on ethical issues relating to autism and neurodiversity between 2013 and 2018. Since then, they have remained active in various political campaigns and have published widely on neurodiversity theory and practice, as exemplified by their previous book Empire of Normality: Neurodiversity and Capitalism. As such, they bring an insider’s perspective combined with a deal of relevant knowledge and expertise.

其中一位作者罗伯特·查普曼（他们/them）是杜伦大学批判性神经多样性研究的助理教授。他们是孤独谱系人士，并对其他神经殊异性障碍与心理健康问题具有亲身经历。他们身为白人、非二元性别者，出身工人阶级背景并曾经历寄养体系。2010 年代初期，他们在攻读哲学期间开始撰写关于神经多样性的博客，随后于 2013 至 2018 年间开展关于孤独谱系与神经多样性相关伦理问题的博士研究。此后，他们持续活跃于各类政治运动，并在神经多样性理论与实践领域广泛发表著作，其前作《常态帝国：神经多样性与资本主义》（Empire of Normality: Neurodiversity and Capitalism）即为明证。因此，他们既具备内部视角，又融合了丰富的相关知识与专业见解。

The second author, Sue Fletcher-Watson (she/her), is a Professor of Developmental Psychology at the University of Edinburgh. Sue identifies as neurotypical, while recognizing the limitations of this category—and any descriptor categories under the umbrella of neurodiversity. She has no personal experience of neurodivergence or mental ill-health. Sue is white, cisgender, pansexual, and came from a privileged background in terms of social class. Her immediate family is neurodiverse. Sue began consciously considering the neurodiversity paradigm in her work from about 2012 and then blogging and writing about neurodiversity more explicitly a few years later. Sue tries to apply the principles of the neurodiversity paradigm in her research and to produce evidence which can support neurodiversity-informed change in services. She does so in her own research projects by establishing partnerships with neurodivergent academics and mentoring neurodivergent students and by using participatory methods to link with neurodivergent people outside academia. Her expertise in participatory methods has resulted in highly cited key papers and awards. Sue attempts to use her leadership roles, for example as Editor-in-Chief of the journal Autism and as Director of the Salvesen Mindroom Research Centre at the University of Edinburgh, as a platform to raise the profile of the neurodiversity paradigm and embed its principles in academic work.

第二位作者苏·弗莱彻-沃森（她/她的代词）是爱丁堡大学的发展心理学教授。苏自认为是神经典型者，同时认识到这一类别——以及神经多样性这把大伞下的任何描述性类别——的局限性。她没有神经殊异性或精神健康问题的个人经历。苏是白人、顺性别者、泛性恋者，并且来自社会阶层上的特权背景。她的直系亲属是神经多元的。大约从 2012 年起，苏开始在工作中自觉思考神经多样性范式，几年后则更明确地开始通过博客和写作探讨神经多样性。苏试图在她的研究中应用神经多样性范式的原则，并产出能够支持基于神经多样性理念的服务变革的证据。她通过在自己的研究项目中与神经殊异的学者建立伙伴关系、指导神经殊异的学生，以及使用参与式方法与学术界外的神经殊异人士建立联系来实现这一点。她在参与式方法方面的专长已催生了多篇高被引的关键论文并赢得了奖项。 苏试图利用她的领导职务，例如担任《孤独谱系》期刊的主编以及爱丁堡大学萨尔维森心智研究中心的主任，作为一个平台，以提高神经多样性范式的知名度，并将其原则融入学术工作之中。

While we believe that our combined expertise and knowledge makes us well placed to write this introductory book, it is important to recognize that our knowledge is limited by our positionality and as such is far from perfect. As two white academics, born and based in the UK, our experiences are less relevant to members of racialized minorities and many people from the majority world. With this in mind, we have sought to emphasize throughout how important it is to recognize how race, ethnicity, culture, and neurodivergence intersect, and how this takes place within a global system that privileges white people at the expense of Black, Asian, Brown, and Indigenous peoples. Neurodiversity as a paradigm is largely grounded in Westernized models of thinking and there are alternative conceptual frameworks and traditions from around the globe which have not gained the same level of international currency and which we are not qualified to introduce with authority. Wherever possible, we instead signpost original scholarship for the reader to explore.

尽管我们相信，结合我们的专业知识和学识，我们有能力撰写这本入门书籍，但必须认识到，我们的知识受限于自身立场，因此远非完美。作为两位在英国出生和工作的白人学者，我们的经验对于少数族裔成员以及来自多数世界的许多人来说，相关性较低。有鉴于此，我们在全书中力求强调，认识到种族、民族、文化与神经殊异性如何相互交织至关重要，以及这一切如何在一个以牺牲黑人、亚洲人、棕色人种和原住民为代价、优待白人的全球体系中发生。神经多样性作为一种范式，很大程度上植根于西方化的思维模式，而世界各地存在着尚未获得同等国际影响力的替代性概念框架和传统，我们并无资格权威地介绍它们。在可能的情况下，我们会为读者指引原始学术资料以供探索。

We are also aware that while neurodivergence is often associated with autism, it encompasses a wide range of diagnoses or disabilities. Nobody has direct experience of all of these, and we only have (direct and indirect) experience of a handful between us. As such, while much of this book draws on the work of autistic pioneers in neurodiversity activism and theory, we have sought to emphasize the relevance of neurodiversity to those with different experiences of mental disablement or distress, not just autistics. As we will come back to, we advocate for a broad, inclusive conception of neurodivergence.

我们也意识到，虽然神经殊异性常与孤独谱系相关联，但它涵盖了一系列广泛的诊断或障碍。没有人能直接体验所有这些情况，而我们两人之间也只（直接或间接地）经历过其中少数几种。因此，尽管本书大量借鉴了孤独谱系先驱们在神经多样性行动主义和理论方面的工作，我们仍力求强调神经多样性对于经历不同精神障碍或困扰的人群——而不仅仅是孤独谱系人士——的相关性。正如我们将在后文重申的，我们倡导一种广泛而包容的神经殊异性概念。

More generally, we seek to follow what Black feminist author Kimberlé Crenshaw describes as an intersectional perspective. This emphasizes how people who sit at intersecting axes of oppression—say, people who are both Black and female, or neurodivergent and trans, and so on—often face more specific and complicated forms of oppression than those who are in one oppressed group, and which may be missed by efforts that focus on single group issues. By the same token, we frame neurodivergent liberation as bound up with collective liberation, and thus as part of a broader struggle for the freedoms of oppressed peoples globally. The power dynamics of neurodivergence sit within a broader system that bell hooks described as ‘imperialist white-supremacist capitalist patriarchy’. We hope to make this clear as we guide readers through the various issues we cover.

更广泛地说，我们力求遵循黑人女性主义作家金伯莉·克伦肖所描述的交叉性视角。这一视角强调，那些身处多重压迫交汇点的人——例如既是黑人又是女性的人，或是神经殊异者与跨性别者等等——往往面临着比单一受压迫群体更为具体和复杂的压迫形式，而这些形式可能被专注于单一群体议题的努力所忽视。同理，我们将神经殊异者的解放视为与集体解放紧密相连，因此也是全球受压迫人民争取自由的更广泛斗争的一部分。神经殊异性中的权力动态存在于一个更广泛的体系之中，这个体系被贝尔·胡克斯描述为“帝国主义白人至上资本主义父权制”。我们希望在引导读者探讨所涉及的各类议题时，能够清晰地阐明这一点。
